**Appendix: Kun Formula**
The true transmission has its secrets, the true transmission has its secrets.
What the *geng* and *jia* must know, the Confucian scholars expound in detail.
Teach people to discern clearly the presence and absence, lest one’s ardent devotion be in vain.
The mechanism lies before one’s eyes; qi is thereby drawn forth.
Above is the Celestial Valley; below is the Spring Cavern.
Recognize these two places—no deviation is permissible.

**Record of Heterodox Ways**

**Preface to Minor Arts of Heterodox Ways by Ancient Buddha Xiangyue Wentong of Jizhong Charitable Hall**

Heterodox ways are those that openly contravene the Dao; minor arts are those that subtly deviate from it. The Great Dao is supremely profound, wondrous, simple, and effortless—untainted by the slightest selfish intent or the faintest desire. Whatever fails to align with the qi-movement of Heaven and Earth, the orthodox principles of sages and worthies, or the preservation and expression of human nature and emotions belongs to heterodox ways and minor arts.

Yet heterodox ways and minor arts are myriad. To enumerate them in detail might offend the virtuous, while to remain silent might mislead later learners. Thus, I shall briefly outline several dozen of the most pernicious practices in the world—those that most grievously corrupt the heart and defile the gates of the mysterious—so as to stem their poisonous flow. This is but the compassionate hope of pulling one from the abyss or rescuing one from the flames.

Should any cultivator have fallen into these arts, they must turn back at once; to mend the fold after losing the sheep is not too late. But if, swayed by doubt and delusion, one clings stubbornly to error, harming oneself and others, one will not only fail to forge great karmic connections but also forfeit any prospect of a favorable outcome.

The boundless karmic affinity of the ten thousand buddhas lies near—let all cultivators of this age take heed. The path to the Three Pure Ones’ hall remains open—let later cultivators discern it with utmost care.

**Responsive Moon’s Literary Correspondence with Ancient Buddhas (Four Poems)**

Mistaking "other" and "self" for truth,
Who knows yin and yang lie within the body’s own frame?
Buying concubines, consorting with courtesans to practice *cai-zhan*,
Seeking to seize primordial *qi* to replenish the spirit—
Could there be immortals of Penglai’s fairy realms
Who instead resemble lewd youths, lustful in their ways?

Now, "other" refers to the youthful yang, to primordial *qi*;
"Self" refers to the beautiful woman, to the primordial spirit.
The principle is this: with the yang *qi* of one’s own body, one ignites the yin spirit within,
So that spirit and *qi* merge as one—this is called attaining the Dao.
Yet the heterodox schools take "self" as man and "other" as woman.
Thus, some buy beautiful women to keep as concubines,
Having an external "yellow dame" watch for the approach of *ren-gui* to practice *cai-zhan* and seize their *qi*;
Others purchase fair concubines or consort with courtesans,
Engaging in *cai-zhan* to plunder their primordial *qi*.
All these err in misconstruing the terms "other" and "self,"
Committing the gravest transgression—
Neither heavenly law, royal decree, nor the punishments of the unseen realm can they escape.
How then can they hope to become immortals?
If such ways could lead to immortality,
Then Penglai’s immortal mountains would be overrun with lewd youths and wanton women.
Speaking in fairness, can such a principle exist?
Can such a principle exist?

This principle inflicts immense harm upon people, and thus the ancient Buddhas placed it foremost among prohibitions.
In Daoist cultivation, the mind must be kept pure above all—first forge the sword of wisdom to sever the root of lust.
Those who, ignorant of forging the sword, instead test its edge,
Are like adding oil to a raging fire.
Even the hands that subdue dragons and tigers
Cannot escape leakage, turning primordial essence into turbid fluid.

When no thought arises, one abides in the primordial;
The moment a thought stirs, one falls into the posterior.
If the mind remains clear, the primordial still lingers within the posterior;
If the mind is clouded, the primordial vanishes entirely from the posterior.
No thought surpasses lustful desire—once it stirs, the numinous *qi* scatters;
If it lingers long, the numinous *qi* perishes.
The cultivator need not fear thoughts arising, only delayed awareness.
Awareness itself is the sword of wisdom.
Awaken and sever at once, awaken and sever without pause—constant vigilance severs the root of lust.
This is called great awakening, this is called forging the sword.

Yet the heterodox schools, ignorant of the wondrous method of forging the sword,
Instead take the union of man and woman as "testing the sword,"
Claiming that if no thought moves, the blade is sharp,
And if thought moves, the blade is dull.
But ask: when the yang stirs, does thought arise from nothing?
Or does it arise from something?
If the yang stirs without thought, this belongs to the primordial—just the moment to gather it.
If thought arises before the yang stirs, this belongs to the posterior—precisely when it should be subdued.
Yet instead of subduing it, they proceed to lewd acts—what is this if not adding oil to a raging fire?
At such times, the primordial spirit cannot govern, and the acquired spirit takes control,
Turning primordial essence into turbid fluid.
To expect it not to leak or drain away—I do not believe it.
This is a stern rebuke of those who "test the sword."

When the yang stirs, the wind blows and draws through the *weilu*,
If it does not disperse after several attempts, the *zhou-tian* begins.
Thirty-six rounds of yang fire advance,
Twenty-four rounds of yin tally follow—fully employed.
But ask the world’s true cultivators:
From which immortal was this method transmitted?

The dispersal of the yang by wind is proper practice.
If the yang does not subside, there are secret techniques.
Those who practice minor arts perform the lesser *zhou-tian* thirty-six times,
From the *weilu* up the spine to the *jiaji*, over the *yuzhen* to the *niwan*, where it halts—this is advancing yang fire.
Then from the *niwan* down the twelve-storied tower, letting it descend naturally—twenty-four times—this is retreating yin tally.
They then combine thirty-six rightward and twenty-four leftward circles to complete the *zhou-tian* count.
Afterward, they gather the spirit and sit in meditation—this is called "bathing" or "supplementing the intercalary."
I know not how the *zhou-tian* can be so rigidly numbered,
Forcing the mind and intent into external work—how can the spirit settle?
How can the elixir form?
It is but futile labor.
This speaks of minor arts—beware them.

The rolling wheel spins before the chest,
Falsely claimed to be transmitted by the "Two-Mouthed Immortals."
Forcibly employing methods to refine the nature,
Yet failing to recognize that true nature is primordial.
The immortals and Buddhas transmitted the method of settling the spirit—
Wondrous in its effortless naturalness.

The "rolling wheel" is a large circle silently traced before the chest,
Then reduced to a smaller circle to bind the nature—this they call "refining the nature," a mere technique.
Could Lü Dongbin have truly passed this down?
Their slander of Ancestor Lü is indeed grave.

The true nature is utterly empty and numinous—
It is by this nature that one becomes immortal or Buddha.
If tracing a silent circle can bind the nature,
Then tracing a silent circle can bind immortals and Buddhas as well.
This principle is easily understood—
Even those of modest wisdom could discern it,
Yet how have so many fallen into such techniques unawares?

The method of settling the spirit transmitted by immortals and Buddhas
Is itself the method of refining the nature.
Wondrously aligned with the natural,
It requires no forced effort,
And of itself enables the nature to become perfectly luminous, fulfilling the great Dao.

As I, an ancient Buddha, have surveyed the world,
I find no shortage of heterodox minor arts.
I record them here in this book
To spare later students from error.

**—Inscribed by Disciple Tan Xian with reverence**

**Ancient Buddha Who Delivers All Beings (Four Poems)**

Each dawn they face the east, mouths agape toward heaven,
Eyes bulging, shoulders hunched;
Expelling all turbid qi, drawing in the pure,
To shed the mortal coil and restore youthful countenance.
Little do they know that perverse winds enter the viscera,
Distending the lower field, swelling the belly—life cut short.

The technique of drawing in qi:
At early dawn, face east,
Eyes bulging, shoulders raised,
Inhale deeply through the mouth,
Taking pure qi within, expelling turbid qi without—
They claim this can make one immortal or Buddha.
Yet who knows that perverse qi accumulates in the five viscera and six bowels?
Over time, the lower field distends, the chest becomes congested,
And some even die of swelling.
Alas!
To seek the Dao without method and die an untimely death—
How laughable, how pitiable!

Foolish men vainly dream of becoming immortals,
Enduring thirst without drink, hunger without food;
They make of themselves hungry ghosts, falling into the three evil destinies,
Yet still hope to ascend to the Great Brahma Heaven.
Many the wise led astray by this,
As inner demons arise and outer demons cling.

To drink when thirsty, to eat when hungry—
This is the principle of nurturing life.
For those who cultivate the Dao,
When primordial qi is abundant, the need for grain may cease.
Yet only when one neither thirsts nor drinks, neither hungers nor eats,
Does one become an immortal.
But there are those foolish seekers of immortality
Who shut themselves away in silent sitting,
Ignoring the wondrous methods of true cultivation,
And merely endure hunger and thirst—
Even to the point of death.
If such words are to be believed,
Then all who die of hunger in the world
Would be enrolled in the registers of immortals.
I have seen many wise men
Led astray by heterodox paths—
This is the result of deluded longing.
Once the demon of intent arises,
Outer demons come to claim their lives.
Foolish men, seek a true teacher while there is still time!

Without cause they kindle fire and recklessly add oil,
Drawing in pure qi through the nose in outward pursuit;
Guiding it upward to the Mud Pill Palace, halting at the Double Pass,
Then reversing its flow down the Twelve-Storied Tower;
Without fire they manipulate fire, then suppress it—
Wasting spirit and energy until the hair turns white!

There exists a method of "kindling fire and adding oil":
Through the nose, one draws in the pure qi of heaven and earth,
Using intent to guide it upward to the Mud Pill Palace,
Halting at the Double Pass,
Then turning it back up to the Mud Pill Palace,
Crossing the Upper Magpie Bridge,
Swallowing it down the Twelve-Storied Tower,
And stopping at the middle field.
If there is no perverse fire, all is well—
Yet they deliberately manipulate fire, then suppress it.
What method is this?
What Dao is this?
Misusing spirit and energy,
Even to the end of one’s days,
One remains a mortal bound to birth and death.
Of the great elixir of golden cinnabar,
They have not even dreamed—
What benefit is there in blind cultivation?

Most detestable are the blind masters who falsely claim immortal talent,
Leaving the "Five Dragons Bearing the Sage" to wild conjecture;
Boasting of their bellows’ skill as it issues from the furnace,
Stuffing objects to block the bowels—how utterly foolish!
Swindling others of their wealth, ruining their lives,
Doomed to suffer infernal punishments in death and calamities in life.

This method originates from the recipe masters.
At the moment of the yang’s ascent,
They vigorously fan the wind and fiercely refine,
If the qi does not disperse,
They concentrate the spirit and engage in battle for one or two watches,
Using five fingers to cradle the kidneys, tightly grasping the dragon’s head as in self-gratification—
This they call "the bellows issuing from the furnace."
Employing the four-word formula of *cuo* (gathering), *shi* (licking), *xi* (absorbing), and *bi* (closing),
They take the impure essence formed by improper means,
Reverse its flow through the Three Passes up to the Mud Pill Palace,
Swallow it into the Yellow Court,
And circulate it through the microcosmic orbit—
Circling left and right, sixty times in all.
Some even claim:
"When the great medicine passes through the passes,
One must tightly block the bowels with a wooden implement
To prevent the elixir from escaping."
Yet when the great medicine crosses the passes and descends the Magpie Bridge,
It naturally follows its path, surging into the tailbone and ascending—
What has this to do with the bowels?
Why subject oneself to such cruel torment?
These two methods are regarded as secret techniques by blind masters,
Who swindle others of their wealth and destroy their lives.
When the mysterious gate has fallen to such a state,
How can one avoid great calamities in life
Or escape infernal punishments after death?
Cultivators, awaken swiftly!

**—Inscribed by Disciple Zhang Xian of Pure Essence with reverence**

**Water Ancestor (One Poem)**

The immortal elixir lies hidden within the body—most potent,
Why seek strange formulas beyond the self?
Gold and minerals rashly consumed bring only harm,
The placenta’s stench is foul and hard to bear.
Yet there are fools, ignorant and base,
Who devour spent essence like beasts.

The primordial qi within the body *is* the immortal elixir,
Yet wayward schools and heterodox paths seek strange formulas outside.
Some refine metals and minerals to ingest, hastening their own death;
Others consume the placenta, turning kin against kin.
Most detestable are those who, after coupling,
Lick spent essence themselves—
How do they differ from oxen, horses, dogs, or swine?
If consuming spent essence could make one immortal,
Would not oxen, horses, dogs, and swine all ascend to heaven?

This folly stems from misreading "elixirs" and "ingestion" in alchemical texts.
Reading books requires discerning principle,
Seeking a master demands true insight.

**—Inscribed with reverence by Lingguang the Great Awakened Immortal**

**Great Awakened Compassionate Perfected One, Transforming Heaven and Earth, Salvaging All Beings (Two Poems)**

Seeking to unblock every joint and bone,
They boast of "transporting qi" as divine skill.
The tortoise’s head bound—yet the tortoise won’t die;
The dragon’s head inverted—the dragon grows fierce.
Then there’s the so-called "Eight Pieces of Brocade,"
All brute force, like madness or frenzy.

Seeking to unblock every joint and bone,
They boast of "transporting qi" as divine skill.
Drawing in a breath to guide it to the lower field,
From both feet to the knees, then to the insteps,
Turning into the Bubbling Spring point;
Then from the heels up the backs of the legs,
Through the Yang Pass, piercing the Double Passes beside the spine,
Up both shoulders to the backs of the hands, flipping into the palms;
From the elbows to the nape, up the Jade Pillow to the Mud Pill,
Down the Magpie Bridge through the Twelve-Story Tower,
Settling in the elixir field—one cycle of the heavens.

The tortoise’s head bound—yet the tortoise won’t die.
While sleeping, wrap the yang organ with a long cloth,
Bind it with cord, then tie the cloth and cord behind the neck,
Lying on the side to prevent erection and elixir loss.

The dragon’s head inverted—the dragon grows fierce.
This method also uses a long cloth and cord to wrap the yang organ,
Tying it from the tip to the back of the neck,
The upper head facing the lower head,
Eyes fixed intently upon it.

Then there’s the so-called "Eight Pieces of Brocade":
Shaking the head and swaying the tail, rubbing the abdomen,
From top to bottom thirty-six times,
Knocking the teeth thirty-six times, swallowing the saliva,
Hands on the hips, deliberately swaying the body,
Hands swinging fists as if striking someone,
Turning the head left and right to peer at the heels,
Standing on tiptoes, fingers interlaced, raising to the brows and lowering to the ground—called the "Duke Zhou’s Salute."
Standing on one leg, stretching with force,
When finished, exhausted, facing the sky and exhaling three deep breaths—called "Expelling the Five Turbid Qi."
Do this after every meal, and when weary, do it again.
All brute force, like madness or frenzy.

All these heterodox practices are sheer brute force,
As if one were mad or deranged.
Those who practice them seek to ward off illness and prolong life,
Or to become immortals or buddhas—alas!
How laughable indeed.

Turning stones to gold and iron to silver,
The alchemy of yellow and white deceives the greedy.
Building elixir chambers and forging elixir vessels,
Falsely claiming ten thousand taels are needed to succeed.
Yet true refinement lies in heart and nature,
Accessible to all, regardless of wealth or rank.

Turning stones to gold and iron to silver,
The alchemy of yellow and white deceives the greedy.
Building elixir chambers and forging elixir vessels,
Falsely claiming ten thousand taels are needed to succeed.
Those who deceive with yellow-and-white arts claim
That once the elixir is refined, it can turn stones to gold and iron to silver.
Thus they seek out the corrupt and greedy,
Urging them to contribute silver—hundreds or tens of taels—
Promising to amass thousands before commencing the elixir work.
With this elixir, they say, gold and silver can be conjured at will,
Funding the construction of lavish elixir chambers,
Exquisite elixir vessels,
Fine robes, sumptuous feasts, servants, and attendants—
All supplied by the elixir’s transmuting touch.
This is a swindle, yet many fall for it.

Do they not know that refinement lies in heart and nature,
Accessible to all, regardless of wealth or rank?
Why resort to yellow-and-white arts?
Why build elixir chambers and vessels, all this splendor?
Let the greedy ponder this deeply.

—Inscribed with reverence by the Wish-Fulfilling True Gold Buddha

**Radiant Cloud Lapis Lazuli Buddha (One Poem)**

Hands cradling the scrotum, wiping the lower field,
Ninety-nine yang counts, left and right complete.
Su Qin bearing the sword—truly unbearable,
Embracing the moon in the bosom, laughing at warming the elixir.
Bending backward to sun the belly—how much more bitter,
Self-entangled in the net—how foolishly sour.

Hands cradling the scrotum, wiping the lower field,
Ninety-nine yang counts, left and right complete.
With the left hand cradling the scrotum, the right hand wipes the lower elixir field eighty-one times;
With the right hand cradling the scrotum, the left hand wipes the lower elixir field eighty-one times.

Su Qin bearing the sword—truly unbearable.
This method uses a willow branch,
Shaped into a crescent board, propped against the wall,
The arched part pressing into the back,
Hair tied to the board, the right foot bound above, the left foot below.
No movement is possible—any shift risks a fall—
Then stealing valuables and violating women.

Embracing the moon in the bosom, laughing at warming the elixir.
In cold weather, a copper bottle filled with boiling water is placed on the navel,
Held in both hands—called "warming the elixir."

Bending backward to sun the belly—how much more bitter.
A deeply curved wooden arch is used,
Lying supine upon it—called "sunning the elixir."

Self-entangled in the net—how foolishly sour.
These heterodox practices are far from reason,
Yet fools are often ensnared,
Casting themselves into the net—how foolish indeed!

—Inscribed with reverence by the Investigating Deity, Disciple of the Tree Hall

**Primal Clarity of the Great Ultimate Buddha (One Poem)**

Eyes fixed on one inch and three below the navel,
This is but a foul sac—how can the elixir form?
Pubic hair and external kidneys are of no use,
Falsely designating cauldrons and furnaces, pointing to the mysterious pass.
The true locus among the body’s pores and orifices—
The slightest deviation spans heaven and abyss.

Eyes fixed on one inch and three below the navel,
This is but a foul sac—how can the elixir form?
One inch and three below the navel—this place is utterly hollow, utterly foul.
To claim the elixir forms here is delusion.

Pubic hair and external kidneys are of no use,
Falsely designating cauldrons and furnaces, pointing to the mysterious pass.
Some focus on the pubic hair, others on the external kidneys,
Yet the true cauldron and furnace lie elsewhere—what use is such observation?

The true locus among the body’s pores and orifices—
The slightest deviation spans heaven and abyss.
Without authentic transmission,
All the body’s points remain uncertain—
Never presume to rely on guesswork.

—Inscribed with reverence by the Inspecting Deity Zhang You

**Ancient Wind Buddha (One Poem)**

The three thousand six hundred heterodox schools—
impossible to enumerate one by one.
All that involves contrivance is false;
purity and spontaneity alone are true.

The ten thousand differences return to one root,
the three vehicles converge in one mind.
Refining myself through myself is most wondrous—
within the fire of longevity, metal is born.

False and true stand revealed as if unveiled;
what to reject and what to follow have their proofs.
If one can truly abandon the false and return to the true,
ascension in broad daylight is assured.

The three thousand six hundred heterodox schools—
impossible to enumerate one by one.
All that involves contrivance is false,
for the heterodox paths are too many to inscribe on bamboo and silk,
and so all contrivance is subsumed under this.

Purity and spontaneity alone are true—
utterly pure, utterly natural,
this is the primordial Great Dao,
through which one may attain immortality or Buddhahood.

The ten thousand differences return to one root—
resolved in the single word "nature."

The three vehicles converge in one mind—
resolved in the single word "mind."

Refining myself through myself is most wondrous—
both form and spirit are perfected.

Within the fire of longevity, metal is born—
metal is yang, born within the fire of longevity.

False and true stand revealed as if unveiled;
what to reject and what to follow have their proofs.
In the entire corpus of immortal and Buddhist transmissions,
whether false or true, the words are clear—
how could the reader fail to know what to discard and what to embrace?

If one can truly abandon the false and return to the true—
this is the heart of immortals and Buddhas in saving beings.

This verse concludes the entire work.

—Inscribed with reverence by the Salvation-from-Calamity Heavenly Worthy
Transmitted by Perfected Lady Sun Buer
*Secret Book of the Elixir Way*
*True Scripture of the Jade Purity Womb-Primordial Inner Nourishment*
Handed down by the Perfected Lord of the Treasured Spirit Primordial Terrace

At that time, the Most High Lord Lao attended court. The Primordial Celestial Venerable addressed the Most High, saying: "When essence is depleted, fire flares upward; when qi is depleted, it flees downward. Yin and yang each course through water and fire, while metal and wood fail to unite as husband and wife. Thus, the people of the lower realms suffer daily decline of true qi, daily encroachment of yin evil, their original lifespan cut short, their spirit and essence incomplete, sinking into the state of lesser ghosts.

I once transmitted to you the wondrous Dao of the Womb-Primordial, whereby the outer Mysterious Female is united with the inner Mysterious Female, the outer true spirit supplements the inner true qi, and the myriad treasures of heaven are gathered to nourish the primordial essence of my womb. Thus, spirit is born within the womb, qi clings to spirit, the Heart-Monarch governs in concealment, breath is harmonized and even, the ten thousand spirits pay reverence, and the hordes of demons bind their forms. You should teach the multitudes first to master stabilizing the heart.

When the heart is stabilized, qi abides; when qi abides, spirit is whole; when spirit is whole, the form is firm. Subtly continuous as if existing yet not ceasing, its use is inexhaustible and its efficacy manifest. The Valley Spirit does not die—it merges with my true lineage.

I pity the people of the world: outwardly ravaged by wine and lust, inwardly ensnared by cares and anxieties, ever coveting fame and profit, dissipating their spirit and essence, clinging to painted corpses, artful smiles and moth-like brows, chasing externals and forgetting their root, collapsing the foundation of their numinous nature. This causes Kan and Li to scatter and disperse, the hun and po to drift apart, children to be born in succession, and the bodily frame to gradually decline. Reduced to a mound of earth in a single coffin, they lose the true mechanism of heaven and earth—how lamentable!

You should exhort the people of the world first to uphold minor precepts, advancing to the great precepts; first to learn to still the heart, gradually entering non-action. Through stabilization, clarity arises; through clarity, the Dao is awakened.

The superior class of people, refining the coarse into the subtle, attain a luminous body and dwell in the Heaven of Purity and Stillness, their lifespan immeasurable. The middling class prolong their years and preserve their form, replenishing and restoring the Womb-Primordial, avoiding premature harm. The inferior class distance themselves from passions and desires, diminish their pursuit of profit and fame, turn toward the true wind, and follow the sagely teachings.

You should disseminate my wondrous words in myriad forms, circulating and teaching far and wide, gradually guiding them to abandon the false and return to the true, to discard the turbid and retain the pure, and to realize the supreme Dao."

At that time, the Most High Lord Lao reverently received the sacred instructions and, together with the Radiant Purple Heavenly Mother, each transformed their forms into as many as the grains of dust, dividing their bodies throughout the worlds to universally deliver sentient beings. Before long, the twelve thousand heavens of the upper realms gave rise to immeasurable heavenly beings within lotus blossoms. Each, riding the void, arrived at the Jade Purity realm, faced the true Venerable, and recited a hymn:

"Supreme Divine Father, who opens the great expedient means,
Commanding the Most High and the Radiant Purple Heavenly Mother,
Transforming their forms below to broadly deliver our kind.
Through precepts and stabilization, all ascend above,
Attaining the body born of intent and realizing the supreme Dao.
We, in turn, transform into hundreds of thousands of millions of forms,
Each embodying eternal ages, extolling the mysterious virtue—
Even through hundreds of thousands of millions of kalpas, it cannot be exhausted.
Vast and towering, its merit defies inquiry.
Having faithfully received this, how shall we repay?
We vow to generate the great resolve for future kalpas,
To deliver sentient beings with this single heart—
This is called requiting virtue."

The immeasurable heavenly beings recited this wondrous hymn, each scattering celestial flowers and precious incense into the void as offerings. Gazing afar at the true Venerable, they bowed a hundred times and withdrew.

*True Scripture of the Jade Purity Womb-Primordial Inner Nourishment* concludes.
*Supreme Jade Purity Inner Landscape True Scripture*

The Great Saintess of the Primordial Heaven of the Great Luo True Heaven, the Purple Radiance Heavenly Mother, transmitted this:

At that time, the Primordial Beginning Most True Great Saint transformed and opened the heavens. With the power of great divine penetrations and the power of great wisdom, he structured the world, harmonized yin and yang, and presided over creation. First, within the Mysterious Void of the Great Brahma True Heaven, he manifested external forms to reveal the inner landscape. He divided the nine qi into the color of the Wood Essence of the East, coalescing them into the Nine Qi Venerable One to govern them, which in humans becomes the liver and the hun-soul. Next, he divided the seven qi into the color of the Metal Essence of the West, coalescing them into the Seven Qi Venerable One to govern them, which in humans becomes the lungs and the po-soul. Then, he divided the three qi into the color of the Fire Essence of the South, coalescing them into the Three Qi Venerable One to govern them, which in humans becomes the heart and the spirit. Next, he divided the five qi into the color of the Water Essence of the North, coalescing them into the Five Qi Venerable One to govern them, which in humans becomes the kidneys and the essence. The remaining qi of the four directions—Water, Fire, Metal, and Wood—were distributed at the center as the color of the Yellow Court, coalescing into the One Qi Venerable One to govern them, which in humans becomes the spleen and thought. The five viscera, containing consciousness, together possess the Ten Perfections. The essence of the Ten Perfections can accomplish the Nine Revolutions, gathering into the elixir medicine and scattering as sweet dew. Circulating above and below, it refines and nourishes the hundred bones, washing away the turbid to retain the pure, dissolving yin to cast yang, restoring our primordial origin, preserving our great wholeness. Emerging from Kunlun, entering the Great Abyss, drawing forth the dragon’s transformation, passing through the Tiger City, the four qi harmonize and unite to perfect our utmost truth. The withered become flourishing, the aged return to infancy, the decayed visage is renewed, white hair turns black again, the voice rings like a bell, the body is as light as a feather. All mortal bones are replaced, and one ascends to fly in the Upper Clarity.

Scholars of the world, establish precepts and uphold concentration to generate wisdom and clarity. Through these three powers, they eternally preserve the qi of light purity for a hundred million years, moving with concentration and transformation to transcend as immortals. The True Sovereigns of the Left and Right Two Mysteries, the Limitless, with this Dao widely disseminate it among heavenly beings and humans, enabling them to abandon the karma of impermanence and enter the wondrous truth of the Real One, never aging, never dying, abiding in serene quiescence.

The Primordial Beginning Venerable True One, from his seven orifices, emitted great radiance, illuminating immeasurable lands. The twelve thousand heavens and the hundred billion human realms, each by their own power, scattered fragrant incense and flowers as shared offerings. All rejoiced without exception, each awakening to their original heart.

At that time, within the Mysterious Void, the Jade Clarity Transformative Palace suddenly beheld a precious moon’s radiance illuminating the ten directions, inner and outer. Within the precious moon, purple qi was contained, and inside it sat an infant on a jeweled lotus dais, emitting golden light. With a great jade voice, he spoke this gatha:

With one heart, true concentration arises,
Myriad forms naturally array themselves.
Following the directions, the five qi divide,
The five qi conceive the one numen.
The one numen penetrates transformation,
Refining and coalescing the original true.
The original true has no form,
Yet neither is it nothing nor non-being.
Those who comprehend this principle
Truly awaken to the pearl that gathers dust.

Within the Mysterious Void, inside the moon’s light, the Jade Infant expounded the teaching. In that moment, all in heaven and earth heard it. Without exception, their wisdom seas became serene, their karma mountains crumbled. Turning inward to illuminate, they eternally merged with the Dao’s truth. Gazing up at the sacred radiance, they bowed in reverence and departed, holding fast to faith and devotion.

*Supreme Jade Purity Inner Landscape True Scripture* concludes.

---

**Treasure Chapter on Guarding the One**

Transmitted by the True Master of Mount Heng.
Also titled *The Heart Mirror of the Mysterious Pearl*

The Dao is non-action, yet nothing is not done.
It can be realized by the heart, not known by wisdom.
What is knowing?
What is realizing?
Wisdom transcends wisdom.
*[After knowing, one should transcend wisdom, concealing traces and veiling light.]*
Realizing emptiness responds.
*[Abiding in empty non-action, over time the spirit effects response, like echo answering sound.]*
Response arises without source,
*[Naturally and spontaneously.]*
And the heart thereby penetrates.
*[With the heart empty and non-active, over time one illuminates the Dao, and with illumination comes divine penetration.]*
Penetrating the One, all matters are complete.
The One is the root.
*[The One is the root origin of the Great Dao.]*
Matters are the gate.
*[Attaining the origin of the One is what the* Supreme Heart Seal *calls "matters."]*
Matters return to the One, the One abides eternally.
*[In guarding the One’s matters, when the work is complete, one returns to the primordial qi. The body and the void become naturally formless, and the one qi abides eternally.]*
Abiding has no possession, provisionally called "guarding."
*[When the one qi eternally abides in the self, do not allow qi to be possessed. Guarding is but a provisional term.]*
Guard the void and nothingness, and naturally endure long.
*[Simply guard the void and nothingness, and naturally the form and spirit will endure long with the Dao.]*

*Treasure Chapter on Guarding the One* concludes.

**Poem on Guarding the One**

The Transmission of the Origin of Obtaining the One by True Maiden Lu Chui of Fanyang to Cui Shaoxuan

*[Note:] The* Daode *[Scripture] states: "Know the white, guard the black."* Those gentlemen who study the Dao, having known the white, must guard the black. The black is the yin qi. At the beginning of guarding the black, the black within the body resembles lacquer. Guarding it without cease, the black qi gradually dissipates, and the tally of yin is entirely consumed. The pure yang white qi, when inwardly luminous at the time of clarity, with eyes closed and vision gathered inward, naturally reveals the five viscera and palace chambers, the thirty-six thousand blood vessels. As the numinous spirit gradually arrives, one emerges from existence and enters non-existence, divides the body into a thousand myriad, and this is called the origin of obtaining the One.

Those who guard the One need only empty their bodies, void their hearts, and constantly abide in emptiness and vacuity. Inwardly, they congeal spirit and thought, and the wondrous qi of the Origin naturally flows back into the body of the one who guards. It presides over nature and life. Lord Lao told Master Wen Shi: "I contemplate this Dao, which originally emerged from the dim and obscure." The dim and obscure is guarding the black—this is guarding the One. When stillness and quiescence endure long, the celestial light illumines within. Shedding the bodily husk, gathering vision inward to observe, the form remains as it is. At this time, outwardly, the radiant flame encircles the body; inwardly, the body divides into a thousand myriad. Such is the subtlety of Lady Cui’s *Poem on Guarding the One*.

The Supreme Lord expounded the *Heart Seal*, saying: *"The Perfected One wears a golden kerchief."* These five characters are the Heart Seal of the Jade Dawn Lord. Lord Lao transmitted this to Master Wen Shi. Guarding this Heart Seal is precisely guarding the origin of the One—this is the gateway to entering the Dao. There are no Highest Sages or Lofty Perfected Ones who did not enter thereby.

In short, the origin of guarding the One is guarding the primordial spirit within the emptiness and stillness. The origin of the One is not visible—it is the formless net. The origin of the One that may be obtained is the primordial pearl. It is not received from heaven but is the truth of the Supreme Lao. *[Note:] Lao may also be rendered as "Non-Existent."* The immortal of the Non-Existent. Light contains, shadow conceals. *[Note:] This speaks of obtaining the origin of the One. One must guard the spirit with utmost sincerity, accumulate merit and refine the form, darken the heart to no-heart, darken the body to no-body. Inwardly, one does not distinguish one’s own body; outwardly, one does not distinguish heaven and earth. With time, even bones and flesh transform into pure yang essence and qi. The yin qi inwardly dissipates, and one begins to perceive the celestial light shining within, brilliantly illuminating the midst of the molted body. When the celestial light unites within, form and shadow vanish and conceal without.* Formed by nature. *[Note:] This speaks of light containing and shadow concealing, spirit congealing in the emptiness and stillness—suddenly, form manifests. This is the countenance of a Celestial Immortal, emerging from nature, not an ordinary body.* Truth and tranquility are not sought. *[Note:] Master Zhenzi of Mount Heng comments: This speaks of the Dao’s completion, when form congeals within the body—not something that can be sought through cunning or skill. One must only darken the heart to no-heart, darken the body to no-body. If there remains even a trace of body or heart, the spirit will not congeal.]* The spirit’s enduring abidance. *[Note:] Wang Sunzhi, the Reclusive Perfected, comments: The true embryo’s tranquility depends solely on congealing thought within, so that the primordial spirit endures long. Formerly, Lord Lao told Master Wen Shi: "If one can retain the spirit within the body, know and embrace the mysterious, with firmness over months and years, the spirit will endure long. Only with enduring abidance does it congeal into immortality." Master Zhenzi of Mount Heng comments: When the work of guarding the One reaches completion, the spirit congeals, and the true form rests within my "child’s palace." The child’s palace is the sea of qi, the sea of blood. The true form resting in the child’s palace is called the spirit’s enduring abidance. One must accumulate merit through arduous effort over long months and years before the form may be completed. The* Western Ascension Scripture *states: "Conceal the person within the person without emergence, conceal the body within the body without manifestation—only then is the celestial Dao flourishing." How profound these words are! It also says: "The heart of no-heart, the body of no-body—this is called the Dao-person."* Beauty and purity become true. *[Note:] This speaks of guarding the One for long, so that the harmonious yang qi illumines the entire body, like a lamp’s flame—bright and clear, utterly luminous and devoid of things. The yin qi is entirely consumed, and the true form becomes ever more true.* The body’s nature is both firm and yielding. *[Note:] This speaks of the wondrous Dharma of formlessness, the Dharma-body of true suchness, which can be firm or yielding. Yielding means it cannot be grasped even when held in the hand; firm means it can pierce through metal and stone.* The azure clouds and jade ruins are the companions of the Highest Sages.

The *Poem on Guarding the One* concludes.

---

**The Primordial Scripture of the Feminine Origin by Perfected Sovereign Sun Bu’er**

At that time, the Primordial Sovereign was in the Huayang Grotto-Heaven, expounding the *Wondrous Scripture of the Feminine Origin* to the Celestial Nymphs Yan Na, the Twelve Stream Maidens, and others. She said:

Heaven is yang, earth is yin; heaven moves, earth is still. Qian acts, Kun yields—primordial, prosperous, advantageous, and upright. The Dao of Qian completes the male; the Dao of Kun completes the female. Yin alone does not grow; yang alone does not generate. Only when firmness and yielding attain the mean can water and fire achieve mutual completion, giving birth to the myriad things. Bearing and supporting the living, compassionate and forbearing without contention, reverent and yielding in assistance—thus abiding in the benevolence of the mother’s Dao, serving as the consort of the later primordial, achieving merit and discussing transformation, their Dao is one.

Since the opening of Qian and the closing of Kun, there have been the Holy Mother, the Queen of Earth, the Heavenly Matriarch, Nüwa, the Dipper Mother, the Buddha Mother, the Primordial Sovereign, the Queen Mother, the Immortal Maidens, the Jade Maidens, and those such as Magu, the Heavenly Consort, the Heavenly Maidens, the Mysterious Maiden, the Non-Ultimate Female Immortals, the Female Bodhisattvas, the Bhikṣuṇīs, the Nāga Stream Maidens, the Purple Maiden, the Xiang Consorts, the Luo Spirit, the Shamankas, the Lightning Mother, the Azure Maidens, the Plain Maidens, and the Weaving Maidens. All, through the yielding and compliance of the feminine origin, cultivated truth and attained the Dao, verifying the loftiest fruit—one in qi with the celestial origin, undivided.

Now, good women, each possessing the feminine origin, can all enter the Dao. Through cultivation and effort, they may verify the wondrous fruit of ultimate bliss and endure through ten thousand kalpas.

If your body obstructs you, making cultivation difficult, yet your original mind has no leaks—why do you obscure yourself? Before the beginningless past, where were forms? Where were bodily traces? There was only the One, only emptiness, originally without a second mind. Why cultivate the body? Why abandon the mind? If you can return and reflect on the origin, there is a swift path to cultivating truth. I now reveal this swift path to you, women of the assembly. Listen carefully.

The Way of Heaven moves; the Way of Earth is still. To cultivate nature and life, you must begin with stillness. Yet you are originally still—why cultivate? The Way of Earth is turbid; the Way of Heaven is clear. To cultivate nature and life, you must begin with clarity. Only by refining the turbid into clarity can you enter the Dao and verify the fruit.

I now teach you the Way of cultivating clarity. Though clarity and turbidity differ in form and substance, their original source lies in the mind and spirit. If you wish your mind to be pure and your spirit clear, you must cultivate your nature. To awaken to cultivating nature is to establish life. If you can awaken, that is your nature. Your nature is not nature; your mind is not mind. Mind is mind; nature is nature. Nature is not your mind; mind is not your nature.

If asked about your nature, nature speaks of nature. If asked about your mind, mind speaks of mind. Mind has no mind; nature has no nature—yet neither is without nature, nor without mind. Nature is not mind; mind is not nature. Nature has no mind; mind has no nature. Nature is originally without mind; mind is originally without nature. If mind has nature, it is not the Dao-mind. If nature has mind, it is not the Dao-nature.

The Dao-nature is my nature; the Dao-mind is my mind. This is true nature, this is deluded mind. If nature is true, you see the Dao-nature. If mind is deluded, it is not the Dao-mind. Though called the Dao-mind, there are distinctions—what is this "cloud-mind" called? There is the fleshly heart and the empty, numinous mind. This empty, numinous mind—what is it called? It is the true Dao-mind, the true real mind. That fleshly heart—what is it called? It is not the Dao-mind; it is the deluded mind.

If you can transform the fleshly heart into the empty, numinous mind, awaken the non-Dao-mind into the true Dao-mind, and break the deluded mind into the true real mind, then with a mind of courage, a mind of diligence, cast aside the mind of affliction and the mind of obstruction. Only the obstructing mind is attachment. To remove attachment, you must cultivate the vajra mind, the empty mind, the dead mind, the unmoving mind, the wise mind, the steadfast mind, the perfect mind, the accomplished mind, the bodhi mind, the compassionate mind, the joyful mind—such minds are called the Dao-mind. To illuminate the Dao-mind is to realize that mind is the Dao.

If you enter this Dao, guard this mind. When encountering forms, remain thus, unmoved. When facing illness, remain thus, unchanged. When thunder strikes, remain thus, unshaken. When right and wrong arise, remain thus, undisturbed. When blades threaten, remain thus, unafraid. When death approaches, remain thus, unbroken. Only in unbrokenness is there no death; only in no death is there the Dao-mind. Only in the Dao-mind is there cultivation of the Dao; only in cultivating the Dao is there cultivation of nature.

If nature is without clarity, it is not true nature. Without this true nature, what mind remains? Without this true mind, what Dao remains? Thus, divine powers and wisdom arise from the mind-Dao; purity, stillness, and emptiness emerge from the nature-Dao. The Three Treasures are one without duality; the Four Elements are but illusory emptiness.

Strive to preserve clarity within turbidity; guard against movement within stillness. To guard against movement is to illuminate nature; to illuminate nature is to guard the mind. If the mind is constantly cultivated, the six thieves cannot enter. With vigilant awareness, how can the five aggregates arise? Wisdom shines brightly, refining harmony into purity. Nature is illuminated, life is established—lead restrains mercury, relying on earth for success. Mercury is cast into the furnace, secluded in true silence, refining form into qi, refining qi into spirit, refining spirit into emptiness—this is the original state. What kalpa cannot endure? What fruit cannot be verified? What body remains leaky?

How can the mind be obstructed? How can the Dao be dual? O virtuous woman, why do you still hesitate to cultivate?

When the Primordial Sovereign had finished expounding this sutra, she addressed the assembled immortals: "The non-dual principle I have just revealed was once transmitted to me by the Mysterious Lady Primordial Sovereign. It is the peerless, wondrous Dao of *Zhenyi* and *Kunyuan*, a bridge across the sea of the Way for you, virtuous women. Even virtuous men do not depart from this. Fearing that you may remain benighted and waver in doubt, I shall now recite a gatha:

Man and woman arise from the same qi,
Yet differ in clarity and turbidity, movement and stillness.
If a woman seeks to refine the true,
She must gather her primordial essence.
Within yin lies the primordial yang—
Preserve clarity, do not cast it aside.
Understand that form and desire
Are fundamentally without encumbrance.
Banish greed, wrath, and delusion;
Sever the bonds of care and anxiety.
Cast off turbidity to cultivate pure nature,
And you shall not fall into evil destinies.
Abide in stillness, guard non-action—
Then I, the woman, am possessed of the man.
No form in the formless,
Yet meaning in the existent and non-existent.
Inwardly perceive form and sound as empty,
Without the slightest clinging.
Rely on earth as the foundation of *Kun*,
For the one yang arises naturally from the ground.
Lead and mercury are not the same,
Yet qi and spirit share a single principle.
The vast, empty, numinous mind—
The spirit of the mind can master it.
When the one qi returns to spring harmony,
It soars beyond the clouds.
Accompanying you to roam the Great Clarity,
This is the gatha of true suchness."

When the Primordial Sovereign had finished reciting the gatha, the celestial maidens of the heavens, the twelve Immortal Ladies of the Streams, scattered fragrant blossoms and bejeweled tassels, while sacred scriptures danced in flight. All rejoiced, received the teaching with faith, praised its rarity, bowed in gratitude, and withdrew.

**Appendix:**
The Primordial Sovereign’s surname was Sun, her Daoist name *Erbu* ("Non-Dual"). She was a native of Ninghai. Born on the fifth day of the first lunar month in the first year of the *Xuanhe* reign of Emperor Huizong of the Song (1119), she married Ma Yifu of Danyang in her youth and bore three sons. Through the ten transformations of the pear offered by Wang Chongyang, husband and wife cultivated together and ascended as immortals. On the twenty-ninth day of the second lunar month, she ascended in broad daylight and was enfeoffed as *Qingjing Yuanzhen Xuanxu Yanzheng Shunhua Yuanjun*, one of the Seven Perfected.

**Sun Buer Yuanjun’s Stages of Inner Alchemy for Women**
Sun the Immortal Lady, named *Buer* ("Non-Dual"), was also called *Qingjing Sanren* ("Serene Scatterer"). She was the wife of Ma Danyang. Danyang’s hands hung past his knees, and three peaks rose from his brow. He once wrote a poem: *"Embracing the One and guarding unity is the work— / The lazy man now has nothing at all. / All day he holds his cup, delighting in spirit’s ease, / Yet in drunkenness, there is someone to support him."* None understood its meaning.

Suddenly, a Daoist calling himself Chongyangzi came to convert Danyang. When the Immortal Lady entered the Dao, she was offered a melon and ate it from the stem, saying, *"Sweetness is sought in bitterness."* When asked, *"Whence have you come?"* he replied, *"From no great distance, only to support the drunkard."* Danyang found this strange. Husband and wife served their master with utmost reverence and established the Quanzhen Hermitage in the Southern Garden. Several years later, their master took Danyang on a westward journey to dwell in the Misty Rosy Cloud Grotto on Kunlun Mountain, while the Lady remained at home, diligently practicing the transmitted teachings. At the age of fifty, she again traveled with the Immortal Lady Feng to Luoyang. After six years, her Dao was perfected, and she wrote a hymn: *"With three thousand merits complete, I rise beyond the Three Realms, / Leaping free of yin and yang’s embrace. / Hidden or manifest, I gain perfect freedom— / My drunken soul shall never return to Ninghai."* She wrote this, sat in lotus posture, and passed away.

Riding clouds past Kunlun, she looked down and said to Danyang, *"I shall await you on Peng Isle."* Thereupon Danyang immediately wrote a hymn: *"Sixty-one years long, / Unknown to the world— / A clap of thunder, / Vast and drifting with the wind."* With that, he cast aside his brush and ascended.

**First: Gathering the Mind**
Before this body had form,
A single qi already abided;
Like jade, the more it’s polished, the brighter it gleams—
Now refined, how could it remain dull?
Sweep clean the sea of arising and ceasing,
Firmly guard the Gate of Total Retention;
In the half-grain’s empty, numinous space,
The alchemical fire glows warm.

**Second: Nurturing Qi**
This was originally the beginning of non-doing—
Who would have thought it would fall into later heaven?
The moment a sound leaves the mouth,
Three inches already govern its power.
Moreover, worn down by worldly toil,
How can it bear the coils of illness?
When the child grows plump, it nourishes the mother—
Do not say there is no turning back.

**Third: Practicing the Work**
Where breath is gathered and spirit congealed,
The qi of the East arises;
Ten thousand conditions all unattached,
A single qi returns to its terrace.
The yin image should descend before,
The yang light may be planted behind;
From mountain peak to sea’s depths,
After the rain, a single thunderclap.

**Fourth: Slaying the Dragon**
Utmost stillness gives birth to movement,
Yin and yang model each other;
In the wind, seize the Jade Tiger,
In the moon, capture the Golden Crow.
Keep watch on the moment of misty union,
Attend to the paths of sequence and reversal;
Where the Magpie Bridge is crossed again,
The cinnabar qi returns to the furnace.

**Fifth: Nurturing the Elixir**
Bind the tiger and return it to the true cave,
Lead the dragon to gradually augment the elixir;
Nature must be as clear as water,
The mind as still as a mountain;
Regulate the breath to gather the golden crucible,
Calm the spirit to guard the Jade Pass;
Each day, add a grain of millet—
The crane’s hair turns crimson once more.

**Sixth: Embryonic Breathing**
To swiftly complete the elixir,
First dispel the illusory realm;
With every thought, guard the numinous medicine,
With every breath, return to Qian’s origin;
Qi once more flows through the Three Isles,
Spirit forgets and merges with the Great Void;
Whether coming or going,
There is no place not thus.

**Seventh: Kindling the Fire**
Where embryonic breathing is unbroken,
Discern the mechanisms of movement and stillness;
Yang’s light must advance further,
Yin’s waning soul must be prevented from fleeing;
In the pool, the pearl holds its radiance,
On the mountain’s peak, the moon sheds its glow;
At all six hours, do not slacken—
Irrigate the medicinal sprouts to flourish.

**Eighth: Receiving the Medicine**
Half the mystery is realized,
The elixir’s head congeals like dew;
Though it can secure life,
How can it be refined into form?
Through the nose, pure yang is received,
Divine lead permeates the body with numinosity;
Nurture it with utmost care—
When full, it will soar.

**Ninth: Refining Spirit**
The pre-born śarīra,
One day enters my embrace;
Be cautious as one holding a full vessel,
Gentle as one cradling an infant;
The earthly gate must be firmly sealed,
The heavenly portal must first open;
Wash clean the yellow sprout—
On the mountain’s peak, earth-shaking thunder.

**Tenth: Ingesting the Elixir**
The great smelting forges mountains and marshes,
Within it, the workings of creation;
At dawn, welcome the sun crow’s qi,
At night, absorb the moon toad’s essence;
When the time comes, the elixir can be gathered,
The body’s years become pure;
Where the original spirit comes and goes,
Ten thousand pores radiate light.

**Eleventh: Abstaining from Grain**
Having attained the feast of numinous qi,
The lungs and viscera grow wondrously cool;
Forget the spirit, unattached to form,
Merge with the ultimate—there is emptiness and separation;
At dawn, seek mountain taro,
At dusk, gather marsh orchids;
If mixed with smoke and fire,
The body will not tread the Jasper Pool.

**Twelfth: Facing the Wall**
All affairs are now complete,
Serene, seated in a small niche;
The light body rides the purple qi,
The tranquil nature bathes in the clear pool;
Qi blends yin and yang into one,
Spirit unites with heaven and earth as three;
When the work is done, ascend to the Jade Tower,
And with a long whistle, emerge from the misty peaks.

**Thirteenth: Exiting Spirit**
Beyond the body, there is another body—
Not formed by illusory arts;
This numinous qi is all-pervading,
The original spirit, lively and free;
The bright moon congeals golden liquid,
The blue lotus refines jade truth;
When the jade hare’s marrow is simmered,
The pearl shines, never fearing poverty.

**Fourteenth: Soaring Aloft**
The auspicious hour arrives, emerging from the valley,
In an instant, ascending to the divine clouds;
Jade maidens drive the azure phoenix,
Golden lads offer crimson peaches;
Before the flowers, pluck the brocade pipa,
Beneath the moon, play the jade flute;
Once immortal and mortal are sundered,
Coldly cross the sea’s tide.

**Seven-Language Quatrains of Immortal Lady Sun Buer**

I.
Not riding a white crane, I love to ride the simurgh,
Twenty banners swirl to left and right;
By chance entering the literary altar for a smile,
Incense of descending truth coils ‘round the jasper balustrade.

II.
In late spring’s weather, the warm wind melts,
Sunlight bathes the Jiangnan recluse’s home;
It urges the winter plum to burst its buds early—
A pure-hearted one faces the pure-hearted flower.

III.
Resources for life and origin all lie in yin and yang,
The Limitless can open the light of the Supreme Ultimate;
The heart-mirror, diligently polished, shines like the moon—
A mustard seed in the great thousand worlds, yet vast and towering.

IV.
Spirit and qi must be like the night air’s clarity,
From of old, the greatest joy lies in silence;
Within illusion, the true—within the true, illusion—
For now, play with the transformations in the silver basin.

V.
To Peng Isle, one must travel with companions,
A single body cannot ascend the azure cliff;
If withered stillness is taken for cultivation,
The weak waters, brimming, offer few boats.

VI.
Nurture spirit, cherish qi to maintain fullness,
Joy harms yang, anger depletes yin;
The inner brightness of both eyes tames the tiger’s tail,
Dimly, both ears hear the *Yellow Court*.

VII.
Thorns must be made to sprout yellow buds,
Within nature, the wondrous lotus flower resides;
One morning, it suddenly reveals the luminous image—
When you recognize it, that is he.

**Sun Buer’s "Stages of Inner Alchemy for Women" with Annotations by Chen Yingning**

**Preface to Sun Buer’s "Stages of Inner Alchemy for Women" with Annotations by Chen Yingning**

I.
The original fourteen poems are elegant in diction and profound in meaning, representing the highest level of alchemical secrets. They are thus transcribed in full at the beginning of this work to facilitate recitation and study.
*Note: The seven heptasyllabic quatrains of Sun Buer’s "Stages of Inner Alchemy for Women" have already been recorded in the section titled "Sun Buer’s Stages of Inner Alchemy for Women" and will not be repeated here.*

II.
Though the poems are titled *Inner Alchemy for Women*, when compared to the entirety of alchemical teachings for men and women, their differences account for but one or two parts in ten, while their similarities span eight or nine. Thus, men who cultivate immortality may also glean insights from these verses.

III.
The poems employ specialized Daoist terminology, which even the most learned scholars may struggle to fathom—ordinary women, of course, would find them even more obscure. This annotation strives to elucidate their mysteries, revealing all hidden secrets so that the true oral instructions leap forth from the page. Where the sequence of practice cannot be explained in full, this is due to the constraints of the original text. Many references to ancient sayings are drawn from memory, as they aptly convey the subtle truths—preferable to original composition and free from the taint of fabrication.

IV.
Though the annotations are not written in vernacular style, they eschew metaphor in favor of plain speech, making them accessible and easy to understand for anyone proficient in classical Chinese. If even this proves difficult, such a person may lack the karmic affinity for the Dao. For these supreme and wondrous teachings must be imparted only to those of suitable capacity. The poet’s intent was to express her own nature and feelings, not to seek others’ comprehension; the annotator’s aim is to transmit profound learning, not to court popular approval. Thus, the notion of universal salvation lies beyond the scope of this work.

V.
The highest alchemical practices are simple and all-encompassing, without fixed sequence or stages. The "stages" in these poems refer only to the depth of their effects. In terms of practice, the fourteen poems form a single, unbroken progression—no division into segments is possible. To grasp their essential principles, one must view them as a whole, rather than dissecting them piecemeal.

VI.
For women pursuing immortality, the *Celestial Origin* method of ingesting elixirs is fraught with obstacles and impractical, while the *Human Origin* dual-cultivation path is never committed to writing. Thus, this remains the sole authentic tradition for women across the ages, worthy of being called the Great Dao. Other schools, with their myriad names and varied teachings, often lead to corruption when misapplied. Even when practiced correctly, they may only strengthen the body, prolong life, and ensure a peaceful death—still far removed from the Dao of immortality. Those of great aspiration should devote careful attention to this work.

VII.
In ancient times, disciples studied the Dao under a master for twenty years or more. Figures like Yin Changsheng, Bai Yuzhan, and Wu Chongxu lived alongside their teachers, practicing diligently, receiving guidance in real time, and correcting errors step by step before achieving full realization. Modern seekers, however, are fickle and inconsistent, making success elusive. The cunning among them often resort to mercenary tactics, probing and provoking to steal oral instructions, believing that obtaining them guarantees instant transcendence. Yet what they acquire are mere dead methods—the true secrets of immortality emerge only through arduous, hands-on experimentation. Such individuals have never glimpsed them. A word to the reader: if you gain any insight, refine it with care and cultivate it earnestly. Otherwise, possession and non-possession amount to the same.
*This flaw is more common among men; women are less prone to it.*

VIII.
Since the Han dynasty through the late Qing, the three teachings—Confucianism, Buddhism, and Daoism—have endlessly debated their relative merits, with no consensus on superiority. After the fall of the imperial system, Confucianism collapsed entirely, Daoism ceased to function as a coherent tradition, leaving Buddhism as the sole surviving school. Though its followers are many, few engage in genuine practice—monastics least of all. Even the so-called "great lay teachers" offer little beyond instructing others to recite *Amitābha Buddha*. Methods like Chan meditation, *hua tou* inquiry, and *gong’an* exchanges have faded with the rise of Pure Land devotion. Tiantai’s *zhiguan* meditation, though a viable entry point, serves only as material for scriptural lectures, with no one pursuing its actual realization. Recently, the Shingon school, imported from Japan, has gained traction in China, but its hasty recitations often disrupt bodily and mental harmony.
These four approaches—Pure Land, Chan, Shingon, and *zhiguan*—represent the essence of modern Buddhism. Yet they remain one-sided, focusing solely on the mind while offering no resolution to the material realities of birth, aging, illness, and death. Their promise of liberation applies only to the afterlife, leaving practitioners to grapple with mundane needs—food, clothing, desire, and infirmity—just like ordinary people. As for what follows death, only the dead can know; the living can but speculate.

Moreover, the habitual tendencies of Buddhist adherents often lead them to exalt the Buddha alone while dismissing all others, rejecting outright any teachings beyond their own tradition. Though such reverence for a religious founder is to be expected, their rigid demarcation and self-imposed boundaries have stifled progress.

The purpose of this present work is to explore principles of learning, to inspire future like-minded seekers to engage in practical experimentation, and to resolve all questions of human existence—an aim fundamentally distinct from the propagation of religion. Thus, it bears no relation to Daoist figures such as the Primordial Heavenly Worthy, the Most High Lord Lao, or the Jade Emperor. As for the scriptures of Confucianism and Buddhism, as well as the works of the Hundred Schools, whatever may be of use will be gathered opportunely and employed as needed, without regard for sectarian divisions.

Within these pages, occasional comparisons between immortals and buddhas, based on the insights of past masters, are offered with brief commentary. Though such discussions may be partial and incomplete, they at least avoid both arrogance and obsequiousness, sparing the reader from blind conformity that misleads both self and others. Such, indeed, is the proper attitude of a scholar.

In short, regardless of sect, one must demand tangible results within a set timeframe and prioritize attainment in this present life. If this is the aspiration, there is no method other than the Golden Elixir of Returning to the Cinnabar. With this humble sincerity, I dare address my fellow seekers.

---

Nine. Among the world’s religions, their rituals, systems, theories, and practices rarely offer equal opportunities for men and women. The school of immortals alone is different. It is often said that women achieve cultivation faster than men: what takes a man three years to complete, a woman may accomplish in one, owing to the unique physiology of her body, which grants her this advantage. Yet once success is attained, one’s standing depends solely on individual effort, with no distinction between male and female. This is the singular insight of the immortal tradition, setting it apart from all other teachings. Clearly, the path of immortals is utterly free, transcending the bounds of religion and existing purely as a matter of scholarship. Readers should not judge it through the lens of religion. Women of great ambition would do well to enter this gate.

---

Ten. I am not a woman—why then study the women’s elixir formulas? Nor do I intend to become a teacher of worldly women—why then annotate the women’s elixir formulas? It is because I deeply fear that the transmission of this art, passed down for millennia, may now be severed. If it remains concealed and unspoken, future generations will have no means to comprehend it, and even the wise will find no entry. Yet the world is not lacking in learned and principled women who, inspired by great resolve and unyielding perseverance, refuse to be content with the conditions of modern life or to take refuge in the afterlife superstitions of religion. They seek to overcome the difficulties of food, clothing, shelter, and mobility, and to shatter the immutable laws of birth, aging, illness, and death. How can their aspirations be fulfilled if not through the study of immortality?

This, then, is the earnest intention behind my annotations.

Men’s immortality practice relies on the *Taiyang* method of refining *qi*, which is still known in this age. Women’s practice, however, depends on the *Taiyin* method of refining form, which has nearly vanished. Since men’s cultivation requires only that they fulfill their own duties, they need not concern themselves with women’s affairs. Thus, those who transmit the Dao often speak vaguely of women’s practice, and among women themselves, few possess the exceptional talent to receive and pass on this art. From this point forward, I deeply hope that successors will arise.

---

**A Brief Account of Immortal Sun Bu’er**

Immortal Sun, styled Bu’er, was also known as the Serene and Secluded One. She was the youngest daughter of Sun Zhongyi of Ninghai County (Ninghai being part of modern Dengzhou Prefecture in Shandong, not the Ninghai of Zhejiang Province). Born in the second year of Emperor Taizu’s Tianfu reign of the Jin dynasty, she was naturally intelligent, gentle, and refined. Her father betrothed her to Ma Yifu, with whom she bore three sons. Yifu was none other than the Ma Danyang Perfected, one of the Seven Northern Perfected.

After Danyang became a disciple of Wang Chongyang, the ancestral master employed various expedient means to persuade Immortal Sun as well. She then left her three sons behind, severed all worldly ties, and journeyed to the Golden Lotus Hall to seek ordination, where she secretly received the essential teachings of the Dao. Several years later, her master urged Danyang to travel west, and they dwelled in the Mist and Cloud Grotto of Kunlun. Immortal Sun, however, remained at home, diligently cultivating without respite.

In the fifteenth year of Emperor Shizong’s Dading reign of the Jin, she went to Luoyang and took refuge with Immortal Feng, residing in her lower grotto. Six years later, her Dao was perfected. On the nineteenth day of the twelfth month of the twenty-second year of Dading, she suddenly bathed, changed her clothes, and asked her disciples what time it was. Upon learning it was midday, she took up her brush and wrote a verse:

*Three thousand merits fulfilled, transcending the Three Realms,*
*Leaping beyond the confines of yin and yang;*
*Hidden or manifest, freely roaming at will,*
*The drunken soul shall never return to Ninghai.*

Having written this, she sat in lotus posture and passed away. Fragrant winds and auspicious vapors lingered for an entire day.

In the *jisi* year of the Zhiyuan reign of the Yuan dynasty, she was granted the title *Qingjing Yuan Zhen Shunde Zhenren* (True Person of Serene Depths and Compliant Virtue), and her lineage was named the Qingjing (Serene) School.

*(The above is drawn from the* Continuation of the Comprehensive Examination of Literature *and the* Dengzhou Prefecture Gazetteer*, as well as other records. For further details, consult the biographies, chronologies, and specialized texts on the Northern Seven Perfected in the* Daoist Canon*.)*

**Annotations**

Here follows the translation:

---

It is noted that among extant texts on female alchemical formulas (*nüdan jue*), only a few survive—barely one percent of the male alchemical canon. This scarcity is lamentable, and worse still, most were penned by men. Though their words may strike true, they remain secondhand accounts, not the lived experience of women. Apart from Cao Wenyi’s *Song of the Great Dao of the Numinous Source*, this poem may well be the sole surviving work authored by a female adept.

The poem has circulated for generations without annotation. Years ago, in the course of discussing the Dao with a certain lady, I offered explanations from time to time, sending them to her by post. Two decades have since passed. The old drafts lay scattered among stacks of papers, nearly unreadable. I have now retrieved and re-examined them; fortunately, no major errors were found, so I have transcribed them here. I make no claim to have fully grasped Immortal Mistress Sun’s profound meaning, but hope to provide later readers with a path into the text. Some notes may yet fall short of perfection, for my aim is to guide beginners, not to indulge in lofty discourse.

**1. Gathering the Mind**

Before this body had its day,
The primal qi already held sway.

Before we had this form, we had this qi. Tanzi’s *Book of Transformations* states: “Emptiness transforms into spirit, spirit into qi, qi into blood, blood into form, form into the infant, the infant into the child, the child into youth, youth into maturity, maturity into old age, old age into death.” This describes the forward course of human life. But those who attain the Dao can reverse the process: blood returns to qi, qi to spirit, spirit to emptiness—thus achieving immortality.

“Primal qi” refers to the undifferentiated qi before the division of yin and yang. Once yin and yang separate and the Two Modes take shape, it can no longer be called “primal qi.” The Confucians say, “As a thing, it is undivided; thus its generation of things is unfathomable”—this too refers to the primal qi. Laozi’s “attainment of the One” means obtaining this primal qi, which demands real practice, not mere empty talk.

Like jade, polished ever brighter,
Like gold, refined to purest luster.

Alchemists speak of the Jade Pool, Golden Crucible, Jade Hare, Golden Crow, Jade Fluid, Golden Elixir, and many such terms. Generally, yin, spirit, and gentle fire are likened to “jade,” while yang, qi, and martial fire are likened to “gold.” Jade embodies warmth and harmony, gold firmness and strength—though exceptions do occur.

Sweep clean the sea of arising and ceasing,
Firmly guard the gate of total retention.

---

The "sea of arising and ceasing" refers to the thoughts of us all. In a single instant, stray thoughts arise without cause, flickering into being and vanishing again, never settling. When a thought arises, it is birth; when it ceases, it is death. Within a single day, one dies and is reborn ten thousand times—thus the wheel of rebirth unfolds before our very eyes; why wait for proof after the body perishes?

Yet to sweep these thoughts away—how easily said, how difficult done! The only way is to employ a method that unifies the mind. What method? Precisely the firm guarding of the "gate of total retention." This "gate of total retention" is what Laozi called the "mysterious female’s gate," later known in Daoist tradition as the "mysterious pass, the single aperture."

Zhang Ziyang said:
*"This aperture is no ordinary one—
Heaven and Earth together form it.
Called the cavity of spirit and qi,
Within it lies the essence of Kan and Li."*

In plain terms, it is nothing more than one yin and one yang, one spirit and one qi. When yin and yang unite and spirit and qi engage, the substance of the mysterious pass is established.

Though it is said that one must first eliminate delusive thoughts, this does not mean the work is done solely on the level of thoughts. If one rejects all and thinks of nothing, the result will be futile, leaving one disheartened and in despair. This is a matter requiring deep reflection and clear discernment.

*(Zhang Ziyang’s verse admits another interpretation, but it lies beyond the scope of this discussion.)*

At the half-grain’s hollow and numinous point,
The fire’s warmth blends in perfect measure.

"Half-grain" describes how, when spirit congeals into the qi cavity, spirit dwells within qi while qi enfolds spirit without—retreating into secrecy. Its function is most subtle and fine, hence the metaphor of half a grain. "Hollow" means not clinging to appearances. "Numinous" means not sinking into torpor. Distracting thoughts must not arise, for their rise makes the fire parched; true intent must not scatter, for its scattering makes the fire cold. Only when it accords with Laozi’s words—"subtly continuous, as though present, yet not exerting"—does it meet the Middle Way. "Blending" means harmonious and fitting. "Warm" means neither cold nor parched.

These two lines of verse describe the true and practical work of guarding the mysterious pass, capturing its essence with precision. Yet this is decidedly not about fixating on some specific part of the body and rigidly holding to it—beware of misunderstanding. If beginners cling stubbornly to one place without adaptability, they will inevitably develop strange illnesses.

**Nurturing Qi, II**
It begins with non-doing—
how did it fall to the postnatal?
Following nature with non-doing is the Dao of the prenatal;
acting through human effort is the work of the postnatal.

Before we were born, we were originally a single undifferentiated qi, nameless and formless. Unaware, we sank into the womb and thus acquired a body. Once we have a body, great trouble follows. The moment the first cry escapes, three inches seize control. While in the womb, the infant has only fetal breathing, with no nasal respiration. But at the first cry upon birth, external air rushes in through the nose, and postnatal breathing thus takes hold of our life’s authority. At first, the inhaled breath is long and the exhaled breath short, and the body grows stronger daily. Later, inhalation and exhalation become equal in length, and bodily development halts at this point. In middle age, exhalation gradually lengthens while inhalation shortens, and the body declines day by day. At the moment of death, there is only the mechanism of exhalation, with no inhalation—once the nasal breath stops, the root of life is severed. "Three inches" refers to breathing.

Moreover, worn down by worldly toil,
how can one endure the coils of illness?
The above speaks of the natural principle of life and death; this speaks of how people harm themselves. Color, sound, scent, taste, touch, and dharmas are called the "six dusts." Mental and physical labor are both called "toil." Our natural lifespan is already very short, and even without self-inflicted harm, few in this world live past a hundred. Moreover, worldly toil and illness deplete one’s primordial qi, preventing one from fulfilling one’s natural years, so many die prematurely before their time.

*(Someone asked: "The theory of the six dusts is Buddhist terminology—why use it to annotate a Daoist classic?"
Answer: "This is not my fault. The original poem already favors Buddhist terms, such as 'arising and ceasing,' 'thusness,' and 'śarīra,' none of which are originally Daoist. Without citing Buddhist texts, how could one annotate it?")*

When the child is plump, it nourishes the mother—
do not say it cannot return.

"The 'child' refers to postnatal qi; the 'mother' refers to prenatal qi. In the Dao of elixir refinement, postnatal qi is metaphorically called 'water,' while prenatal qi is metaphorically called 'metal.' According to the Five Phases theory, metal generates water—this is prenatal transforming into postnatal. The Dao of elixir refinement emphasizes reversing the course of creation, making water generate metal instead—this is returning from postnatal back to prenatal. The ancients called this the 'Ninefold Cyclic Elixir,' where nine represents the ultimate yang number and also the completion number of metal, hence 'nine returns.' This does not mean it is limited to nine cycles. Prenatal is difficult to grasp, so one must begin with postnatal practice to return to the prenatal. When postnatal qi is sufficiently cultivated, prenatal qi naturally arises—thus it is said, 'When the child is plump, it nourishes the mother.' 'Returning' refers precisely to this reversal and reversion.

**Third Stage of Practice: Gathering Breath and Concentrating Spirit**
At the place where breath is gathered and spirit is concentrated, the generative qi of the East arrives.
'Gathering breath' means the breath of inhalation and exhalation is stored and unmoving. 'Concentrating spirit' means the numinous spirit is focused and undispersed. 'The East' is the position of sunrise; 'generative qi' is spoken of in contrast to dead qi. Ancient practitioners of breath cultivation generally faced east during the hours of *yin* and *mao*, drawing in the generative qi of the void into their bodies, using its power to expel the accumulated dead qi within. Though superior elixir methods are not bound by time or place, they are best practiced in quiet mountain forests during warm, gentle weather—then the effects in the body appear immediately, like a shadow cast by an upright pole. If one can consistently concentrate spirit and gather breath, fermenting and steaming, before long one may extract the primordial qi from the cave of creation.

Confucius said, 'Acting before Heaven, one does not oppose it.' If even Heaven does not oppose it, how much less would humans or spirits? This is real practice, neither empty talk nor mere theory—only those who realize it will know. If one asks, 'How is breath gathered? How is spirit concentrated? Where does one abide? From where does it come?'"

"Since it cannot be clarified in a few words, nor fully conveyed through brush and ink, it requires repeated debate and repeated experimentation. Moreover, the learner must possess innate wisdom and pursue it with painstaking dedication before gaining entry. If every detail were committed to paper, the living method would become a dead one. People’s natures differ, and their constitutions vary—applying this dead method would only invite illness, not merely failing to benefit but causing harm. What good would that serve?

Let go of all entanglements, and the single qi returns to the terrace.

As the ancients said: 'Those who cultivate the Dao must sever all entanglements, uphold a single thought, making this heart as still as death—only then can one avoid death; making this qi unbroken and ceaseless—only then can it endure forever.'

What is this 'terrace'? It is the numinous terrace. The numinous terrace is one’s nature. The 'single qi' is one’s life. When life returns to nature, it is the restoration of the elixir.
