**VII.** The lecture hall should be equipped with a blackboard and chalk. When encountering passages relevant to the scripture’s meaning, the lecturer may write them out on the spot for the audience’s reference.

**VIII.** Regarding the practical oral instructions of *nüdan* cultivation, any details unsuitable for public discourse should follow the transmission rules of past masters. The lecturer must not violate ancient precedents, nor should the audience insist on disclosure.

---

**Chapter One: Nourishing Life**
The two modes intermingle, life originating from Qian;
All things take form, nourished by Kun.
Kun’s yielding and steadfastness align with Qian’s compliance,
Storing and congealing, its Dao is upright.
The work of bearing all things—none but Kun can achieve it.
Paired with Heaven, it establishes the ultimate standard.
In singularity and constancy, yin and yang do not err,
Mysteriously giving rise to transformation.
Every being relies on it for growth and sustenance,
Each breath draws from its enduring presence.
Profound is the principle of ceaseless generation;
Subtle is the source of endless transformation.
Within utmost stillness lies utmost movement,
From the turbid abyss, the clear stream divides.
To grasp the guiding threads of feminine virtue,
First discern the profound mysteries of Kun’s primal power.

The earth bears all beneath the sky,
Yin holds the marvel of containing yang.
Illuminating the Four Conducts to establish a fragrant model,
Rejecting the Seven Emotions to return to the supreme Dao,
Moderating deportment to leave a mark in history,
Refining the spirit to attain the Purple Palace’s title—
Discoursing on the scripture to uphold the eternal model of motherhood,
Wielding the brush to impart teachings to all women.
The work of nourishing life begins with proclaiming its essence.

---

**Chapter Two: Transforming Qi**
Yin and yang alternate in endless cycles,
Day and night shift in ceaseless motion.
Qi divides at the two solstices,
Its movement embracing the Three Origins’ marvels.
The mechanism of transformation leaves no trace,
Its pivot lying at the center;
Substance and function are interdependent,
Each concealing the other at their juncture.
Vast and boundless, it begins as non-being yet manifests being,
Ultimately returning from being to non-being.
Flowing in primordial vastness, from solidity it becomes void,
From void it verifies solidity.
Void and solid, solid and void—
their origins remain inscrutable;
Being and non-being, non-being and being—
their signs are equally unfathomable.
The precelestial Supreme Ultimate is the root of creation,
The great Dao of Qian and Kun is the vitality of all beings.
Women, embodying Kun’s form and inheriting Qian’s work,
Attain stillness and oneness.
Stillness concentrates in tranquility,
Oneness refines in virtue.
Unknowing and unperceiving, they follow the Emperor’s decree,
Grasping the true mechanism of receptivity,
Harmonizing the sun and moon within the body.
Ceaselessly flowing in natural spontaneity,
Each breath returns to the root and cave.
Drawing the clear spring from the Water Palace,
Nurturing the luminous moon of the Spirit Terrace—
Awakening to the subtle and mysterious,
They become immortals of the Jasper Pool.

---

**Chapter Three: Purifying Karma**
To ascend the immortal’s steps, one must eliminate evil karma.
Before evil is purged, virtue cannot flourish.
If the mind is deluded by desire,
Or emotions entangled in attachment—
Whether lingering in coquetry,
Or swayed by sorrow, laughter, or tears;
Whether ensnared by unbroken threads of longing,
Dragged into the depths by their pull;
Or misled into the net of illusion,
Suffering injustice on the wrong path—
The Yellow Springs echo with sorrow,
Vainly lamenting the loss of reason;
The netherworld’s winds scatter regrets,
Yet the roots of love remain.
Bound by such fetters,
How can one escape the wheel of rebirth?
To emerge from the sea of illusion,
Rely solely on the torch of wisdom.
Body, speech, and mind must never invite transgression;
Killing, stealing, and sexual misconduct must be scrupulously avoided.
Sincerely embracing goodness is like fine grain basking in the morning sun;
A myriad of thoughts dissolve like boiling water melting snow.
Purify the source to properly cultivate,
Awaken to causes and conditions—
Attaining the Dao is then no difficult task.

---

**Chapter Four: Cultivating Goodness**
When worldly karma is fully cleansed,
Sweeping away dross to expand the mind’s clarity;
When past and present harmonize,
Clearing the brambles to illuminate the nature’s sky—
The empty and numinous shine forth,
Revealing the constancy of innate goodness.
Gather the spirit and focus on cultivating noble conduct.
Accumulated goodness brings blessings,
While accumulated evil brings calamity—
As the Kun hexagram records, good intentions run deep.
The Dao of the Most High refines qi to achieve suppleness;
The words of the *Chu Book* declare goodness as the essence.
A gentle and yielding nature can rectify conduct;
Goodness returns to softness, manifesting kindness and humility.
Compose the will with solemnity,
Restrain the body with warmth and tranquility.
Embrace emptiness with harmony,
Uphold constancy with wondrous responsiveness.
Nurture qi through silence,
Purify the heart without contention.
Cherish all life to preserve vitality,
Study the Dao’s essentials to clarify true nature.
Having fulfilled the duties of human relationships,
Delve into the profound mysteries of the unseen.
Avoid empty talk of embroidered images—
Instead, investigate the heart-seal of the returned elixir.
Never dismiss small acts of goodness,
Nor resent the goodness of others.

Amidst the harmonious light of wind and moon, within the curtains of one’s natural disposition, one lights incense to reverently worship the primordial spirit of one’s own nature, and pours water to cultivate the luminous treasury of clarity. Let none say that women lack outstanding talent, for one must know that the Mysterious Gate holds the wondrous subtleties of *Kun*-tranquility.

**Chapter Five: Exalting Virtue**
Heaven has five thieves—when employed, they bring prosperity;
Humans possess five blessings—when cultivated, they bring goodness.
Great virtue does not claim virtue, flowing like a river;
Small virtues accumulate virtue, earnestly practiced and transforming.
In essence, it is *Gen*-stillness; in function, it is adaptability.
Attaining the mean, all traces and images dissolve.
The great transformation is called sageliness—its spirit cannot be fathomed.

The work of women’s cultivation begins with eliminating hidden faults.
What is the key? Distinguishing delusion to attain truth.
Now, women’s perceptions often err toward yin’s secrecy,
Wavering in ambiguity, suspicion, and indecision.
Thus, their passions and desires are prone to arrogance and folly,
While their understanding is frequently clouded by confusion.
Moreover, they seldom peruse the classics,
And even refined daughters of official families merely adorn themselves with embroidered curtains and painted chambers;
Noble ladies of gentry clans do no more than recite verses on snow and wind.
Needlework and embroidery may display boudoir marvels,
While seductive dances and amorous songs further flaunt their allure—
Yet how few know the noble beauty of chastity and stillness,
Or possess the pure excellence of lofty virtue.
Of old, the woman of Beiguo declined office, her fame resounding in Chu;
Meng Guang lifted the tray to eye level, earning praise from Liang Hong.
Yet while great families issued instructions, their words were not detailed;
The *Biographies of Exemplary Women* left their transmissions incomplete.
Here, therefore, the *Kun-Tranquility* is wondrously expounded
To serve as a model for the inner chambers.
Talented women of the boudoir, let virtue be your foundation;
Fragrant bedding and fine talents—may they aspire to this exalted hope.
From beginning to end, never abandon it, that your roots may remain firm.

**Chapter Six: Women’s Education**
To nurture correctness in youth is the work of sage-making.
*Kun* is fundamentally yielding—this is the Dao of softness.
Of old, there were worthy women who established teachings through their own conduct.
Their orchid-like nature was innate; their fragrant words were emulated.
They preserved chastity without marrying, guarding the inner chamber for a decade.
Gentle in temperament and graceful in demeanor, their wisdom was serene and refined.
Rising early and retiring late, their filial piety and reverence were sincere.
They governed subordinates with harmony and cultivated themselves with dignity.
In movement and speech, they adhered to rules and discipline.
The tortoise-mirror and grand chronicles once recorded women’s histories:
Some moved their husbands through filial devotion to the divine,
Some surpassed men in loyalty and steadfastness,
Some were as stern as autumn frost,
Some as radiant as the sun in the heavens,
Some had righteousness that could pierce metal and stone,
Some had valor that could stir wind and thunder,
Some had wisdom to resolve great doubts,
Some had talent to aid an era.
Tracing their virtuous deeds, their fragrance lingers through the ages.
Drawing from their fine example, a hundred years gain luster.
You, ladies of the boudoir, keenly observe these precedents.
Do not covet empty glory or pride yourselves on literary brilliance.
Wash away cosmetic adornments; do not boast of extravagant attire or exotic makeup.
Compose your brush with solemnity; do not craft ornate phrases or flowery lines.
Cultivate ethical relations and love learning;
Delight in the *Book of Rites* and understand the *Book of Poetry*.
Devote yourself to weaving and sewing; do not merely adorn yourself with delicate craft.
Purify your conduct in the inner quarters, embodying frugality and diligence.
Rectify soft virtue to perfect your reputation.
Further refine your true nature and preserve your primordial essence,
Achieving merit in both inner and outer realms,
Refining qi from dawn to dusk.
Thus, even in maidenhood, one may attain the Dao,
And ride the simurgh or crane to ascend in flight.

**Chapter Seven: The Way of the Wife**
The way of the wife is revered and requires steadfast cultivation.
She is the equal counterpart to *Qian*, her maternal demeanor impeccable.
At the time of tying the sash, her kind mother’s instructions
Must be respected and heeded, never disobeying her husband.
The bond of husband and wife is the beginning of human relationships.
Governing the household requires teaching; the main chamber demands propriety.
Pulling the deer-cart together, sharing coarse blankets without shame,
Drawing water and grinding grain with one’s own hands, finding no disgrace in simple fare.
Do not meddle in trivial matters or speak of inner-chamber affairs.
Having assisted the head of the household, instruct children and grandchildren.
Like Jing Jiang, who diligently spun thread,
Or Meng Mother, who moved thrice for her son’s education,
Or the mother who prepared bear gall to aid her son’s studies,
Or the wife who sent salted fish to cultivate integrity,
Or the woman who received lessons from behind a screen,
Or the one who cut her hair to detain a guest—
These former worthies have passed; who will continue their fine legacy?
In all wealthy and noble families, one must abandon haughty airs.
Within the household, foster benevolence and deference—
Thus, descendants will be fine and their fragrance enduring.
Even those who engage in humble work must extinguish the sprouts of resentment.
With mutual respect, joy and contentment may be found;
Children and grandchildren will surely flourish.
Caution against greed and delusion to pacify violent temper,
Sober infatuation to prevent dissipation and excess.
If a wife’s virtue is irreproachable, human relationships will be fulfilled.
Good fortune then brings sons and longevity;
Blessings bring peace to the body and glory to one’s name.
Having attained such noble beauty, the mysteries of cultivation may be pursued.
Having guided you in your fundamental duties,
I further instruct you in the true scripture.

**Chapter Eight: Scriptures and Treatises**
In high antiquity, the world was undifferentiated, its qi and beings pure and simple.
Harmonizing yin and yang, all was luminous and bright—names and forms were undivided.
Then the *Qiu Suo* arose; in middle antiquity, Fu Xi and Shen Nong
Drew diagrams and expounded the trigrams, creating written records to inaugurate teachings.
They bequeathed canonical texts and plans, flourishing from the Yu and Xia dynasties.
Yet all their writings transmitted this single heart-seal—
There was no distinction, much less division between men and women.
Moreover, in this endowment of life, all share the same primordial origin.
Though their forms differ, their principles are the same.
Only essence and qi, with spirit as their master.
Whether pure or turbid, the heart-monarch governs.
Curb desires and forget passions to lay the foundation and refine the self.
The Mysterious Female harmonizes; the tide’s mark vanishes.
From the ordinary and near, one ascends from the dust to the heavens’ summit.
Stabilizing contemplation is the work of self-mastery;
The *Yellow Court* conceals the true person’s countenance.
The Western Flower proclaimed wondrous transformation;
The Golden Mother drew forth the numinous wind.
Preserving form requires no corpse-liberation;
Refining qi enters directly into the celestial vault.
Maidens, unharmed by the injuries of intercourse and childbirth,
Easily transform their forms to awaken enlightenment.
Women, often defiled by the corruption of pregnancy and childbirth,
Must purify their aspirations and cultivate their bearing.
Abandon all private desires; extinguish the myriad distractions.
Broadly study scriptures and treatises to enter the gate of myriad wonders.

**Chapter Nine: Awakening from Delusion**

Vast as the dusty sea, surging as wind and waves,
Water and land shift through kalpas; ancient and modern pass like morning and dusk.
This floating life is but a transient lodging—
Alas for the five turbidities of this bodily form, a dream dissolving by dawn;
Lament the fleeting decades, skin like a chicken’s, hair like a crane’s.
Scarce can youth’s crimson glow endure—jade beauty and flower-like visage
Are swiftly entombed in the green barrow.
Some are burdened by sons and daughters,
Others stained by the allure of splendor.
If one does not seek early escape from the path of delusion,
How can one abide long in the mortal realm?

Born, life is already ephemeral;
Dead, how then to transcend?
Women, by nature serene and retiring,
Thus find cultivation secure and steadfast:
Firmly seal the golden essence within the mysterious chamber,
Sever the celestial waters at the layered pass.
Their merit surpasses the crimson snow elixir,
Their spirit roams the gardens of Langfeng.
They laugh at the coquetry of powdered faces,
Equating it with the affectations of actors.

Seizing this opportunity for universal deliverance,
Swiftly board the Dharma-boat and retreat into seclusion.
The women of old who realized the Dao
All dwelt atop Penglai’s summit.
Awaken the deluded beside your pillow;
Do not mistake the illusions before your eyes.
Know that the work of return and restoration
Must be undertaken with urgency and diligence.

The pure and tranquil source is the foundation of life and destiny—
The sublime principle of Earth’s origin is known to few.
A trace of dawn’s moon glimmers in the east,
Yet none fathom the time before this bodily birth.

---

**Chapter Ten: The Earth’s Foundation**

The two qi intertwine; the central yellow responds to the mysterious.
The five phases engender one another, yet only Earth is complete.
Its virtue is stability,
Its merit deep accumulation,
Its nature single-minded,
Its function true and constant.
It nurtures the ten thousand beings, fostering their flourishing;
Above, it aligns with Heaven; below, it connects with the abyss.
It harmonizes the hundred meridians,
Irrigates the three fields.

The yellow sprout emerges from the soil—
Behold the tender shoots of the medicine;
White snow congeals into butter—
Discern the wondrous tone of the ice-pure vessel.
Secure the primal essence within the mysterious female;
Enter a single thought into the profound obscurity.
Begin by mastering the self;
Apply effort solely in preserving the spirit.
In the four dignities, practice silent illumination;
Within inner visualization, settle the mind.
Only when the Celestial Monarch attains tranquility
Can one circulate and traverse freely.

Without grasping the true essence,
All efforts are but empty names.
It is like building a house—
First, one must lay the foundation.
Or like firing a furnace—
First, one must kindle the flame.
The five phases gather and cluster,
Binding the affinity of the central palace’s numinous terrace;
The four images are arranged,
Unfolding the mysteries of the Earth’s alchemical chamber.
Without recognizing the mysterious pass,
One cannot speak of the supreme Dao.

Constantly illumine the root within this bodily birth;
Investigate life and destiny through the teachings of immortality.
Mind is Dao; Dao is attainable.
---

**Chapter Eleven: The Root**

In this world, whether man or woman,
To know the root is to enter the Dao.
The root is the origin of nature;
The stem is the stalk of life.
Like a tree, one must cultivate its root—
Only when the root is firm can it flourish.
Or like a flower or fruit, which first sprouts from the stem—
Only when the stem is replete can it ripen.

How can one fail to safeguard the human root?
Tracing back to its origin, the root was originally steadfast—
Why willingly hack and wound it?
Self-inflicted harm,
Extinguishing nature and trivializing life,
One sinks among the blind multitudes.
Thus, the single spark of numinous light from the primordial beginning
Gradually erodes,
Inevitably leading to perdition.

Consider the myriad beings of the cosmos—
Each has its own root.
Even the tiniest creatures
Know to nurture their lives.
How can humans,
Of all beings, be inferior to them?

Yet when blood and qi are disharmonious, the root is difficult to establish;
When the bodily form is leaky, the root is difficult to complete;
When pregnancies are many, the root is difficult to secure;
When love and desire cling, the root is difficult to strengthen;
When ignorance and turbidity mingle, the root is difficult to clarify;
When spirit and will are chaotic, the root is difficult to pacify;
When greed and self-interest disturb, the root is difficult to purify;
When deceit and pretense become habit, the root is difficult to preserve.
Thus, in cultivation, progress cannot be refined.

Knowing these ills, sweep them away one by one.
Do not shake your root;
Do not harm your foundation.
Cherish your nature and life;
Guard your essence and qi at all times.
Calm the spirit and preserve the true;
Dispel delusion and uphold sincerity.
Investigate the root alone—
Thus may one attain longevity.

---

**Chapter Twelve: Nature and Life**

Life originates from nature; nature is rooted in life.
They are the ancestors of Heaven and Earth,
The numen of the ten thousand things.
Before life was established, nature was originally the same;
After life exists, it does not depart from this nature.
The goodness of innate virtue
Is possessed by all.
Though there are men and women,
Nature knows no distinction.

Tracing back to the origin,
Nature is nameless.
Before the Supreme Ultimate divided,
How could nature and life be separate?
Only after the Two Modes emerged
Did nature and life become manifest.

Nature is the treasure of life;
Life is the source of nature.
To cultivate nature is to preserve the mind;
To refine life is to realize the Dao.

Do not resign yourself to fate—
That is to belittle life.
Do not falsely claim nature is evil—
That is to misconstrue nature.
To know the root of nature and life,
One must investigate the wondrous workings of Heaven and Earth.

Within yang, yin is contained to receive form;
Within the moon, the sun is embraced to generate light.
This inherent interplay of Heaven’s mechanism
Is the sublime principle of nature and life.

Movement begins in the beginningless;
When movement reaches its extreme, yin arises.
Stillness abides in the endless;
When stillness reaches its extreme, yang arises.
One yin, one yang;
One movement, one stillness.
Clear and turbid, above and below—
Thus creation is revealed.
The root of yin and yang, movement and stillness,
Is the essence of nature, life, body, and mind.

A single numinous awareness illumines—
The sea of nature ever emits the light of wisdom.
When the ten thousand things are all empty,
The Gate of Life alone opens the path of birth.
To preserve nature is to preserve the whole, to receive the whole, to return to the whole;
To refine life is to refine immortality, to refine the Dao.
Mutual cultivation of both
Is the ultimate practice.

---

**Chapter Thirteen: The Substance of the Mind**

The substance of the mind is non-action,
Profoundly still and ever tranquil.
Before any sign appears,
The mechanism of transformation vanishes.
The Supreme Void is undifferentiated,
Silent and motionless.
The Great Emptiness is formless,
Its wonder beyond comparison.
Subtle and minute, pure and unified—
When yin and yang first divide,
There is one to preside.
Forcibly made the pivot,
It is called the Celestial Mind.

**Chapter Fourteen: Pointing to the Mysterious**

The primordial qi is employed with the acquired spirit;
The acquired substance is named by the primordial.
Thus do heaven and earth establish life,
And all beings secure their bodies.
Tang and Yu transmitted it in succession,
While sages and worthies preserved it in perpetuity.
Tracing the ten thousand things to their one source,
Uniting the Three Teachings in the one truth.
Only the real, only the one—
Ever wakeful, ever luminous.
Vast and empty yet undimmed,
Its substance radiant and clear.

To know the Dao-mind as the root of the human mind
Is to see the human mind as the function of the Dao-mind.
To speak of the Dao-mind is not the Dao-mind;
To speak of the human mind is not the human mind.
To speak of a mind as existent yet not perceive it as such,
To speak of no-mind yet not perceive it as absent—
Do not stir the deluded mind,
But stir the mind of awareness.
The mind of awareness ever illumines,
The deluded mind ever empty.
The fundamental substance thus abides,
And the true mind appears.

To grasp or abandon it is still effort;
To forget both grasping and abandoning
Is to attain the solitary realization of the fasting of the mind.
The teaching of the four "do nots"
Returns to spontaneity.
Like the moon’s reflection in a cold pond,
Like still water’s clarity—
The substance of the mind, profound and still,
Is likewise thus.

Goodness or evil of nature are but provisional names;
Dao-mind and human mind have caused endless dispute through the ages.
Clinging to words and grasping at images,
None fathom the original truth.
Primordial and acquired—
Which aligns, which diverges?
I reveal the substance of the mind to you all:
Seek only the Dao-mind, do not scrutinize the human mind;
Awaken only the true mind, do not give rise to the deluded mind;
Preserve only the mind of awareness, do not stir the selfish mind;
Abide in no-mind, do not cling to a mind of existence.
In such tranquil equanimity,
The hundred parts of the body obey.
To cultivate the Dao or refine immortality
Follows what the mind realizes.

**Chapter Fourteen: Pointing to the Mysterious**

The mysterious cannot be pointed to;
To point is not the mysterious.
Since nothing can be pointed to,
The mysterious is hard to express.
What then is spoken of?
The empty void itself.

The mysterious within the mysterious
Is called the ultimate meaning.
When mind and nature are utterly still,
The empty void shatters.
Without substance or form,
What aim or flavor could there be?
Yet this wondrous method
Is the supreme vehicle.
Mysterious beyond mystery,
Beyond all description.

The pure Dao-body—
All may attain this.
Sudden awakening to the nature of heaven
Leaps beyond all bounds.
Those of middling capacity or below
Scarcely hear of this subtle principle.
Thus is guidance offered,
Opening the gate of expedient means.
Though its meaning ranks second,
Its Dao is the same in return.
Those who aspire to cultivate truth
May rely upon this.

The Dao’s wonder is stored in the subtle and profound,
While spirit and essence congeal in the mysterious female.
The gate of life, the door of death—
Exiting Kan, entering Li—
None surpass this,
For the mysterious is the barrier.
The bellows blends yin and yang,
The furnace and tripod are established—
None lie beyond this,
For the mysterious is the key.

This mysterious one
Is the master of nature and life,
The foundation of creation,
The seed of the embryo,
The abode of the primordial spirit.
Thus it is called the Five Mysteries,
Establishing the ultimate of the Three Powers.
Heart, liver, spleen, and lungs
Each have their repository,
Yet the primordial essence
Returns solely to the sea of the kidneys.
This is the pivot of the human body,
The destination of the stars,
Where the hundred vessels converge,
Where the three carts transport,
Their axle set in motion.
For men and women cultivating truth,
All lies here—
Mysterious, oh mysterious!
Dark and indistinct,
Being within non-being,
Non-being within being.
I would point to it,
Yet nothing can be pointed to.
Know this mystery,
Then gathering medicine and applying fire,
You may naturally achieve the seven returns and nine reversions.
Without the work of refining the self,
You will struggle to lay the foundation.
The immortals and sages of past ages
Have spoken of this in detail.
Pointing to the true mechanism,
The great elixir is easily refined.
Universally binding Earth’s affinity,
Together we become companions in the Dharma.

**Chapter Fifteen: The Golden Elixir**

Eons of true cultivation,
A legacy unbroken through millennia—
Who has heard its echo?
Who can discern the scorched paulownia?
Who can split the jade?
How would they know the uncut stone?
Hares nursing foals,
Different species seeking one another.
Swallows nesting in a phoenix’s nest—
Lesser virtues delude themselves.
With such examples,
How can one hope to learn longevity?
To shoulder the great Dao
Is no different from bearing a mountain.
Unenlightened about life and death,
How can one grasp the elixir’s essence?
Rather than stray into side paths,
Better to rest in stillness.
Yet most learners in the world
Are just like this.
Gazing across land and sea,
How truly lamentable!

Moreover, women,
Unenlightened about the subtle and profound,
Sit secluded in chambers,
Wasting their beauty in vain.
Even with aspiration,
Where would they find a teacher?
Pitying your delicate forms,
I open a swift path—
A method grounded in truth,
Free from fragmentation.
Within this very body,
Trace the source to its origin.
The female elixir is most simple,
The Earth Dao most easy.

As the dawn sun rises,
Its light just beginning to appear—
Circulate mercury to match lead,
Spirit and qi both abiding.
Accumulating qi begins in the land of generative qi;
Preserving spirit is the path to refining spirit.
First cut off desire and forget emotion,
Then enter the chamber and sit in meditation,
Refining the self as men do.

Regulate the breath, soft and unforced—
When the first yang stirs,
Practice the work of zi, wu, mao, and you.
When the hundred vessels are open,
Determine the positions of Qian, Dui, Kan, and Li.
The mysterious female established,
The tripod emits the yellow sprout.
The bellows opens,
Heaven bestows sweet dew.

Primordial essence congeals mercury in the mud-pill of the Niwan;
The fire of spirit circulates, refining the Jade Peak.
Carefully observe the signs of the tide’s approach,
Reversing the flow of the Yellow River, the waters naturally course through.
Golden essence transforms into liquid,
Cinnabar mercury radiates light.
Guard the numinous elixir in the original chamber,
Nurture true qi in the yellow room.
After forty-nine days, the elixir’s foundation is firm;
After a hundred days, the Red Dragon descends.
Refining form is refining qi—
This is the great elixir’s method.

**Chapter Sixteen: The Jade Dipper**

Heaven has the seven luminaries,
Wielding the authority of the jade armillary.
Humans have the seven orifices,
Subtly employing form and spirit.
Vessels and channels align with celestial movements,
Stars converge at the mysterious aperture.
Comprehending the pivot and balance of the Jade Dipper,
One ascends to the rank of the celestial perfected.
Using this as a universal bridge,
It guides you directly into the land of immortals.

All women,
With sincere and pure hearts,
In the stillness of night,
When the first yang of zi turns,
Concentrate the spirit and sit upright,
Calm the breath and lower the light.
Knock the teeth to gather essence,
Silently recite the numinous verses.

Direct the spirit to the primordial sea, passing straight through the kidney hall, ascending via the Jiaji Pass to pay homage to the Jade Emperor. The essence of stars moves the seal, the celestial sun blazes brilliantly. Above, it connects with the Northern Dipper, purple qi rising between the brows. Visualize the true form, illuminating my yellow chamber. The cinnabar primordial spirit-palace radiates luminous splendor, containing and emitting light. Azure, vermilion, white, and yellow—Wood, Fire, Metal, and Earth—along with the dark essence of kidney water, form five colors. These align directly with the Dipper’s radiance, intertwining as companions. Together they enter the cinnabar primordial, nurturing the sea of essence, transforming into the true person’s form, bursting forth from the crown of the head. Passing through the North Polar Palace, with sincere devotion, one pays homage, circling the Dipper’s city before returning to the original body. Gathering the golden light, nurturing essence and cleansing marrow, the five qi return to the origin—no practice surpasses this. Diligently cultivate it, and in three years, distant ascension is achieved.

This is the secret chapter of the Jade Dipper, the supreme vehicle’s essence. Those of wisdom who truly cultivate, if destined, may attain it.

**Chapter Seventeen: Realizing the Truth**

To cultivate the Dao is to cultivate immortality; to aspire to sageliness is to aspire to worthiness. There is no distinction between men and women—only in the single-minded devotion of the heart. Sincerity without ceasing endures; spiritual illumination lies within each person. If one can practice with embodied dedication, wisdom and perfect comprehension naturally arise. To hear of the great Dao, one must understand true cultivation. If cultivation is not genuine, how can realization be authentic? Know that true realization discards superficialities, exhausting principle and fulfilling nature to grasp life itself. Leaping from the mundane cage, one reaches the realm of the sacred.

Worldly cultivation clings to names, and by clinging to names, it lacks substance. To pass away without awakening is deeply lamentable. Though the Three Teachings all possess true realization, their fruitions are not necessarily identical. From beginning to end, in substance and function, they may be partial and incomplete. Grasping only one aspect, few achieve success. You must understand: in women’s cultivation, the work is divided into nine grades, each grade into three steps. Three nines accumulate, forming twenty-seven layers. Cultivating both nature and life—this is the great vehicle. Illuminating substance and mastering function, penetrating beginning and end, the yang spirit universally transforms, its light filling the void. Yet the void is not clung to—what void is not real? Within lies the profound mechanism, the ebb and flow of yin and yang. Profoundly still and perfectly luminous, the true reality is clearly understood. May all of you devote yourselves to this meaning, verify it through practice, and not merely chase names and reputations. The Most High forgets emotions, extinguishing thoughts and deliberations. True realization is not empty—aim for the highest.

**Chapter Eighteen: Arousing the Mind**

The great void is profound and boundless, its dharmic vow vast and deep. The sea of suffering is endless, but turning the heart is the shore. All good devotees, present and future, holding this heart-incense, together pledge sincere vows: arouse the mind of true faith, without doubt; arouse the mind of diligent progress, without laziness; arouse the mind of resolute determination, without entanglement; arouse the mind of humility, without arrogance; arouse the mind of aspiration, without mundane attachments; arouse the mind of purity, without desire; arouse the mind of compassion, without harm; arouse the mind of wisdom, without greed or anger; arouse the mind of perfect comprehension, without attachment. Vow to refrain from all evil and practice all good.

**Women’s Orthodox Methods**
*Editorial Note on the Daoist Studies Series*

**I.**
The origins of Daoist studies trace back to the Daoist school of the pre-Qin era. The teachings of Daoism originated with the Yellow Emperor and reached their culmination with Laozi. They flowed into Zhuangzi and Liezi, transformed into Han Fei and Guiguzi, and branched into Heguanzi and Huainanzi. The history of Chinese Daoism predates the emergence of Indian Buddhism by over two thousand years, making its lineage the most venerable—unmatched by any other religious or philosophical tradition in the world.

**II.**
Daoism diverged into distinct streams, one of which evolved into Confucianism. Confucianism further branched into the Neo-Confucianism of the Song and Ming dynasties. Thus, the scope of Daoist studies is broader than that of Neo-Confucianism.

**III.**
Within Daoism, the tradition of self-cultivation became the foundation of later Immortalist schools. The Yellow Emperor pursued immortality even amid warfare, while Laozi explicitly expounded the Way of "longevity and enduring vision." Therefore, the term *Daoist studies* encompasses the study of immortality.

**IV.**
The editor had long planned a comprehensive *Anthology of Immortality and Dao*, vast in scope and profound in depth, which has since been published in woodblock editions. However, as the process requires considerable time, the editor—eager to satisfy scholars’ desire for early access—has now undertaken the compilation of this *Daoist Studies Series*. The selection of materials is meticulous, publication swift, and emphasis placed on practical application, eschewing empty discourse. Though the volumes are concise, their methods are boundless.

**V.**
The editorial aim of this series is to promote China’s indigenous Daoist studies while resolutely eliminating superstition. Any text even slightly tainted by superstition has been excluded.

---

**Preface to *Women’s Orthodox Methods* by Chen**
This work was originally titled *Zhihua’s Direct Pointers to Women’s Orthodox Methods* and was authored by Qingxia Lingyang Daoren. It was transmitted to the world as one of the few specialized texts for women’s cultivation.

Its purpose is to guide women—whether renunciates or lay devotees of the Dao—in verifying and refining their pure practice. However, due to its long circulation, the text has been extensively corrupted by blind and misguided practitioners. For instance, the *General Explanation* section, though over twelve hundred characters in length, is a patchwork of hackneyed phrases and trite expressions, and thus has been omitted. Additionally, the sections on Daoism, Confucianism, Buddhism, and heterodox teachings have been removed, as they bear no relevance to women’s internal alchemy (*nüdan*). Moreover, their discussions of the three teachings’ core principles and histories contain numerous omissions and errors, while the section on heterodoxy is particularly unrefined. The text has therefore been revised beginning from the first chapter through the sixth, which detail women’s internal alchemy methods. Though these techniques are somewhat contrived and not entirely natural, they have a long-standing tradition, and practitioners should be familiar with them. The seventh chapter is overly brief, while the eighth and ninth chapters, which discuss the yang spirit, incorporate many foreign terms inconsistent with Immortalist terminology. The present edition follows the corrections of Yang Yiyu’s 1858 woodblock version to avoid the confusion of "fish eyes with pearls."

The tenth chapter is of little importance, and the eleventh consists merely of the author’s speculations, neither warranting discussion. The two appended texts are included for reference only. The original edition also contained sixteen seven-character quatrains titled *Quick Methods for Women’s Orthodox Practice*, but as they merely reiterate the preceding content, they have been omitted.

**A Note to the Reader**
The study of immortality rests on four fundamental principles:
1. **Value substance over emptiness**;
2. **Focus on practice, not theory**;
3. **Prize the counterflow over the compliant**;
4. **Emphasize oral instructions over written texts**.

All authentic internal alchemy scriptures and Daoist works should be evaluated according to these principles to avoid delusion. This book, in its present form, adheres to these tenets: it speaks of *practice*, not theory, and advocates the *counterflow*, not compliance.

What has been transmitted here are *oral instructions*, not mere *text*. It conforms to the second, third, and fourth principles, yet the original has been recklessly altered by later hands. Terms like *maṇi dhāraṇī* have been misapplied, muddling the underlying principles, and the entire system of women’s practice has been rendered neither fish nor fowl—deviating from the very essence of the Dao of immortality and thus failing the first principle of valuing substance over emptiness. Therefore, all obvious interpolations have been excised to strip away the false and preserve the true. Men of wisdom in this world will surely concur.

*Dated June, the twenty-fourth year of the Republic of China (4632 in the Yellow Emperor’s calendar), inscribed in Shanghai by Chen Yingning of Wanjiang.*

**Women’s Orthodox Methods of Practice**
*Original author: Lingyang Daoren*
*Editor: Chen Yingning*

**General Discussion**
At sixteen, a boy’s essence flows; when full, it spills. At fourteen, a girl’s menses begin; when full, they overflow. To prevent spillage or overflow, one must master wind and fire. Fire is the primordial spirit; wind is the true breath. Spirit and breath depend on each other, attained through contemplation. The method directs the gaze through the mysterious aperture of the eyes into the qi cavity, where qi enfolds the spirit, both gathered by intent. The natural interplay of wind and fire, ceaseless in motion, transmutes essence into qi, qi into spirit. When spirit is perfected and form transcended, a body exists beyond the body.

The oral instruction states:
*If spirit and breath ever attend each other,*
*The jade liquid flows, transforming the frame.*
*Only by gazing long into the cave of longevity*
*Is the yang spirit refined, emerging at the crown.*
*Know that all born things must die,*
*Yet grasp that the primordial spirit, though dead, revives.*
*If the heart’s spirit dwells within qi,*
*The infant is nurtured, and the work is complete.*

Those who cultivate thus need not fear the internal elixir will fail.

The method employs the *Chong*, *Ren*, and *Du* meridians, circulating through the outer, middle, and inner passes. Women’s practice differs slightly: it begins at the upper pass of the breast stream, proceeds to the middle pass within the navel, and culminates at the lower pass of the womb. The middle and lower passes are then merged into a single cavity. Men refine essence, called *Taiyang refining qi*; women refine blood, called *Taiyin refining form*.

The secret of fire and wind lies in balancing civil and martial. The martial resides in the center, while the civil operates from start to finish. The celestial revolution never strays from observation and cessation. Within a single day’s twelve hours, wherever intent arrives, practice may commence.

Those who attain the primordial qi and the postnatal qi live as if perpetually intoxicated.

Worldly women, deeply entrenched in habit, crave meat and fish, easily stirred by desire. Witnessing others marry, they harbor resentment; moved by spring, grieved by autumn, they invite weakness and illness. Overindulgence in cold foods exacerbates menstrual stagnation. Further tempted, they ruin both body and reputation, leaving lifelong regret. Let this be a warning: avoid karmic entanglements. Endurance brings peace; repentance brings joy. Intent should cradle fullness; the heart should mirror still water. Emulate the golden man: seal the mouth, conceal the tongue. In movement and stillness, preserve chastity and integrity. Shatter the passions, leap from the sea of desire. The heavenly water within the body is the wellspring of life. Urgently seek the method to refine and transform it into truth. With merit accumulated in the human realm, the spirit ascends to heaven. Cultivators, take heed and strive.

**Section One: Recognizing the Foundation and Purifying the Heart**
To recognize the foundation, first purify the heart. Let no dust cling, no illusions delude. With the heart empty and desires stilled, tranquility arises naturally—clear as a mirror, limpid as water. Once the heart is purified, seek to recognize the foundation.

A woman’s body is fundamentally *kun*: yin on the back, yang on the abdomen. The outer aperture is the breast orifice; the inner cavity is the breast stream. The sixth *chonglou* lies at six and a half divisions, opposite the outer gate of the tenth *chonglou*. Begin seated, legs crossed like a crane’s, knees locked. Secure the lower pass (the spring gate) to consolidate primordial qi. Activate the upper pass (the breast stream) to prevent leakage. The middle pass lies within the navel, one *cun* and three *fen* deep.

To avoid the five leakages, guard the three passes: ears turned inward to listen, eyes turned inward to see, mouth sealed to refrain from speech. Qi is drawn into the breast stream; spirit congeals in the golden chamber; nature settles in the sea of awareness; intent focuses on the elixir palace. Return to oneness through contemplation. The Golden Mother contemplates the heart; Laozi contemplates the aperture. Throughout the twelve hours, observe before emotions arise. The seven passions vanish; the five aggregates are originally empty. The heart remains free, vibrantly alive.

As our master Lü [Dongbin] taught: the source of Dao is in the Jade Clarity. Concentrate spirit in the qi cavity; direct intent from the eyes into the qi cavity. When primordial qi arrives, postnatal qi enters. Maintain this moment by moment.

For women, the upper elixir cavity is the breast stream. Behind the navel and before the kidneys lies the middle pass. The lower pass is the *pinhu* (womb gate); the womb is the great cauldron. All are accessed by guiding from the eyes into the breast stream, the navel, and the womb—one continuous channel. The primordial seed is the root of life.

A man’s primordial essence is the utmost yang qi; a woman’s true blood is the utmost yin essence. These are the treasures of life, the root of all transformations. Men store it in the *mingmen*; women store it in the *pinhu* (the womb). Once stirred, it is hard to retain. Only with a tranquil heart and the refining power of wind and fire can it be preserved.

**Section Two: Cultivating the Menses and Initiating Practice**
At fourteen, a girl’s menses begin, depleting her blood. Though the monthly flow regenerates, it also monthly drains. Those determined to cultivate the menses refine and transform it. Even after menopause, they can restore it. Avoid cold and raw foods to prevent blood stasis.

*(Chen Yingning’s note: This is a conventional belief, but one need not be rigid.)*

The menstrual blood is the root of life. The method of initiation seems active, yet it replenishes blood and qi, preventing further loss. Non-being arises from being; being culminates in non-being. Where effort is applied, postnatal qi flows; where intent is absent, primordial qi abounds. The eyes follow intent; spirit and breath depend on each other. Blood is transmuted into qi; qi is refined to nourish spirit.

Begin at the middle pass. Intent seems to exert force, drawing upward thirty-six times to the upper pass. Rotate thirty-six times on each side, then proceed to the breasts, rotating thirty-six times on each side. If the celestial valley is not warm, qi has not ascended; if the earthly spring is not warm, qi has not descended. Intent guides; the eyes focus on the upper and middle passes.

Cross the hands below the navel and above the spring. Intent seems to exert force, drawing upward thirty-six times to the breast stream, then to the inner cavity of the breast orifice, rotating thirty-six times on each side.

**Section Three: The Dragon-Severing Method**

The Dragon-Severing secret technique combines active and passive practice. At the *zi* (11 p.m.–1 a.m.) and *wu* (11 a.m.–1 p.m.) hours, sit as if straddling a crane. Tap the teeth seventy-two times to activate the *Feishu* (Lung Shu) point, employing postnatal intent. Breathe naturally through the nose thirty-six times, and the meridians throughout the body will open.

Press the heels firmly against the *quanfei* (Spring Gate). Cross the hands below the navel and above the spring. Intent seems to exert force, drawing upward thirty-six times to the upper pass. Rotate the intent and gaze thirty-six times on each side, then proceed to the middle pass, rotating intent and gaze thirty-six times on each side. Raise the hands toward the heavens, slowly thirty-six times, then swiftly thirty-six times. When the *weilu* (coccyx) suddenly stirs, clasp the hands at the waist, clench the jaw tightly, and raise the shoulders straight up. Squeeze the *jiaji* (double passes along the spine) so that the *Feishu* (Lung Shu) points are activated. Intent lifts the head and back straight upward to the *yuzhen* (Jade Pillow), connecting to the *niewan* (Mud Pillow). Press the lower lip tightly over the upper lip, and intent guides the true *qi* upward to the *niewan*, descending near the nostrils.

The tongue rests on the heavenly bridge, and sweet dew flows naturally. With a slight contraction of the nose, swallow the saliva as intent directs it downward to the navel. Place the hands over the *pin* (female gate), and intent seems to exert force, extending to the *zigong* (womb) thirty-six times. The sweet dew enters the cauldron, and warm *qi* spirals within. Press the heels firmly, and body and mind settle as the womb becomes tranquil.

Master Wei Yuanjun said: *"The treasure returns to the Northern Sea—calm and secure."*

---

**Section Four: Refining the Breasts to Restore Youth**

The breasts connect upward to the heart and lungs and descend to the *qi* sea. To refine the breasts to the form of a maiden’s, incorporate the Dragon-Severing method by guiding the sweet dew to the *jiangong* (Crimson Palace). Focus intent on both breasts, rotating thirty-six times on each side. Press the upper and lower lips together, clench the teeth, and close the nostrils, employing internal breathing.

Within the breasts, use the palms to knead each side seventy-two times—first slowly, then swiftly; first lightly, then with greater force. After one hundred days of practice, the breasts will take the shape of walnuts. The Immortal Fengxian’s breast-refining formula states:

*"Left sun, right moon—one yin, one yang.
Nasal breathing circulates the inner *gang*.
To return yin and yang to sun and moon,
Refine both palms with true fire."*

---

**Section Five: Stabilizing the Cauldron and Conceiving the Embryo**

In men, the lower, middle, and upper *dantian* serve as cauldrons. In women, the womb, the area within the navel, and the breast stream serve as cauldrons. The womb lies 1.3 *cun* below the lower *dantian*, 2.8 *cun* from the navel, and beneath the upper pass of the breast stream. The upper breast stream, the middle navel area, and the lower womb form the three positions, arranged from outer to inner, with practice moving from inner to outer. Men lack a womb, so the lower *dantian* serves as the great cauldron—thus the names are the same, but their referents differ.

Master Lü’s *Jinhua Collection* states: *"With both eyes returning light, focus intent evenly between them and direct it to the lower* dantian*."* After practicing the Dragon-Severing method, women should rest in stillness for a moment. Direct intent from between the eyes, returning light to the breast stream thirty-six times, then to the area within the navel, and finally to the lower *dantian* (the womb), thirty-six times each. Guide the water of the *huachi* (Flower Pool) to the upper cauldron, draw the fluids of the heart and lungs to the upper cauldron, and send the true gold from the sea to the upper cauldron. Then, intent seems to exert force, guiding it downward to the middle cauldron, and further to the great cauldron, spiraling eighteen times. Inner heat rises, the cauldron stabilizes, and the embryo congeals.

(Note by Yingning: The function of this passage remains unclear, and its meaning is likewise obscure. Beginners may find it difficult to practice accordingly.)

**Section Six: Self-Regulation of Embryonic Breathing**
To avoid the faults of windy, panting, coarse, or shallow respiration, nasal breathing must be regulated. When each breath returns to its root, embryonic breathing is achieved. As breath moves, the pulse stirs; when breath stills, the pulse halts.

Ancient texts state: *"Ingesting qi does not confer longevity; longevity requires the subjugation of qi."* When true breathing circulates, qi is naturally subdued. After practicing the Dragon-Severing method, rest in stillness for a while. With the seven emotions unarisen and stray thoughts stilled, press the feet against the *quanfei* (Spring Gate), enclose the lips over the teeth, and let intent follow the gaze to the space between heart and kidneys—three *cun* and eight *fen* apart. Rotate left and right for forty-nine breaths. Sweet dew will arise of itself; when swallowed, it is drawn upward, then directed to the navel, where qi congeals. With prolonged practice, embryonic breathing forms: exhalation and inhalation occur spontaneously, as does the upward drawing. Within the *pinhu* (Mystery Gate), opening and closing proceed naturally, warm as spring. The elixir then takes shape.

(Note by Yingning: The phenomena between regulated breathing and embryonic breathing are left unexplained. The claim that the heart and kidneys are three *cun* and eight *fen* apart is also unreliable.)

**Section Seven: Elixir Reversion and Embryo Formation**
For male practitioners, the River Chariot method involves the divine fire stilling the wind. Daily gathering refines the lesser medicine in the furnace. When qi is abundant and spirit whole, the greater medicine forms. The Five Dragons bear the sacred, merging with the natural. From the lower field, it ascends to the middle, augmenting qi and nourishing spirit, then to the upper field. First, it pierces the *dingmen* (Crown Gate). Jade fluid returns as the elixir, *tihu* (divine nectar) bathes the crown, and the yang spirit is refined—this is called immortality.

As for women’s jade fluid returning as the elixir: the Red Dragon transforms into the White Phoenix, filling the lower field as if with embryonic gestation. When practice is complete and qi transforms, the radiance of spirit becomes whole, piercing the Crown Gate. The yang spirit is refined, jade fluid returns as the elixir, and *tihu* bathes the crown. This does not depart from prior practice—one must listen to the subtle and wondrous sounds as if in the Kunlun Palace of the Queen Mother.

(Note by Yingning: The discussion of women’s practice is overly brief and insufficient as a method.)

**Section Eight: Refining and Transforming the Yang Spirit**

For men’s inner elixir: essence is transmuted to augment qi, and qi is refined into spirit. For women’s inner elixir: blood is transmuted to augment qi, and qi is refined into spirit. Both employ fire and wind. In women’s practice, severing the Dragon lies in transforming blood into qi. It is also said: regulate the breath to transform qi into spirit. If qi is not refined, spirit remains insufficient, and form does not coalesce—this yields only yin spirit, not yang spirit. The method begins with entering stillness, applying the Six-Character Formula, and moving intention with the Three-Word Seal. Starting from within the navel, abide in the Central Elixir Field, rotating left and right thirty-six times each while directing intention with the character *lan*. For the Liver Palace in the east, rotate left and right thirty-six times each while directing intention with the character *luo*. For the Heart Palace in the south, rotate left and right thirty-six times each while directing intention with the character *bo*. For the Lung Palace in the west, rotate left and right thirty-six times each while directing intention with the character *dai*. For the Kidney Palace in the north, rotate left and right thirty-six times each while directing intention with the character *tai*. Ascend to the Mud Pill Palace, rotating left and right thirty-six times each, with intention centered. The hun, shen, po, and qi are gathered at the crown, refined and transformed into yang. Yin resides in the great cauldron; stillness guards the embryo. Then, move intention with the Three-Word Seal through the Central Pass nine times. When practice is complete, yin ascends and yang descends, uniting in the Central Cauldron. Radiance fills the Crown Gate, and one becomes like the Queen Mother seated in the Kunlun Palace, listening to the wondrous, stringless music in the void.

**Section Nine: The Yang Spirit’s Radiance Becomes Whole**

When jade fluid returns as the elixir, the yang spirit is not yet pure. When the Red Water obtains the Pearl, the yang spirit’s radiance becomes whole—like the Queen Mother seated in the Kunlun Palace, listening to the wondrous, stringless music in the void. The heart is the Vermilion Bird, soaring through the sky and descending in utmost sincerity. The root of intention returns to its origin; the six roots are liberated, and spirit becomes naturally luminous. The kidneys resemble the *wangxiang*, revolving to obtain the precious pearl, which is offered before one. Radiance envelops the ten directions. When heart and kidneys unite, spirit and qi naturally merge, forming the true seed and nurturing the sacred embryo. The Purple Chamber seals it away, for the liver’s nature is benevolence. The White Parrot dances, for the lung’s disposition is righteousness. Metal and wood intermingle, and nature and disposition harmonize. The tiger is subdued and the dragon descends; water and fire balance. The pure precious vase symbolizes the lung’s fluid; the willow branch symbolizes the liver’s tail. The fluid of the Flowery Pond is like sweet dew. Atop the Mud Pill Palace, one sits steadfast upon Kunlun. The method employs firmness: move intention with the Three-Word Seal into the true breath’s abode—the great cauldron. The millet-like pearl flies and revolves, entering the navel. The mouth seems to chant, *bu bu xi lie*, with undivided focus. In all worlds, concentration and wisdom become perfectly interpenetrating. Though the Southern Sea’s waves surge, when original yang qi is full, the spirit-fire’s radiance becomes whole. The great medicine surges through the passes, yet I remain ever pure and ever still. The heart is settled, intention is clear—profound stillness alone. This great method, this wondrous and true mechanism, surpasses the Dragon-Severing practice in excellence. After nine revolutions, the Seven Returns are achieved. The work returns to the navel, the yang spirit appears at the crown, and precious radiance ascends. Form and spirit are both wondrous; merit and virtue are complete. The Jade Edict descends.

**Section Ten: Nurturing and Facing the Origin**

When the great cauldron is settled, the great medicine obtained, the sacred embryo formed, and the yang spirit manifested, it must still be nurtured—nursed for three years, faced in wall-sitting for nine. The breath is continuous, intention undivided. Spirit and breath attend each other. For three thousand days, guard it as one would a newborn child, never forgetting this for even a moment. No need for distraction: the two eyes lower their lids, light following intention inward. The deeper the stillness, the more profound the entry. Qi is warm as spring; sweet dew arises frequently. Qi circulates throughout the body, beginning in the Palace of Childbirth, then ascending and descending. The River Chariot turns of itself, transforming the mortal frame into my true form. In men’s Facing the Origin, white light pierces the crown, followed by black, then blue, then red, then gold. In women’s Facing the Origin, black light pierces the crown, followed by red, then white, then blue, then gold. When practice is complete and radiance is whole, the five lights merge into one. The earthly thunder rumbles of itself; the Heavenly Gate opens of itself. When the yang spirit emerges, it emerges and returns—first near, then far. Do not become deluded. At this juncture, one must be even more cautious.

**Section Eleven: Merit Complete, Transcending the Mortal**

When the yang spirit comes and goes freely and the true self roams at will, one may remain in the mortal realm to broadly establish merit and virtue. When virtue is deep and conditions mature, a true teacher will come to guide one. One is led to audience with the Supreme Emperor, then to pay homage to the various heavens, and finally to the Jasper Pool to present oneself before the Golden Mother. One is appointed as an immortal—this is transcending the mortal.

**Appendix:**
1. First, treat channel illnesses.

For ailments before and after childbirth, menstrual blockages, and resulting illnesses, apply the method of rubbing the waist thirty-six times, alternating left and right. For the shoulders, perform thirty-six upward and downward motions on each side, alternating left and right. Additionally, massage the navel and center, crossing the hands to rub one hundred forty-four times each until internal heat arises and ceases.

For flooding and spotting, add the "Inverted Tiger" technique to the previous methods: suspend a horizontal beam in the air, hang upside down by both feet like a golden hook, and press the fingers into the ground. Focus the mind below the navel, rotating left and right one hundred twenty times. Perform this daily at midnight and noon to also treat menstrual blockages, blood stasis, and blood accumulations.

To the previous methods, add the "Sequential Hook of the Golden Turtle": suspend a horizontal beam in the air, clasp the palms and hang downward, toes touching the ground. Lower the eyelids like a curtain, bow the head to observe the heart, and perform thirty-six repetitions. Let the mind follow the gaze to six-tenths below the navel for thirty-six repetitions, then direct the gaze to the afflicted area for another thirty-six. For all such ailments, apply these principles accordingly.

The secret use of the mind’s true fire to treat illness is the esoteric healing method of Immortal Wei Yuanjun, Cui Fengsun, and the "Hemp Ball, Fish, Glare, and Turtle" technique.

**Two: Restoring the Menstrual Flow After Cessation**
When the monthly flow has ceased, first restore it. Within the "Dragon-Sealing Method," direct the intention upward, then shift to outward projection. Rotate left and right, then change to rubbing motions. After one hundred days, the menses will return. Three days thereafter, resume the previous method. After one hundred days of practice, the flow will cease permanently.

**Four Principles of Female Practice**
*Inscription of the True Character*

**Inscription of Stillness**

At birth, humans embody stillness, the undifferentiated Great Ultimate. Mind, destiny, nature, and emotions are as yet undivided. Later, the postnatal takes precedence, and principle and desire stand side by side. When desire overcomes principle, peril follows; when principle overcomes desire, desire wanes. Eliminate desire to preserve principle, and the spirit-terrace remains pure. The sages’ method of the heart is to cleanse the mind and embrace tranquility. Like polishing a mirror to remove grime, like facing a wall in meditation, the five aggregates dissolve into emptiness, and the ten thousand conditions settle into stillness. Without seeing, without hearing, the true nature sprouts. Cultivate this embryo, and the study of longevity begins. Women, in particular, align with stillness and contraction. Abiding in stillness and preserving sincerity, they stand alongside immortals and buddhas.

**Inscription of Purity**

Sages, worthies, immortals, and buddhas—all maintain perfect sincerity from beginning to end. The Dao of Heaven flows unimpeded. The thoughts of ordinary people are杂 and impure; even if they briefly cease, the supreme Dao does not coalesce. As the sun and moon shine long, as the four seasons endure, so too must the cultivation of the Dao and nurturing of nature persist without end. In haste or turmoil, not a moment departs from benevolence. Unceasing and enduring, sever the seven emotions. Through deep familiarity, the marvelous arises; radiance and brilliance follow. The slightest lapse, and the study cannot succeed. Only through unwavering purity is the heart of the Dao preserved. Women of affinity, let none shame their lives.

**Inscription of Oneness**

The Dao is not distant from humanity; humanity distances itself from the Dao. With a virtue divided, no success is possible. All things are thus—how much more so the mysterious and wondrous? Focus on one without distraction, and grasp the essential. Do not stray into side paths, do not enter heterodox teachings. The non-dual Dharma gate reveals its secrets. The Great Void is undifferentiated, empty yet with subtle signs. Firmly guard the inch of the heart, silently observe the mysteries of the elixir. Women, do not abandon or neglect yourselves. Within, nature and destiny; without, integrity and conduct. With one heart and one virtue, you will attain profound mastery. The fruit of the Dao will be perfectly luminous, and the ranks of immortality may be reached.

**Compendium of Elixir Secrets**

*The Awakening Path of Kun* states: Before cultivating this Dao, first uphold the five precepts.
1. Do not kill—this is benevolence.
2. Do not steal—this is righteousness.
3. Do not engage in illicit sex—this is propriety.
4. Do not consume alcohol or meat—this is wisdom.
5. Do not speak falsely—this is trustworthiness.

Having upheld the five precepts, next eliminate the six desires: the eyes do not gaze wantonly, the ears do not listen wantonly, the nose does not smell wantonly, the tongue does not speak wantonly, the body does not move wantonly. With the six desires eliminated, how can the seven emotions—joy, anger, sorrow, fear, love, aversion, and desire—remain? Once the seven emotions are gone, then enter the chamber and begin practice.

*The Scripture of Kun’s Peace* says: "Without true refining of the self, all efforts are difficult to commence." It also says: "First cut off desire and forget emotions, then enter the chamber to sit in meditation. The refining of the self is the same as for men; regulate the breath so it is continuous and unbroken." It further states: "The four great elements of the body converge at the spirit-terrace of the Central Palace. The two qi intermingle, the Yellow Court responds to the Mysterious, and the five phases generate one another—only Earth is complete."

It also says: "A trace of dawn’s moon appears in the eastern sky, seeking the origin of the unborn body." This is like building a house, where opening the entrance comes first; it is like firing a furnace, where kindling the flame is the method.

*The Discernment of Cultivating the Dao* states: "For men, the essential practice is refining qi, called ‘Yang Refining Qi.’ When qi is refined and returns, the White Tiger descends, transforming into a youthful body. Then the postnatal essence does not leak, longevity is possible, and the elixir may be formed. For women, the essential practice is refining form, called ‘Yin Refining Form.’ When form is refined and vanishes, the Red Dragon is severed, transforming into a male body. Then the impure yin blood no longer descends, transcending death and entering life. Thereafter, cultivate using the men’s method, and the great elixir may be attained in a year." Yet there are also secrets, timings, and methods.

*The Three Lives Mirror of the Sacred Medicine* says: "The human navel is called the ‘Gate of Destiny.’ Above it is the Primordial Pass, within it is the Yellow Court, and below it is the Sea of Qi."

Lazy Daoist says: "Women have three destinies: upper, middle, and lower. The upper is the Yang Cavity, the middle is the Yellow Chamber, and the lower is the Cinnabar Field. In youth, begin with the lower; in decline, proceed from the middle; only when accomplished, turn to the upper."

*The Discernment of Cultivating the Dao* says: "A man’s destiny lies in the Cinnabar Field; a woman’s destiny lies in the breasts." The breasts are the source of blood, located one inch and two fen within the center—not the two breasts. Women take blood as their kidneys, which is an empty cavity. The blood source generates blood, the Cinnabar Field generates the elixir. The practice occurs at the zi and wu hours: focus the mind on the empty cavity of the breasts, breathe continuously, exhaling less and inhaling more. When the monthly signal arrives, guide it from the Cinnabar Field upward to the breasts. Some say that when the signal arrives, it is like the living zi hour for men. This is what *The Scripture of Kun’s Peace* calls: "At dawn’s sunrise, a trace of light appears. Circulate mercury to match lead, and both spirit and qi abide." Accumulating qi originates from the land of generative qi; storing spirit is the path of refining spirit. When the Yang stirs, practice the work of zi, wu, mao, and you. When the hundred vessels are open, stabilize the positions of Qian, Kun, Kan, and Li.

However, the monthly signal is not the arrival of the menses. *The Three Lives Mirror* says: "It is like a person away from home whose letter arrives first."

When the signal arrives, she will know it herself. Sometimes there is pain in the waist and legs, or discomfort in the head and eyes, with no desire for food—this is the signal arriving, about to transform into blood, and it is *qi*. She should focus her efforts two and a half days *before* this. If the menses flow, the Red Dragon’s yin essence cannot be controlled; reckless circulation will harm many, so she must wait two and a half days after the menses end. Test with white silk: if it turns golden yellow, this is the sign that the menses have ceased. Then proceed as before, circulating upward to sever it. After several months, the menses will turn yellow, yellow will turn white, and white will vanish entirely—this is the Dao of returning from existence to non-existence. If she is past forty-nine and her waist is dry with blood exhausted, there is no life left, but with prolonged nurturing, blood and primal essence will regenerate, and she will resemble a maiden once more—this is the marvel of generating existence from non-existence. When she sees it present, sever it at once, and life will be renewed.

The Lazy Daoist also said: "With long practice of inward reflection and breath regulation, true breathing naturally arises, opening and closing. Nurturing the *yinqie* (yin barrier), spirit and *qi* become abundant, true Yang flourishes, the menstrual flow ceases, and the breasts shrink like a man’s—this is called severing the Red Dragon." After this, the seven-day great return and great cycle proceed without distinction between men and women.

**Discerning the Living Zi Hour**
Heaven and Earth generate beings through *yinyun* (intermingling) and joyful nurturance—this is true for all things, so how are men and women different? This is the natural principle of creation, the Dao of non-thought and non-action. Moreover, the *Dan Jing* (Alchemical Scriptures) clearly state: "For women, blood serves as the kidneys." The *Inner Canon* also says: "At eight, a boy’s kidney *qi* is full, his hair grows and teeth change; at seven, a girl’s kidney *qi* flourishes, her teeth change and hair grows." Clearly, both men and women have kidneys—why would their *zi* hours differ?

Further, examining texts on conception: Inside a woman’s yin is a lotus-bud shape called the "uterus." Each month, after the menses, regardless of the day, there is a time of *yinyun* and joyful nurturance—*qi* steams and grows hot, she feels drowsy and stifled, subtle movement stirs in her meridians, and the lotus bud shows a desire to open. At this moment, life’s vitality surges. If used in accord, it can conceive a child; here, it is used in reversal. How can there be doubt about the living *zi* hour? Yet without a pure body and mind, it is difficult to perceive and comprehend—this depends on the practitioner’s spiritual insight.

**On the Living Zi Hour in Women’s Alchemy**
The living *zi* hour for men is recorded in alchemical scriptures, but for women, the ancients did not speak of it. However, the *Yi Jing* says: "Heaven and Earth intermingle, and the myriad things transform into harmony; male and female unite their essences, and the myriad things come to life." The *Book of Rites* states: "Food and sex are humanity’s greatest desires." Generally, the movements and stillness of Qian and Kun depend entirely on the mechanism of opening and closing—there is no difference between the two. Observing animals: sows, cows, and ewes, when in their time of *yinyun* and joyful nurturance, invariably cry out loudly, compelled by the moment. Heaven generates beings, and humans are the most intelligent—surely they too have this moment. The living *zi* hour arrives, but humans, more refined than animals, endure it in silence.

The people may be made to follow it (procreation), which is the natural course, but not to know it (reversal), which is the alchemical path. Practitioners observe the waxing and waning of the moon, reflect inward to cultivate virtue, and stabilize their practice in stillness. Gathering primordial true *qi* and preventing its transformation into blood—this is the moment to begin severing the Red Dragon.

**Distinguishing Differences in Men’s and Women’s Alchemy**

**Editorial Principles of *A Compendium of Women’s Daoist Learning***
1. Select ancient and modern exemplary conduct and wise sayings, along with concise writings from women, to cultivate lofty character and instill exceptional intelligence—this pertains to the psychological aspect.
2. Carefully choose methods of cultivation, scriptures, and poetry from women throughout history to foster extraordinary talent in women and develop robust, graceful physiques—this pertains to the physiological aspect.
3. Daoist learning is the quintessence of the Chinese nation, unique to our country and absent in others. Previously, due to limited women’s education, this transcendent knowledge could not be studied. Now, following the principle of gender equality, this learning is gradually being made public.
4. Ancient writings vary in depth; some are profoundly abstruse and difficult to understand, while others are overly vulgar and unrefined. To ensure accessibility, abstruse texts are annotated for clarity, and vulgar ones are slightly refined to avoid offending refined sensibilities.
5. The purpose of this compilation is to promote China’s indigenous Daoist learning while absolutely rejecting superstition. Any text tainted with superstition is excluded.

**Reader’s Note**
This book was written in the *guimao* year of the Guangxu reign, eight years before the founding of the Republic.

2. The author was a woman who remained unmarried all her life, devotedly serving her mother with filial piety. Her mother observed widow’s chastity, and the daughter preserved her maidenly purity. Both mother and daughter were devoted to the Dao, yet lacking a teacher, they could only search through various Daoist texts for oral instructions. At her mother’s behest, the author compiled this book, which consists entirely of excerpts from other alchemical classics rather than her own compositions.

3. The excerpted texts vary in quality; some are sound, while others are not. Thus, their theories occasionally contradict one another, and their prose is often verbose. Though some revisions have been made, the original intent has been preserved as much as possible. Scholars should use their own discernment when studying these passages.

4. Terms in this book such as "Ancient Perfumed Mother," "Supreme Emperor of the Dark Heavens," "Golden Portal Emperor Lord," "Queen Mother of the Jasper Pool," and "Luminous Dao Matriarch" are all borrowed names from other texts. In this age of dispelling superstition, such appellations ought not to be used, yet they remain unchanged here as they appear in the original sources.

5. The book states that a woman’s alchemical attainment requires awaiting deliverance, a theory that is far from satisfactory. This stems from the old custom of valuing men over women. Most religious systems worldwide have historically denied gender equality—not just in China. Only through the emergence of exceptional women can such conventions be broken.

6. In one passage attributed to the Golden Portal Emperor Lord, he argues: *"Some claim that without severing the Red Dragon, the elixir cannot form and the Dao cannot be realized. Yet if the blood is exhausted, so too is the qi. Just as a man’s essence decays and his elixir becomes difficult to refine, the principle is the same. For men, essence, and for women, blood, must not be entirely cut off. Qi arises from blood, and when blood transforms into qi, essence flows freely. If blood must be drained to refine the elixir, why do young women with blood depletion fall ill instead? This is clear evidence that blood cannot be forsaken."*

Now, to clarify: "Severing the Red Dragon" refers to the practice of refining and halting menstruation through cultivation, not to blood depletion in women. To equate severing the Red Dragon with blood cessation, exhaustion, or desiccation would be to mistake it for the pathology of consumptive blood stasis. If a woman truly suffered from such a condition, she would require special methods—both meditative and medicinal—to restore her menstrual cycle to its natural, healthy rhythm before gradually refining and halting it according to the oral instructions for severing the Dragon. This gentleman’s conflation of the effects of severing the Red Dragon with consumptive blood stasis is a grave error.

7. The differences in initial methods of cultivation for men and women arise from physiological distinctions. If a woman wishes to enter the Dao, she must first acquire a solid understanding of basic medical knowledge before undertaking practice. Otherwise, she risks following the wrong path. Among those who study immortality, none have succeeded without also studying medicine. This is a concrete principle, not mere abstract theory or lofty discourse on nature and mind.

8. Regardless of gender, those who lack the capacity to conceive mortal offspring will never achieve the formation of an immortal embryo. The principles of human birth and immortal transformation are fundamentally the same, differing only in whether one follows or reverses the natural course. Severing the Red Dragon is a reversal of creation’s flow. If one mistakenly believes that the cessation of menstruation alone leads to immortality, then women over fifty, whose menses naturally cease, would all possess the qualifications of immortals. If one argues that the elderly are an exception, what of modern young women who undergo surgical removal of the uterus or ovaries, causing their menstruation to cease naturally? Can this be considered severing the Red Dragon? Such matters demand careful scrutiny.

October, the twenty-fourth year of the Republic of China, the four thousand six hundred and thirty-second year since the Yellow Emperor.

Respectfully inscribed by Chen Yingning of Wanjiang

**Preface**

Ze Huan lost her father in youth, leaving her mother to uphold chastity without an heir, with only we three sisters beneath her care. Soon after, my second sister passed away, and my third sister was betrothed, awaiting marriage. Unwilling to bear my mother’s lonely widowhood, Ze Huan vowed to remain chaste and serve her, swearing never to marry. At the age of twelve, I began to observe vegetarian precepts alongside my mother, entertaining ourselves with the *Exhortations to Virtue* and its verses. I often admired the accounts of cultivation’s beauty and the nobility of immortals and buddhas in devotional texts, yet lamented the absence of an enlightened master to guide me in the secrets, nor any alchemical scriptures to verify my mind and body. Silently, I sought heavenly affinity for nearly a decade.

Then, in the summer of Gengzi during the upheaval in the capital, I accompanied my mother to seek refuge on Mount E, where I first learned of Buddhist texts on female cultivation: the *Sutra of Lady Moye*, the *Sutra of Matanga’s Daughter*, the *Sutra of the Daughter of Anathapindika*, the *Biographies of Bhikkhunis*, and the *Biographies of Virtuous Women*—a mere drop from the vast ocean. Later, I obtained the *Mani Candles for the Earthly Realm*, a collection of over seventy works compiled by Lady Rushan, a laywoman named Shanyi. However, the Buddhist canon is profound, emphasizing nature over destiny, and is not readily accessible to beginners.

As for Daoist texts on female elixir cultivation, they are often appended within the *Daoist Canon*, lacking order or dedicated volumes, like an endless sea—overwhelming and disorienting. Undeterred by my own inadequacy, I excerpted and compiled passages on female elixir cultivation, amassing over a hundred pages. I shared these with my mother to dispel her solitude and encourage our quiet practice. Beyond our filial joy, at my mother’s behest, I extracted the distinctions between male and female cultivation from my collection, transcribing them into a separate volume of over five thousand characters. Entitled *On the Distinctions Between Male and Female Elixir Work*, I placed it by my side to prevent confusion in practice, lest one incur strange illnesses or be ridiculed for superficial understanding. If such errors are inevitable, how could I dare presume to share this with fellow seekers?

Recorded in the spring of the year *Gui Mao* in the Guangxu reign by Yan Zehuan, the Bamboo Grove Historian.

**On the Distinctions Between Male and Female Elixir Work**
Compiled and Narrated by Yan Zehuan, the Bamboo Grove Historian
Collated by He Weilie, the Immortal Well Historian
Revised and Edited by Chen Yingning of Wanjiang

Sun Yuanjun’s *Commentary on the Kun Formula* states:
