Among the *Jishantang Poems*, works such as *The Wondrous Method of Scent Observation*, *The Method of Invoking the Heavenly Worthy*, and *The Six-Character Scripture Method* serve as metaphors for Immortal Learning, offering introductory practices. This is not to suggest that Daoist cultivation ends here, nor that no further progress lies beyond. Readers must not dismiss them as commonplace. Ordinary women, lacking in learning, may struggle with abstruse principles; thus, they are guided by what they already understand. Those of higher knowledge, of course, have no need for such instruction.

7. The supplementary *Twenty-Four Oral Instructions on Female Alchemy by Zhenyizi* were not part of the original compilation. I have selected them from another Daoist text and included them here, amending one hundred and ten characters in the process. They hold considerable value for study—readers are urged not to overlook them.

Written in December of the twenty-fourth year of the Republic of China, the four thousand six hundred and thirty-second year since the Yellow Emperor.
By Chen Yingning of Wanjiang, as preface.

**Preface to the *Female Alchemy Poetry Collection***
*Former Section* – *Brief*
*Latter Section* – Compiled by Jishantang of Qianzhong
Edited and Annotated by Chen Yingning of Wanjiang

**1. Cleansing the Heart and Curbing Desires**
The ground of male and female elixir differs,
Yet the principle of yin and yang is one and the same.
Cleansing the heart and curbing desires form the root—
To lay the foundation, first sever the Red Dragon.

The ground of male and female elixir differs:
The initial work for men and women is not the same.
Yet the principle of yin and yang is one and the same:
Both must refine themselves into pure yang—truly, the principle is identical.
Cleansing the heart and curbing desires form the root—
To lay the foundation, first sever the Red Dragon.
*Red Dragon*: the monthly flow.
When, through refinement, the monthly flow ceases and the menses no longer rise,
The two breasts naturally shrink like a man’s retracted turtle—
Only then is the elixir’s foundation complete.

**2. Blood Transforms into Qi**
Born in stillness, seek within stillness,
Steam and nourish the broken vessel with singular devotion.
When blood transforms into qi and the tide of menses ceases,
The primordial unity is restored, and one ascends Penglai.

Born in stillness, seek within stillness:
Women are born with a nature inherently still—
Refining the elixir within stillness, success comes swifter than for men.
Steam and nourish the broken vessel with singular devotion—
When blood transforms into qi and the tide of menses ceases,
Women, abundant in blood, employ the method to transmute it entirely into qi,
And the monthly flow may be extinguished.
The primordial unity is restored, and one ascends Penglai:
Returning to the original nature, one may attain immortality and the Dao.

**3. Nurturing the Yellow Sprout**
When the passions bloom like a split melon,
Rely wholly on the virtue of earth to grow the yellow sprout.
Morning and night, diligently nurture it—
Naturally, one obtains the flower of ageless life.

When the passions bloom like a split melon:
When the water of heavenly gui arrives, it is like a melon splitting open.
Rely wholly on the virtue of earth to grow the yellow sprout:
The sprout arises within earth, hence it is called the *yellow sprout*.
Morning and night, diligently nurture it—
Naturally, one obtains the flower of ageless life:
From the yellow sprout, diligently nurture it without harm,
And it will gradually blossom—
This is the foundation for transcending kalpas and attaining longevity.

**4. The Wondrous Fragrance Observation Method**
Within the body lies a White Crane Temple—
Learn the wondrous method of observing fragrance to refine it.
When the work is complete, ascend to the Jasper Pool,
And all shall together attend the Peach Banquet.

Within the body lies a White Crane Temple:
This refers to the breasts—
Transform red into white, hence likened to the White Crane Temple.
Learn the wondrous method of observing fragrance to refine it:
Long ago, the Immortal Maiden of Fragrance Observation refined her method within the White Crane Temple,
And ultimately attained the great Dao.
When the work is complete, ascend to the Jasper Pool—
All shall together attend the Peach Banquet:
A hope that all may cross to the other shore—
Such is the universal compassion of the ferryman’s heart.

**5. The Heavenly Worthy’s Secret Intent**
Women, swiftly distance yourselves from worldly affairs,
For the Heavenly Worthy of Salvation suffers in mind.
Day and night, sit and lie with the Yellow Dame—
The mortal frame will shed, and immortal bones take its place.

Women, swiftly distance yourselves from worldly affairs—
The Heavenly Worthy of Salvation suffers in mind:
Constantly reciting the four-character scripture is the method to tether the heart.
Day and night, sit and lie with the Yellow Dame:
Guard the true intent at all times—
Thus, the work may swiftly be accomplished.
The mortal frame will shed, and immortal bones take its place:
With such benefits, how can one not cultivate?

**6. The Mysterious Awakening of Life and Death**
To learn death before dying is never to die;
To kill life when encountering birth is never to be born.
Neither death nor birth—truly entering the wondrous—
The mysterious awakening is realized, and the great work complete.

To learn death before dying is never to die:
Though not yet dead, one is like a dead person—
Thus, one ultimately does not die.
To kill life when encountering birth is never to be born:
When the deluded mind arises, sever it with the sword of wisdom—
Thus, one ultimately does not give birth to it.
Neither death nor birth—truly entering the wondrous—
The mysterious awakening is realized, and the great work complete:
The body does not die, the mind does not arise—
One may realize the wondrous fruit of mysterious awakening.

**7. Turning the Light Around and Reflecting**
Turn the light around and reflect between the two breasts,
Focus the spirit before the golden lock.
After two and a half days, yellow transforms to white—
Shift the cauldron and change the furnace to refine into immortality.

Turn the light around and reflect between the two breasts—
Focus the spirit before the golden lock:
Gaze between the two breasts, concentrate the spirit below the two kidneys—
Naturally, the river chariot will ascend to the central field to mend the broken body.
After two and a half days, yellow transforms to white:
After this period of practice, blood transforms into yellow.
At this time, purify the heart and apply effort—
Soon, it will turn white, the red vessels severed,
And the body will resemble that of a maiden.
Shift the cauldron and change the furnace to refine into immortality:
The Red Dragon already severed, the ground of practice differs—
With the proper method, refinement may lead to attainment.

**8. Compassion as the Root**
Compassion as the root, harmonious in nature and temperament,
Endure humiliation, swallow bitterness, and bear hardship.
Every person possesses the Kalpa Tree—
Sit long beneath the Kalpa Tree to ascend the Great Web.

Compassion as the root, harmonious in nature and temperament—
Endure humiliation, swallow bitterness, and bear hardship:
Whether laywomen or Daoist nuns of the mysterious stream,
All may cultivate—
But the root must be compassion.
Every person possesses the Kalpa Tree—
Sit long beneath the Kalpa Tree to ascend the Great Web:
Knowing where the Kalpa Tree resides,
And applying effort upon it,
One will surely attain the heavenly treasure.
*Note*: The first two lines of this poem originally read:
*"Compassion as the root, the heart is the matriarch—*
*At home or in retreat, nurture great harmony."*
They have now been amended.

**9. Employing Medicine and Fire in Dual Use**

**9. Employing Medicine and Fire in Dual Use**

The medicine refines within the fire,
The fire manifests within the medicine.
With fire but no medicine, one boils an empty pot;
With medicine but no fire, all eventually scatters.
When fire and medicine harmonize,
The Golden Elixir coalesces, and one enters the Jasper Garden.

The medicine refines within the fire—
The medicine is *qi*,
That is, spirit guiding *qi*.
The fire manifests within the medicine—
Spirit grows ever more numinous through *qi*.
With fire but no medicine, one boils an empty pot—
One must not play with fire!
With medicine but no fire, all eventually scatters—
One must not lack fire.
When fire and medicine harmonize,
The Golden Elixir coalesces, and one enters the Jasper Garden.
Spirit and *qi* interdependent—
How could it not succeed?

**10. Gathering Form in Great Yin**

Secluded, serene, and steadfast—nurturing nature and temperament,
A woman’s way is perfected, her virtue no light matter.
Ever mindful of the breasts and Sea of Blood,
Gather the form to unite with Great Yin.

Secluded, serene, and steadfast—nurturing nature and temperament,
A woman’s way is perfected, her virtue no light matter.
The first line nurtures nature; the second cultivates virtue—
This is the work of inner and outer refinement.
Ever mindful of the breasts and Sea of Blood—
The initial practice: gather the form to unite with Great Yin.
The method of refining form in Great Yin
Shrinks the breasts like a man’s.

**11. The Six-Character Scripture**

Best of all is the Six-Character Scripture,
From front to back, dwelling in the heart.
Within it lies the hidden River Chariot method—
Unknowing, unseeing, one refines into truth.

Best of all is the Six-Character Scripture

**18. The Root of Heart-Nature**

The Four Great Sacred Mountains teem with female immortals—
Some through filial piety, some through chastity, some through profound meditation.
Yet all rely on heart-nature as their root;
When conduct is complete and merit perfected, they ascend to heaven.

The Four Great Sacred Mountains teem with female immortals—
Half by devotion, half by discipline, half by mystical inquiry.
Though their paths differ, their destination is the same.
All rely on heart-nature as their root;
When conduct is complete and merit perfected, they ascend to heaven.

The twin characters "heart-nature" are the foundation of elixir refinement—
Neither man nor woman can do without them.
This verse concludes the *Female Alchemy Canon*.

---

**Supplement to the *Collected Poems on Female Alchemy***
**Oral Instructions on Female Alchemy by Zhenyi Zi**
**Collated and Revised by Chen Yingning of Wanjian**

**1. Gathering the Mind**
The principles of the Golden Elixir run most profound;
Seek each stage’s work with careful intent.
If you are but entering the gate and beginning practice,
Sweep away delusive thoughts to gather the mind.

**2. Nurturing Nature**
A seed of dark jade, once clear as crystal,
How could dust and grime obscure its brilliance?
But if you sit in stillness and turn the light inward,
The heart of heaven’s moon shines bright again by night.

**3. Cultivating Qi**
Though holding the thought may open the mystery,
When breath reaches harmony, it returns to the natural.
To cultivate qi, there is no other art—
Walk together, sit together, sleep together in accord.

**4. Congealing Spirit**
Spirit is the husband, breath the wife;
Do not let them part on divergent paths, sundered like cloud and mud.
When the two unite in the root-cavern,
The elixir is complete, and the crane arrives.

**5. The Three Destinies**
Light divides into yellow, white, and purple—three in all,
For a woman’s destiny is not like a man’s.
Youth in the upper, decline in the middle, fulfillment in the lower—
Master this single path through the crucial pass.

**6. The Qi Cavern**
The qi cavern is clearly the breasts;
Do not mistakenly guess below the navel.
If you do not recognize where yin arises in elixir refinement,
How can you tame the tiger and subdue the dragon?

**7. Knowing the Time**
Each time the flower blooms beneath the moon,
The ram is about to butt against the fence.
I urge you: when the moment comes, do not delay—
Lest the dragon’s form emerge from the water’s edge.

**8. Slaying the Dragon**
When yang stirs and yin emerges from the jade ravine,
Drive the fire-wheel without pause.
Let the *xun*-wind blow upward to the Crimson Palace;
Reverse the river chariot, relying on the counterflow.

**9. Concealing Form**
The ordinary body flows with monthly blood,
And by seventy, the signs of age appear.
But when you refine to conceal form in Great Yin,
From then on, the immortal body rejoices in long life.

**10. Seeking the Elixir**
Refining form into qi is the work of laying the foundation—
Not the same as the highest-grade celestial immortals.
If you ask where the Golden Elixir truly lies,
It is the sun shining on the moon, illuminating the primordial chaos.

**11. Refining the Self**
The living dragon and tiger battle in the lotus chamber;
Most feared is the heart-monkey and mind-horse running wild.
If refining the self has not reached pure mastery,
How can you cross Chen Cang in peace?

**12. Sequence and Reversal**
Following the sequence, one becomes human; reversing it, one becomes immortal—
The union of *qian* and *kun* is the true teaching.
Do not be surprised if the elixir is hard to congeal at the furnace;
When you reverse the ram’s chariot, heaven will appear of itself.

**13. The Elixir’s Birth**
In dim obscurity, as if entranced,
When fusion and harmony arrive, it is the moment the medicine is born.
The cinnabar field gives its sign, the opportunity arises—
Prepare your work to gather the jade mushroom.

**14. Gathering the Medicine**
Suddenly beholding the primordial single grain of elixir,
Its radiance blazes like a golden pellet.
If the *xun*-wind does not frequently urge the drum,
How can the great medicine pass through the barrier?

**15. Ascending the Origin**
The sun rises over Fusang in the eastern sea;
The fire-wheel flies across—do not pause in your work.
The deer cart carries it to the summit of Kunlun,
Where the wood-mercury naturally returns to the spirit chamber.

**16. Uniting the Elixir**
The *gen*-boy first returns to the chaos nest,
Where husband and wife henceforth weave their silken bonds.
Seal the six gates tightly and diligently add fire—
Within the curtains, the springtime harmony must be supreme.

**17. Fire Timing**
Though six hundred chapters on fire timing have been handed down,
The true timing has never been inscribed on phoenix paper.
Nothing is clearer than the words of *Chongxu*:
When inhalation and exhalation are distinct, immortality is attained.

**18. Warm Nurturing**
Already you see white snow sown in green sand;
Regulate cold and warmth—take care not to err.
When the thirty-six palaces are full of spring’s intent,
Naturally, a path opens for the immortal raft.

**19. Fetal Breathing**
Let your work be fine and close, not coarse or careless;
Spirit and breath, continuous as the Great Void.
If you ask what nurturing the fetus resembles—
It is as if returning to the time before father and mother were born.

**20. The Count**
Gathering the medicine and firing the elixir follow an order—
*Kan* and *li*, *gen* and *xun* are inverted and reversed.
When the work completes the ninety-nine revolutions of the celestial cycle,
Only then have you become a transcendent beyond the world.

**21. Shedding the Fetus**
After ten months, the fetus is round and the count complete,
The yang spirit suddenly wanders to the fontanel.
With a thunderous crack, it bursts forth into the sky—
Above the crown, all see the white qi floating.

**22. Nursing**
The newly born infant’s qi is not yet pure;
Still, it swallows wood-mercury to restore primordial truth.
After nursing for three years,
Its transformations become wondrously numinous.

**23. Facing the Wall**
Though the elixir work is complete, there is still labor to be done—
Sit in silent emptiness within the cave-heaven.
Forgetting form, enter samadhi without reckoning years;
Shatter the void to witness the sacred work.

**24. Ascension**
When you refine to true emptiness, the Dao grows ever higher;
The elixir scripture’s decree summons you to tread the clouds.
From now on, you dwell forever in the Jasper Pool gardens,
Following the spirit consorts to the early court.

**Yingning’s Note:**
These twenty-four poems on oral instructions for female alchemy,
Comprising six hundred seventy-two characters,
Have now been meticulously collated and corrected in one hundred ten characters,
Improving upon the original. Thus, they are printed here.
Recorded in the mid-winter of the *yihai* year.

**Songs of the Dao’s Subtle Source: Female Immortal Practice**
*(From the *Daoist External Canon*, Volume on Daoist Texts)*

For female immortality practice, one must first dispel illness and regulate the monthly flow to precision. Only then may one refine the self and sever the Red Dragon—its principle identical to a man’s subjugation of the White Tiger. Men possess a body of pure Yang, round and complete; their Yang essence may daily grow or discharge, and through this growth and discharge they replenish and perfect the firmness of Qian. Yet only a man of resolute will, one who has mastered the work of subduing the tiger, may achieve this. Women possess a body of pure Yin; their celestial water flows once each month. Thus, their initial practice aligns with that of men.

After severing the Red Dragon, a woman’s practice follows the same principle as a man’s: beginning with the Small Celestial Cycle, progressing through spirit emergence and returning to emptiness—all remains identical. Yet many women suffer irregular monthly flows, for their Conception and Girdle Vessels harbor stagnant blood from excess or deficiency. First, one must employ herbal medicine to treat these tangible ailments.

Begin with a single dose of *Tongqiao Huoxue Decoction*, composed of:
- Five *li* of true musk (infused),
- Three *qian* of safflower,
- Three *qian* of peach kernel paste,
- One *qian* of red peony leaf,
- Two *qian* of Sichuan lovage,
- Three *qian* of ginger,
- Three stalks of scallion,
- Seven red dates.

Crush these three ingredients, then decoct with half a *jin* of yellow wine until reduced to half a cup. Strain, add the musk, and decoct thrice more before consumption. This ensures all blood pathways throughout the body are unobstructed, and it also treats consumptive ailments.

Next, take the *Modified Four Agents Decoction* to harmonize qi and blood, ensuring neither excess nor deficiency, until the monthly flow arrives with a fresh, bright red hue and precise timing. Only then may one refine the self. If the monthly flow remains irregular, one dare not sever the Red Dragon—this is the immutable principle.

The *Four Agents Decoction* consists of:
- Three *qian* of tangkuei root,
- Two *qian* of white peony,
- Two *qian* of Sichuan lovage,
- Three *qian* of raw rehmannia,
- Two *qian* of ginseng,
- Two *qian* of white atractylodes,
- Two *qian* of bupleurum,
- Three *qian* of poria,
- Two *qian* of pinellia,
- Three *qian* of cyperus,
- One *qian* and five *fen* of honey-fried licorice,
- Three slices of ginger.

For qi deficiency, add five *qian* of astragalus. After two or three doses, qi and blood will be abundant, and one may proceed to sever the Red Dragon. Seek a master’s guidance without delay to refine the self and cultivate the true, transforming the Kun body to the firmness of Qian.

Women, being of pure Yin, base their practice upon the menstrual flow. Blood belongs to the Lesser Yin meridians, coursing alongside the Girdle and Conception Vessels in ceaseless circulation. It is the sea from which celestial water descends and ebbs, the primary channel through which the flow perpetually courses. Yet each month, a woman receives one *sheng* and three *ge* of this celestial water, and as it flows, so too do her meridians.

From childhood, a girl has no menstrual flow. Only at fourteen, when she awakens to the desires of union between man and woman, does passion stir, her body grow warm, and her qi pathways open—until celestial water surges forth. To cultivate the Way of longevity, one must seclude herself in a quiet chamber, sever all contact with men, and shun the company of wanton women. Her mouth must not speak of idle matters, her eyes must not gaze upon distant or near sights, her ears must not heed any extraneous sounds. She refines her spirit between her breasts, silently forgetting passion and extinguishing thoughts, her heart never straying outward.

Whenever worldly desire stirs, she must immediately rectify her mind. When the root of lust arises, she must swiftly employ the *Lute-Playing to Summon the Phoenix* method: stoke the martial fire to nurture the Northern Sea, then raise the Xun wind to fan its depths, allowing the light of wisdom to illuminate the Dragon Palace. She concentrates her spirit between her breasts. Without unwavering resolve, if her nature wavers and her passions overflow, the Red Dragon cannot be severed.

For example, if her flow arrives on the first day of the previous month and ceases by the third, she begins her practice on the third day of the current month. The first session severs the tail; the next month, she begins on the second day to sever the waist; the following month, on the first day, she severs the head—thus, the Red Dragon is cut off. If she is past seventy, her celestial water has already ceased. Yet with a true master’s guidance in the *Lute-Playing to Summon the Phoenix* method, she may coax the Red Dragon forth and sever it—this is the true secret.

For virgin maidens, there is no need to sever the Red Dragon. They may directly ascend to primordial chaos in an instant—this is the practice of virgin immortality, akin to a man’s work of gathering the essence. The foremost requirement is to refine the self to perfection, for even the slightest deviation will cause one to miss the moment of essence production—this is the method of refining the form in the Greater Yin.

At the first stirring of desire, true qi arrives. One must then gather the true qi from the crucible of the pre-parental state, forcefully drawing it upward with intent and guiding it to the right breast thirty-six times. With the right hand, knead the left breast thirty-six times. The gathering and drawing of true qi must be performed six times, totaling two hundred sixteen repetitions. Then, sit in silence, holding the breath, and clasp both breasts with both hands. After a moment, when the breath settles, true qi will arrive again. Forcefully draw the true qi from the pre-parental crucible and guide it to the right breast twenty-four times. Perform this six times, totaling one hundred forty-four repetitions. Again, sit in silence, holding the breath, clasping both breasts with both hands. The work of the twelve double-hours is complete, aligning with the fire phases of the Celestial Cycle.

Each day, persist in this practice. By the second day of the following month, sever the waist as before; by the first day of the third month, sever the head. In the fourth month, the Red Dragon will be fully severed, and this work must no longer be performed. Instead, clasp both breasts with both hands, hold the breath, and sit in stillness. Daily, forget passion and cleanse the mind of all worldly thoughts. Progress steadily without slackening, and naturally, essence will be born.

From the Mysterious Female, Yang qi will surge upward, ascending from the coccyx through the spine, passing the Jade Pillow, and rising straight to the Mud Pillow Palace—identical to a man’s practice.

When the Passes open and the essence-fluid is obtained, it descends through the Yellow Court in union, irrigating the five viscera. This practice must not be interrupted; one must advance with diligent effort to achieve the perfection of the Infant. The work of harmonizing and nurturing requires meticulous care. Observe the stages of practice as employed by men, and one must understand this method. Only when encountering a woman of utmost sincerity—a chaste, virtuous, and refined lady—may the secret be revealed. Guard this well! Should it be transmitted to a woman of lewd or deceitful nature, one will surely incur heavenly punishment and retribution.

This is the supreme and wondrous Dao of the Great Awakening, the Golden Immortal of Primordial Heaven. It was first transmitted by the Queen Mother of the West to the Old Mother of Li Mountain, who then directly instructed Daoist Nun Cui. Nun Cui passed it to Daoist Nun Li, who transmitted it to Immortal Chen. Chen then taught Yang Saihua, who conveyed it to Huanghua Gu, who in turn instructed the Young Lady. Huanghua Gu also transmitted it to Ma Gu, who passed it to Wang Jinlian, who then taught Daoist Nun Yang. All these transmissions were oral, one to another.

Dazhi asked: *"Have male immortals ever transmitted this to female immortals?"*
Qiaoqiao replied: *"The Great Dao is the same for men and women. If one knows the true secret, a man may transmit it to a woman, and a woman may transmit it to a man. In ancient times, Patriarch Lü Chunyang directly instructed He Xiangu, and later Zhang Zhennu. Patriarch Wang Chongyang transmitted it to Sun Bu’er, the Primordial Sovereign—this is an example of a man transmitting to a woman. There are also cases of women transmitting to men: Sun Bu’er established the ‘Pure Serenity School’ and has since guided countless later disciples—this is a woman transmitting to men."*

Zhao Dawu asked: *"Are there those who have attained the Dao through self-realization?"*
The answer: *"In former times, there was Wei Yuanjun, named Huacun, styled Xian’an, a native of Bianliang. Her father, Wei Shu, styled Yuanyang, served as Left Deputy Minister during the reign of Emperor Cheng of Jin, later rising to Minister of Works and being enfeoffed as the Duke of Juyang County, posthumously honored as Wen Kang. Her mother was Lady Deqing. Yuanjun was born on the fifteenth day of the second month in the eighteenth year of Jian’an during the reign of Emperor Xian of Han. Gifted with extraordinary talent from birth, she studied the books of the Yellow Emperor and Laozi in her youth and was deeply drawn to the arts of divine transcendence. She longed to cultivate the Dao in seclusion, but her parents vehemently opposed it. At twenty-four, she was compelled to marry Liu Yi, a subordinate of the Grand Protector, and bore two sons. Her husband died early. Her eldest son, Liu Xia, became the Prefect of Ancheng, and her second son, Liu Pu, served as Gentleman of the Palace. At this time, Yuanjun renounced worldly ties and devoted herself to cultivation. On the sixteenth day of the twelfth month in the first year of Taikang during the reign of Emperor Wu of Jin (the year *wushen*), at midnight, the Dao Lord bestowed upon her a thousand volumes of immortal scriptures, along with oral instructions from a true adept of the Western Regions. She also transmitted the method to Qi Gu and her three daughters, as well as to Lingzhao Nü. All practiced this Dao. After Yuanjun attained the Way, she composed the *Jade Sword and Golden Writ*, which circulated in the world. She ascended as the Primordial Sovereign of the Purple Void, governing the life-destinies of the Southern Marchmount’s Perfected Ones, her influence extending between the Dipper and Ox constellations. She transcended the mundane and ascended in the ninth year of Chengxuan during the Jin dynasty, on the fifteenth day of the ninth month, by imperial jade decree. She left behind the *Exhortation to the World* and a collection of verses, including the *Songs of Refining Form in the Great Yin*."

**First Song of Refining Form in the Great Yin**
A woman’s path to immortality lies at hand,
Two wondrous gates open to the Mud Pillow Palace.
Align true breath with the tides,
Spirit returns to the Celestial Valley, naturally circling.

First refine the two breasts with true fire,
Then guide it into the Elixir Field, transmuting into lead.
With utmost sincerity, forge a body of pure Yang,
Reversing age to regain youth, living ten thousand years.

**Second Song of Refining Form in the Great Yin**
Essence and qi are the root, establishing the foundation of nature.
Still the mind, illuminating inner and outer with non-action.
In continuous breath, absorb the Yang waters,
Silently harmonize the elements, uniting Kan and Li.

Hunger and thirst quenched by the true fluid of Earth,
Drunk and asleep, clad in the Fire Dragon’s robe.
With a turn of the body, the sword strikes the Heavenly King’s Pagoda,
Transforming into an immortal, ascending the ladder of sixteen feet.

**Third Song of Refining Form in the Great Yin**
The wondrous workings of Qian and Kun adapt to square and circle,
Grasp the Double Passes, and qi spirals upward.
Reverse the flow of the Yellow River’s three-foot waves,
Scoop back the primal spring from the Mysterious Valley.

The pure vase opens upward, gathering clouds and snow,
When the clear flute is blown, heaven and earth respond.
Swallow the elixir of the two eights into the belly,
The body in an instant transforms into pure Qian.

**Fourth Song of Refining Form in the Great Yin**
Close the door, open the Passes, and the hundred channels flow,
Silently cultivate the work before midnight and after noon.
Refine the form, revolving through the wondrous gates,
Circulate the fire, fanning the bellows’ wind.

Harmonize pure Kun into the tiger within the cave,
Encircle and bind the dragon of the Zhen Palace.
The thunder of Earth issues commands, clouds dispense rain,
Washing the Yellow Sprout, piercing the nine layers.

**Fifth Song of Refining Form in the Great Yin**
To secure destiny, first regulate the original form,
Forget words, extinguish thoughts, and do not cling to scriptures.
The cauldron boils the red dust-water of the eight seas,
The mouth absorbs the azure essence of the three mountains.

The five-colored Mysterious Pearl pierces the Crimson Wall,
A sprig of willow leaf is planted in the golden vase.
The fair maiden displays her divine skill,
Carving bamboo into a flute, playing a single note.

**Sixth Song of Refining Form in the Great Yin**
Yin and Yang’s ebb and flow entrusted to the Yellow Dame,
Silently, true feelings harmonize two minds.
The old tiger feasts on the young phoenix’s marrow,
The red snake pierces through the black turtle’s nest.

Five hues intermingle, free from demonic obstacles,
Entering water, returning to the source, waves cease.
Clouds spread, the dragon roars, white snow flies,
The cowherd plays his flute, turning toward the western slope.

**Seventh Song of Refining Form in the Great Yin**
To refine the form, seek the root’s origin,
Qi circulates and gathers in the Upper Mystery.
Seize the Red Dragon, hiding in the field,
Secure the White Tiger, sleeping in the mud.

Summon the immortal maidens, the Blue Maidens,
Accompany the Perfected One, the White Jade Toad.
Mouth to mouth, transmit the talisman, connecting one qi,
Mutually consuming, turning back to heaven.

**Eighth Song of Refining Form in the Great Yin**
The divine maiden plays the flute at the two eights’ hour,
Clear notes resound, echoing in the western flowers.
The jade lad startles from the Dragon’s den,
The Queen Mother invites her to the Tiger’s foundation of Dui.

The hundred apertures open, qi circulates as one,
The nine palaces close breath to sever the Three Corpses.
Heaven’s Gate and Earth’s Axis communicate their tidings—
The inversion of yang’s return is known by few.

**Ninth Song of Refining Form in the Great Yin**
Ever since the Three Treasuries set forth to fetch the scriptures,
They toppled the Nine-Bend City of the Western Heaven.
To rectify heaven and earth, one must accumulate qi,
Seek to replenish water and fire to restore the primal form.

After three cycles, without inquiry, divine work is complete,
In a single moment, aligned with creation, it is accomplished.
Once more, the spring breeze welcomes the cosmos,
Transcending the ordinary to enter sagehood, eternal and everlasting.

Since ancient times, the true cultivation of women
Has been ten thousand times harder—scarcely one succeeds.

Master Zhao Dawu asked: *What should a woman prioritize when cultivating the Great Dao?*
The answer: *Sweep away desire first, sever attachment with urgency.*

Again, he asked: *Why?*
The answer: *If desire is not eradicated, her menses will not cease; if attachment is not cut, the Great Dao remains obscure. These two are the seeds of life and death, the root of rebirth. Thus, they must come first. If one can extinguish desire, sever emotional bonds, abandon greed and wrath, and dedicate body and mind, why fear the Dao’s difficulty or wisdom’s failure to arise? Even the dull-witted, following the method, may refine the primordial One Return—wisdom will multiply a hundredfold. Poetry, prose, and essays will flow without thought, understanding will dawn without study.*

For example, the common folk, entangled in passion, give birth to children in the usual way. But if one reverses this process, returning it to the self, spiritual wisdom grows. Over time, transformation occurs—one may then be called an immortal, Buddha, or sage.

Lü Zu said:
*To escape the suffering of rebirth, first extinguish ignorance.
Hold fast to the mind’s resolve, firmer than iron.
A single thought of womanly longing—
Not even raging fire can warm it.
Worldly ties and wealth,
Honors and splendor—all must be wiped away.
Retreat from the dusty realm,
Forget others, forget the self.*

The Dao, though nameless, is cultivated into form through unwavering awareness of the true source.
Why does the body exist? Through the power of the Great Ultimate,
A small heaven and earth, the five phases congealed.
From the parents’ twofold mystery, the true essence arises—
Only then do the four great elements form the fetal sac.
The five senses and four limbs gradually take shape,
Like a melon ripening on the vine, the body naturally appears.

Desire stirs awareness, anger and sorrow awaken emotion,
True knowledge and perception of things become complete.
From youth to maturity, the seven emotions shift,
The nature of consciousness alters, distinguishing signs emerge.
Desire rages, ambition swells, the heart clings to fame and profit—
Ten thousand times harder to break free from this great barrier.
Thus, the common saying: *Life and death are self-made.*
The sages could not bear to leave people trapped,
So they crafted alchemical scriptures to guide the worthy back to truth.

From entering the womb, spirit and breath harmonize,
Joining with essence to coagulate the sacred infant.
The method lies in silent contemplation, envisioning the original form.
The parents’ root is the Buddha-seed,
The parents’ paradise is one’s own foundation.
By this root, transcend the ordinary;
By this root, attain sagehood.
Do not mingle with the mundane—
The heart’s filth defiles the Kidney Palace.

The two qi come and go, yin and yang delight,
As if parents bestowing this body.
The noble one achieves the Dao; the common man clings to base emotions.
Only the resolute husband can temper his nature.
Governing the self is hardest—
Without virtue, one drifts empty, unaware of when to stop.
To embrace the highest good, gather and refine.

Rely on mutual forgetting, entering hibernation like a hidden insect.
True intention is the fire, breath is the wind.
Do not miss the appointed time—
When the thunder rumbles in earth and sky,
Gather and forge, drum and blow the flute.
When things submit and peace prevails, nurture gently, do not startle.
In an instant, with utmost urgency, return to play.
After two watches, the pearl coalesces, the Muni takes form.
The true master transmits the method, reversing the ascent upward.

The prior and posterior heavens merge in one place,
Three revolutions, nine returns, seven reversals refine it.
The Buddha calls it *Perfect Enlightenment*,
The Daoist calls it *Elixir Achieved*,
The Confucian calls it *Vast Integrity*—eternal, divine power,
The greatest, most unyielding, nurtured by virtuous power.

Again, a chant:
*The three teachings’ forbidden secrets are now revealed,
The River Chart and Luo Scripture name this source.
Confucians speak of the two and five congealing in wondrous union,
Daoists speak of the river chariot circling the heavens.
Buddhists speak of the deer cart and the turning Dharma wheel—
For ages unspoken, now fully transmitted.
I wish for like-minded friends of true heart,
To cultivate earnestly, awaken deeply, and discern with care.*

*From the "Women’s Alchemy Section of Chinese Immortal Studies"*
*Letter from Chen Wuxuan of Baoying, Jiangsu*

To the Venerable Master Yuandun, Enlightened One of Sudden Awakening:

With deepest respect, I humbly report: Since first hearing the Dao twenty-odd years ago, I have drifted in confusion, remaining unchanged. Reflecting on this, shame and regret overwhelm me. In past years, I have entered many gates and met numerous cultivators, most of whom merely copied teachings without true realization. Few achieved genuine verification. Alas, my fate is thin and karma deep—I have rarely encountered a true master. Thus, I turned to the immortal and Buddhist authentic transmissions, such as *The True Principles of Heavenly Immortality*, reading in stillness and pondering in darkness. Gradually, I gained some understanding. Later, I sought out an elderly Daoist master, Li, who at seventy still possessed robust vitality. His Daoist name was Zhongzhou. His teachings aligned with the classics, so I entreated him to transmit oral instructions such as "Severing the Red Dragon." Following them, I witnessed effects. Unexpectedly, Master Li passed away within a few years. Each time I recall him, I sigh deeply. In the twentieth year of the Republic, floods wrought disaster, disrupting my practice. The following winter, during meditation, I entered a state of forgetting form with eyes closed. Suddenly, the room filled with radiant light, clearer than daylight. When I opened my eyes, nothing remained. Soon after, repairs to my dwelling led to neglect.

Last year, I reflected: human life resembles a dream; awakened, one sees its illusory, impermanent nature. Unresolved in life and death, one remains bound to the wheel of rebirth. Thus, I vowed to enter seclusion, hoping to refine and deepen my practice. Nearly a year has passed, and I dare say I have achieved some verification. Yet, I regret not having received direct transmission of celestial oral instructions from a named master. I often fear treading perilous paths and straying onto wrong turns. Recently, Mr. Shi Zhihe delivered your writings, revealing your lofty Dao and profound virtue, your vast vows and deep compassion. Regrettably, confined to my seclusion chamber, I cannot pay homage in person. Joy and agitation mingle—my reverence is beyond words! Thus, I take the liberty of humbly beseeching you, Master, to generously bestow mercy. Kindly elucidate in detail the crucial oral instructions: advancing the *yang fire* at *zi*, retreating the *yin tally* at *wu*, bathing at *mao* and *you*, gathering the great medicine over seven days, crossing the passes to ingest it, forming the sacred embryo, and the great celestial cycle, among others. May this spare me from wasting time and missing the opportunity. Should I ever attain success, it shall be entirely your grace. Your boundless kindness will be engraved in my heart, and I vow to honor it throughout my life.

Having read your esteemed works, I see your advocacy for virtue, with particular emphasis on the feminine current and earnest guidance. Though I have not formally entered your lineage, I presume my bold request will not be rejected. I shall say no more. I earnestly await your reply.

With utmost respect, I bow a hundred times,
Your disciple, Chen Wuxuan

---

Reply to Ms. Chen Wuxuan of Baoying, Jiangsu

To Ms. Wuxuan, Disciple of Sudden Awakening:

Your letter has been received. Your sincerity in pursuing the Dao fills me with admiration. As for the immortal Dao, I can only be called a researcher. Deeply ashamed of my own lack of attainment, I am unworthy to serve as a teacher. Yet, moved by your earnest seeking, I fear silence may lead to disappointment and disheartenment. Thus, I cannot disregard your plea. However, as this is our first correspondence, I cannot presume to know your circumstances. Please answer the following questions in detail, after which we may proceed further:

1. Are you a monastic or a layperson?
2. Have you married, or are you unmarried?
3. What is your age?
4. Is your family situation favorable?
5. Do you have living parents? Any siblings or children?
6. Which Confucian, Buddhist, and Daoist scriptures have you read?
7. Which texts on women’s cultivation have you studied?
8. When does your seclusion period conclude?
9. What practice are you currently engaged in during seclusion?
10. What level of attainment do you aspire to achieve?

Respectfully,
Yuandunzi

---

Second Letter from Ms. Chen Wuxuan of Baoying, Jiangsu, with Answers

To the Venerable Master Yuandun, Enlightened Teacher:

With deepest respect, I humbly report: Burdened by deep karmic obstacles, I was born a woman. In my youth, I received little formal education, merely observing and mimicking my brothers’ studies. Fortunately, my family possessed many virtuous texts, which I perused in leisure. I particularly enjoyed reading *The Precious Scroll of Immortal He Xiangu*, which inspired my aspiration for cultivation.

**Yuandun’s Note:** From the perspective of immortals, men and women are equal in potential. In terms of practice and verification, women progress faster than men. In future attainment, there is no distinction of high or low. The common prejudice of valuing men over women is a human construct, not a natural one. In major world religions—Buddhism, Catholicism—and various secret sects in China, such as certain gates, halls, or societies, men and women are not treated equally. Only in the Daoist path is there no such hierarchy. Other religions guide ordinary people, while true Daoist cultivation is reserved for the most wise. Thus, it transcends such prejudices. Those with aspiration must not feel discouraged merely because they are women.

Later, I obtained works such as *Authentic Transmissions of Immortals and Buddhas*, *The Unity of Immortals and Buddhas*, and *The True Principle of Heavenly Immortality*, and only then did I realize that the Dao of immortality was a matter of easy cultivation and tangible verification.

**Yuandun’s Note:** For women, *The Unity of Immortals and Buddhas* and *The True Principle of Heavenly Immortality* may serve to clarify principles but cannot be practiced as written. *Authentic Transmissions of Immortals and Buddhas*, moreover, is too disordered and lacks structure, falling short of the other two works.

Thereupon, I upheld the precepts of refuge and vowed to renounce the red dust of the world. By this time, I had reached the age of sixteen or seventeen, and my widowed mother had already entrusted matchmakers to arrange my marriage. I then earnestly declared my aspirations to her. Not only did my mother refuse to believe or heed me, but she sought to undermine my resolve—when that failed, she resorted to relentless abuse.

**Yuandun’s Note:** Most people behave this way. I recall that around the age of ten, I found two volumes of *Biographies of Divine Immortals* by Ge Hong of the Jin dynasty at home. Too afraid to read openly, I placed the book on my lap and read in secret, while a copy of the *Analects* lay spread on the desk as a decoy.

For I feared that if my father learned I was reading heterodox books, he would beat and scold me. At thirteen, I slipped out to the streets to learn the talismans of Chen Prefecture, only to be thrashed severely upon returning home. At fourteen, I bought a copy of *The Ten Thousand Dharmas Return to the Source*, which was seized by my family and cast into the fire. Not until I turned sixteen did I gain some freedom, as they grew too weary to interfere further. Yet even then, I dared not openly display things like thunder-struck jujube-wood seals, camphor-and-willow spirits, or peachwood swords.

My maternal uncle, seeing that I endured every trial without wavering from my original resolve, took pity on me. He devised a ruse to deceive my mother, enabling me to be brought here—a place for practicing the Way while keeping my hair, where several Daoist nuns already resided. At last, my early aspirations found some solace. Yet this was but a desolate temple, a poor hermitage with no property to its name. Having come this far, I had no choice but to endure hardship and bitterness, fending for myself. The depths of my plight defy description. In the tenth and twentieth years of the Republic, two floods brought further setbacks.

**Yuandun’s Note:** Remaining at home entangles one in worldly affairs, while leaving home makes survival no easier. Is it truly better to cultivate the Dao at home or in seclusion? This is indeed a profound question. Not only women face this dilemma—men who seek the Way encounter the same difficulties. I have long wished to unite like-minded individuals across the nation to devise a sound solution, but the time is not yet ripe. When this wish may be fulfilled remains unknown. From my twentieth year to the present, over two decades have passed, and though I have known constant hardship, the pursuit of the "Dharma, wealth, companions, and place" has never left my thoughts for a single day.

In recent years, several chaste widows and virtuous maidens have come to the hermitage to cultivate. Reflecting on my own lack of true transmission, I cannot hope for swift attainment—how then can I guide them to fruition? Thus, two years ago, I traveled to the capital to seek instruction. Alas, the wise had concealed their traces, and I found no one to consult. I then turned to Buddhist organizations. After visiting many, I encountered only ordinary practitioners, and none whose understanding promised liberation.

**Yuandun’s Note:** In this day and age, traveling to seek the Way is no easy task. I have seen many monastics and lay practitioners devoted to the Dao who spent their lives journeying across the land, yet still gained nothing. How much less could one achieve by confining the search to the capital in so short a time? Buddhist organizations, aside from teaching people to recite the Buddha’s name, offer no other methods. I knew this could not satisfy your aspirations. In my earlier work, *Record of Minor Heterodox Arts*, I made a few remarks that may supplement what is left unsaid here:

*"Seeking a true teacher early—what a laughable idea! A true teacher does not advertise, distribute flyers, hang a sign, boast, or bear any special mark. The world is vast, and those who seek the Way—how are they to know who is a true teacher, or where one resides, in which province, county, mountain, cave, street, or alley? Let me speak plainly: a true teacher is encountered, not sought."*

Yet I believed the discipline and rituals of that teaching could restrain later learners and serve as a means for universal salvation. Thus, I returned home, shaved my head, and presumptuously donned the guise of a Buddhist monastic. Though I achieved some minor success in exhortation, I deeply regret my own inability to attain liberation.

**Yuandun’s Note:** Her circumstances are pitiable, yet her resolve is admirable!

Last year, on the ninth day of the third lunar month, I formally entered seclusion, intending to devote three years to quiet cultivation in pursuit of ultimate attainment.

**Yuandun’s Note:** This is an excellent decision—I wholeheartedly approve!

Since entering seclusion, I have maintained a regimen of three sittings by day and three by night, totaling six sessions daily. In recent months, I have frequently heard rushing wind within my ears and seen flashes like lightning before my eyes. At times, faint strains resembling silk and bamboo music or the chirping of insects arise, prompting me to send someone to investigate outside, though no trace is ever found.

**Yuandun’s Note:** Such phenomena are common to all who earnestly practice Daoist cultivation and are nothing to be alarmed by—do not let doubt or fear arise!

When internal respiration becomes perceptible, I must immediately enter meditation; otherwise, I feel discomfort. Only after sitting for two or three hours do I sense my qi restored and my spirit at ease. I am uncertain whether these two experiences are auspicious or inauspicious, or what their underlying cause may be. I humbly beseech my revered teacher for instruction.

**Yuandun’s Note:** These are merely physiological transformations within your own body and are not harmful. Persist in your practice, and even more wondrous states will unfold. I refer you to the letters of Li Chaorui, a student at Anhui Normal University, published in earlier issues of this journal, as well as the eight queries from Liu Yuliang of Zhongshan County, Guangdong, in the current issue. Though male and female physiology differs, the process of reversing the course of nature remains the same.

*The Ten Principles of Female Alchemy* states: “When a woman severs the Red Dragon, she must refine it with true fire and align it with true talismans. Should the fire or talismans falter, not only will the Golden Elixir fail to form, but she may also suffer from blood collapse.” These words are true and not empty. Your disciple has already undergone this once.

Afterward, it took more than a month of effort before recovery was achieved. That is now a matter of the past. As for the most recent attempt, when the Red Dragon was severed again within a short span, more than half a year has since passed—yet unexpectedly, what was cut off has returned. This is surely due to a failure to grasp the true fire and true talismans.

I privately reflect that for women who cultivate the Dao, transcending the cycle of rebirth and attaining liberation hinges entirely upon this. If this barrier is not thoroughly penetrated, efforts will be in vain, and the outcome will be nothing more than aging and death—no different from ordinary people.

*Yuan Dun’s note: Your insight is most apt; my own view is the same!*

The practice of "severing the Red Dragon" is not particularly difficult—indeed, it is several times easier than the practices of men. That it is cut off only to return must have a cause. When men cultivate the Minor Celestial Cycle, they may seal the Yang Pass and retain essence for a year or half a year without leakage, yet later, leakage may still occur. If one examines this closely, one finds that if the practice is out of harmony—whether excessive or insufficient—problems arise. One must grasp the principle of the "mean." Even minor details in diet may have an effect.

Those who maintain a vegetarian diet often favor such savory delicacies as mushrooms, bamboo shoots, and monosodium glutamate, but these are most unsuitable. One should consume bland, flavorless meals and dishes; even soy sauce, salt, and spices like pepper and chili should not be eaten in excess. There are many other minor considerations, but I shall not enumerate them all here.

In a moment of hesitation, I learned of your esteemed teacher’s great name and, a few days ago, took the liberty of writing without due consideration. Having prepared this letter, I am deeply grateful that you did not dismiss my humble words. Receiving your generous reply, I have read it again and again, filled with joy and gratitude beyond measure!

*Yuan Dun’s note: At present, I appear in the guise of an outer-path practitioner, devoted solely to the study of immortal arts, which differs from the principles of the Buddhist school. Since you, madam, have shaved your head and taken refuge in the Buddha’s gate, if you were to study the Dao under me as well, would you not fear reproach from your fellow disciples? In past years, there have been lay Buddhists who came to study the Dao with me. Occasionally, one or two of them, due to ill fortune, were discovered by their fellow practitioners, leading to great disputes. Frightened, they dared not show themselves and later consulted me, asking that I keep their studies secret and not make them public. I believe that studying the Dao is an upright and honorable matter—why conceal it? If one acts in such a furtive manner, what dignity remains? Would this not tarnish the reputation of the immortal arts? Though they had their own difficulties, I could not agree to their request and had no choice but to let the matter drop. I wonder if you, madam, face similar obstacles. This is why I have not yet published your name—it is for this very reason. I now present the full account to you, though it may weary your ears. If you do not disdain my unworthiness, I humbly beseech your esteemed teacher to compassionately reveal, in detail, the secret oral instructions on advancing the fire, withdrawing the talisman, bathing, nurturing, the Major and Minor Celestial Cycles, the civil and martial firing times, gathering and sealing, the living Zi hour, and all other such esoteric methods, so that I may cultivate accordingly. Should you deign to impart these teachings, any future attainment I achieve will be entirely the gift of your great kindness. My gratitude would know no bounds!*

The Perfectly Sudden One replied: Those who study Buddhism are often bewildered by terminology. Daoist practitioners share this affliction. In time, I shall dispel these knots of doubt for you—pray, do not fret.

In response to your ten queries, I humbly answer as follows:

1. I am a monastic.
2. I have never married.
3. I am forty-six years of age.
4. My circumstances spare me from cold and hunger.
5. My family home lies fifty *li* from here. My father passed early; my mother remains alive. Though I have siblings, we do not keep in touch.
6. I have perused the essential texts of both Confucianism and Buddhism. As for Daoist works, I have read: *The Twelve Kinds*, *The Seal of the Unity of the Three* (*Cantong Qi*), *Awakening to Reality* (*Wuzhen Pian*), *The Pointers on the Cultivation of Nature and Life* (*Xingming Guizhi*), *The Complete Guide to Daoist Cultivation*, *The Union of Dao and Buddha* (*Xianfo Hezong*), *The True Principles of Heavenly Immortality*, *The Authentic Transmission of Dao and Buddha*, *The Complete Works of Patriarch Lü*, *The Scripture of the Mysterious Pass*, *The Realm of Profound Mystery*, and *The Complete Works of Zhang Sanfeng*, among others.
7. The *Daoist Studies Minor Series* published by the Yihua Hall is nearly complete in my collection. As for the *Daoist Studies Minor Series for Women*, I have also acquired *Ten Precepts of the Female Elixir*, *The Orthodox Methods of Women’s Work*, *The Songs of Sun Buer’s Female Elixir*, and *A Discernment of the Differences Between Male and Female Elixir Cultivation*.
8. My initial seclusion was set for three months, but as I gained benefit within, I extended it to three years.
9. In my current practice, during seated meditation, I first guard the *hai di* (Sea Bottom). When the *qi* mechanism there stirs, I shift to guarding the breasts.
10. My aspiration is to attain the state of “ascending in broad daylight,” that the multitude may witness it.

Further, I have observed in texts on the female elixir the saying, “A woman’s destiny has three.” This likely refers to the *hai di* (Sea Bottom), *zhong gong* (Central Palace), and breasts. Yet I remain uncertain: when a woman first begins cultivation, which locus should she guard?

The Perfectly Sudden One replied: Guarding the Center is most fitting. This “Center” signifies the union of spirit and *qi*, not the Central Palace; it is the nexus of inner and outer resonance, not a fixed point within the body. While the *hai di*, *zhong gong*, and breasts may be guarded, clinging rigidly to any single locus strays from the Great Dao.

As for your disciple: what practice must now be employed to witness the auspicious sign of *yang* stirring within? Though all may know the method, its proper application is not necessarily understood. As the ancients said: “A hair’s breadth in error leads one a thousand *li* astray.” Truly, these are words of profound truth.

The Perfectly Sudden One replied: For now, proceed temporarily with the practice you are accustomed to. You must maintain *"an unbroken continuity, as if present yet not exerting force."* (These two lines are from the *Daodejing*, and are precisely applicable when first beginning.) As for the auspicious sign of *yang* stirring, you must first clearly understand the "Living Zi Hour." To discern whether the manifestation of the "Living Zi Hour" is pure and authentic, you must first comprehend the "Living Wu Hour." In women’s cultivation, most speak only of mercury and not of lead. The *Song of the Great Dao of the Numinous Source* by the Song-dynasty Immortal Lady Cao Wenyi is of great value among women’s alchemical texts—it is indispensable reading. If you have not yet seen it, I may copy a version for you in the future.

Whenever you encounter elders in the Dao, you ask them about the profound and wondrous, yet they respond vaguely—is this because they are unwilling to speak plainly, or because they do not know? The Perfectly Sudden One notes: There are three reasons for this. First, the boundary between male and female makes it difficult to speak freely. Second, men understand only the cultivation of the *qian* Dao and lack thorough knowledge of women’s physiology, so their explanations often miss the mark. Third, when they first studied the Dao under their masters, they did not inquire about women’s practices, and thus cannot answer such questions later. These are the shortcomings of male instructors.

As for female instructors, though they may avoid these three flaws, their level of attainment is often not yet equal to yours, so if you ask them, they naturally cannot provide answers. I humbly beseech the Venerable Master, whose wisdom encompasses both inner and outer, whose merit and fruition are complete, whose words surpass those of ordinary people, and whose aspirations transcend even the sages of old. In my joy and gratitude, I dare say this is the good fortune of three lifetimes. Though our exchange is but through letters, it is no different from receiving your oral teachings in person. Yet I fear that the celestial mechanisms and oral instructions are guarded as strict secrets, requiring face-to-face transmission and not to be lightly committed to paper—this would indeed be an unavoidable憾事. Reflecting on the Master’s boundless heart for propagating the Dao and earnest wish to deliver all beings, might you, for the sake of convenience, make an exception and impart them? I offer fervent prayers and await your gracious reply with reverence.

Your disciple, Chen Wuxuan, bows in respect.

The Perfectly Sudden One replied: Correspondence is acceptable, but do not be impatient. This matter depends on karmic conditions and timing, and cannot be forced. When an opportunity arises, I intend to copy several oral instructions on women’s alchemy and send them by post. However, success also depends on the disciple’s wisdom and merit. Relying solely on oral instructions does not guarantee attainment.

*Answering the Ten Questions of Miss Chen Wuxuan of Baoying*
*The Perfectly Sudden One*

**Question One:** You mentioned that there are only twenty-some extant texts on women’s alchemy in the country. Here, I possess only the *Winged Transformation Hall’s Minor Compendium on Women’s Daoist Studies* and your own *Annotated Poems on Women’s Alchemy*. I am unaware of others. If there are places where they may be purchased, kindly provide the addresses. If they are rare treasures, might I borrow two to copy?

**Answer:** Such books do not circulate publicly and cannot be purchased. When an opportunity arises, they may be disclosed in this publication.

---

**Question Two:** When I practice seated meditation during the day, stray thoughts are easily stilled, and tranquility comes with relative ease. Yet upon waking at night, I feel my spirit vigorous and my qi abundant, while scattered thoughts surge uncontrollably, preventing me from settling my mind. This is most disruptive. I humbly request an ingenious method to correct this.

**Answer:** Carefully study the *Treatise on Sitting in Forgetfulness* and thoroughly read the *Classic of Earthly Tranquility*—you will find the subtle method for "halting thoughts" therein. In my view, "scattered thoughts" pose no great harm to beginners. So long as your body remains still, let these thoughts rise and fall naturally. "Still water without ripples"—how easily said!

---

**Question Three:** Among women in our tradition who possess both merit and wisdom, some may be expected to achieve attainment. Having sought the Dao for many years, you must have encountered such individuals. Might you name a few to gladden my heart?

**Answer:** In this world, those lacking both merit and wisdom form the vast majority. A small number may have merit but no aspiration, or aspiration but no merit. Those who possess both are exceedingly rare. And among these, those who both love the Dao and may be expected to attain—such women are truly difficult to find today. I am presently making inquiries; if I learn of any, I shall inform you.

---

**Question Four:** There is a chaste widow who married at nineteen and was widowed at twenty-four. Though robust in body and keen in mind, the strange thing is that she has never menstruated. She now intends to cultivate the Dao—might she have hope of obtaining the medicine and refining the returning elixir? I humbly seek your guidance.

**Answer:** Women who never menstruate are not uncommon. If not due to a hidden ailment, this is likely a karmic root from a past life. When she truly begins Daoist practice, she will have greater advantage than women who menstruate, for she may omit the procedure of "slaying the red dragon." There was once a veteran film star who was born without menstruation. Though highly intelligent and youthful in appearance despite her age, she knew nothing of cultivation and lived a dissipated life—most regrettable.

---

**Question Five:** All alchemical texts state that women’s practice differs from men’s, and that "they speak of mercury but not of lead." This humble disciple is dull-witted; I humbly request your instruction.

**Answer:** This arises from the natural physiological differences between men and women, not from deliberate contrivance. The phrase "speak of mercury but not of lead" does not mean women possess only mercury and no lead. Rather, in former times, women were constrained by old rites and morals, often too shy to speak openly of such matters.

---

**Question Six:** Women’s alchemy texts say: "When the wind is about to come, seize the tiger at once; when rain is about to fall, then may you slay the dragon." Timing is critical—only by slaying at the right moment can refinement proceed. The profound subtleties elude me; I humbly beg your detailed explanation.

**Answer:** The character "slay" (*zhan*) in "slay at the right moment" may be a misprint for "gather" (*cai*). For details, consult the poem "Slaying the Dragon" in the *Annotated Poems on Women’s Alchemy by Sun Bu’er*. If you still do not understand, words on paper can hardly convey it—this must be transmitted orally in the future.

---

**Question Seven:**

**Question Seven:**
Is it true that "Yang Fire" descends first and "Yin Talisman" ascends afterward? How exactly does this circulation operate, and when should it be applied? I humbly beg your instruction.

**Answer:**
This kind of operation is profoundly subtle and intricate—it cannot be clearly explained on paper and must be addressed face-to-face. Moreover, it is not something that can be grasped in a short time. The learner and the transmitter must remain together, practicing constantly while receiving guidance at every turn. If errors arise, they must be corrected immediately; if flaws appear, they must be removed at once. Only then can one hope to reach the stage of perfection.

**Question Eight:**
The alchemical classics state, *"Set up the furnace, move the crucible, and establish the Celestial Cycle."* Where exactly are the furnace and crucible to be placed? Some say they are set in the Central Palace—is this correct?

**Answer:**
The furnace is the *Kun* furnace, located in the lower region; the crucible is the *Qian* crucible, situated in the upper region. The Central Palace is not the place for setting up the furnace and crucible.

**Question Nine:**
*"When the elixir is ripe, fire phases need not be applied; if fire phases are still applied, the elixir will be harmed."* What exactly constitutes the ripeness of the elixir?

**Answer:**
The ripeness of the elixir refers to the point at which the elixir has already formed. At this stage, one should focus on gentle fire for nurturing and not employ fierce fire for intense refinement. If one continues to refine with the same intensity as before, the formed elixir will be unable to stabilize in its place, risking dispersal or loss. Not only will all prior efforts be wasted, but grave illness may also arise.

**Question Ten:**
Master Chongxu said, *"When the elixir is ripe, pass through the barriers, ingest it, and enter the divine chamber to practice the Great Celestial Cycle for nurturing with fire."* Is this teaching accurate?

**Answer:**
It is entirely accurate.

Further Response to Ms. Chen Wuxuan’s Inquiry on Preserving the Achievement After Slaying the Red Dragon

By Yuandunzi

Last month, I received your letter but had no time to reply. Now, I specially set aside this moment to write these few lines, hoping to ease your distant longing.

This kind of work is a living method, not a rigid one. It must adapt to each person’s physical constitution and circumstances. Those who transmit the Dao often teach rigid methods, leading to strange illnesses—all because they fail to adapt. No matter what oral instructions one follows, every benefit carries a potential harm. Stubborn teachers paired with dull disciples often bring harm before any benefit is gained.

When a physician prescribes medicine to treat an illness, they must carefully examine the patient in person. If one merely inquires about symptoms and dispenses remedies, danger cannot be avoided. How much more so for such great matters as contending with the transformations of creation and the profound mysteries beyond even ghosts and spirits? How can one resolve them without a single face-to-face encounter, relying only on a few letters of inquiry? If illness arises, who will bear the blame?

Thus, the only guidance I can offer you on paper is these four words: *"embrace the One and guard the center."*

*"Embrace the One"* means that the heart and breath depend on each other, and spirit and qi unite without separation.

*"Guard the center"* means that after spirit and qi unite, one abides in perfect stillness within the central palace, returning to the primal chaos before heaven and earth existed.

This is the highest-grade elixir method—beneficial without harm. Since the Red Dragon has already been slain, it is fitting to continue with this work. If one can reach its most profound and wondrous state, one may transcend the cycle of rebirth and rise above the turning of kalpas, standing shoulder to shoulder with sages, immortals, and buddhas. Looking down upon the realms of humans and gods, one plays freely with life and death, and trivial transformations of this illusory flesh-body become no concern at all.

*"When the Dao is spoken, it seems as bland as if it had no flavor."* If you are of superior root and sharp capacity, you will surely trust these words.

**Appendix: Original Letter from Ms. Chen Wuxuan**

Respectfully submitted,

Last month, I was already enlightened by your teachings in this publication, and you further graciously copied and sent me the *"Song of the Great Dao of the Spiritual Source."* The blockage in my heart has gradually opened. How can I ever express my gratitude for such kindness and virtue?

I should not presume to trouble you further, but should quietly await the right moment and reverently follow your instructions.

Yet your disciple, acutely aware of the critical importance of the *Fire Talisman* and the peril of its loss, cannot but make repeated entreaties.

In recent months, there has been some consolation: the dragon has been slain and has not returned. Yet as the *Fire Talisman* remains obscure in its depths and workings, I secretly fear that what has been gained may yet be lost, and what has departed may yet return. Thus I urgently beseech you, Master, to bestow great compassion, look down with pity, and reveal a hint of the celestial mechanism—transmit but one true formula—so that I may attain the ultimate in elixir refinement and ascend the true path of the Perfected. Then I shall not waste years in vain, nor bear the empty name of cultivation.

Looking back upon the aspirations I expressed earlier, I now see how they might invite the reproach of boastful words. Upon reading the venerable discourse on the reality of ascension in the seventy-fourth issue of this publication—where not a single soul has yet succeeded—I realize how my dull and clumsy faculties led me to rashly declare such transcendent ambitions, surely provoking the laughter of the wise.

I prostrate myself before you, Master, whose learning spans all schools and whose resolve to deliver sentient beings is unmatched in ancient or modern times, in China or beyond. With but a single foolish impulse, I have secluded myself to practice quietude and presumptuously pursued the Way of the Real, yet have failed to present myself before you to reverently receive your teachings—how deep is my shame!

Herein I record several doubts and humbly implore you, Master, to generously bestow your vast wisdom and provide detailed instruction. The secret celestial mechanisms I especially entreat you to address in writing. Should I ever treat these teachings with disrespect or transmit them lightly, I vow to suffer the destruction of my body.

I dare not make such bold requests lightly, but only fear repeating past mistakes. If you would deign to look upon this lowly one with compassion and indulge my foolish sincerity, I would be infinitely grateful.

I beseech you to graciously elucidate the ten questions listed below. Should you condescend to grant my plea, my gratitude would know no bounds. With reverence, I prostrate myself and bow a hundred times.

Your disciple, Chen Wuxuan of Chahé Town, west of Baoying Lake, respectfully submits.

**Reply to Ms. Chen Wuxuan of Chahé Town, Baoying**
*Yuandunzi*

Having received your previous letter introducing Ms. Zhang Zhide, who has practiced the art since severing the Red Dragon, she personally sought me out in the countryside last month and stayed for two days. I explained to her in broad terms the advance and retreat of the *yang fire* and *yin tally*, as well as the circulation of breath in ascent and descent. Though her literacy is limited, her practice is indeed commendable. Now forty-one years of age, her monthly courses have ceased for three years. Regarding the subtle conditions within her body—which I found improper to inquire about directly—my wife, Yizhu, acted as intermediary, relaying my questions. Her past bodily experiences align perfectly with the oral instructions I have received, confirming she is no deceiver. As a practitioner of substance, her foundation is already firm, so she grasped my teachings at once. She far surpasses more learned women in this regard—a most encouraging development. She departed content, though I regret not obtaining her address. I hear she rents a garret in Yangshupu, Shanghai, cooking for herself and living independently, not residing at the Tang residence. Have you heard of this? Your seclusion period remains unfulfilled, so it is best not to emerge prematurely, lest the vulgar mock you.

The operation of *yang fire* and *yin tally* belongs to the *youwei* method, emphasizing the word *"refine."* The subtleties of *embracing the One* and *guarding the center* belong to the *wuwei* method, emphasizing the word *"nurture."* The *youwei* method cannot encompass *wuwei*, but *wuwei* can encompass *youwei*. What I shared with Ms. Zhang pertains to mid-level alchemical practice, whereas what I previously conveyed to you in this journal constitutes the supreme attainment. Take care not to dismiss it with disdain or harbor dissatisfaction.

**Further Reply to Ms. Chen Wuxuan Regarding Post-Severing the Red Dragon**
*Yuandunzi*

I received your letter last month but had no time to respond. I now take this moment to pen these few lines, hoping to ease your distant longing.

This practice is a living method, not a rigid one. It must adapt to each person’s physical constitution and circumstances, flexibly adjusting as needed. Those who transmit the Dao often teach rigid methods, frequently causing strange illnesses—all due to their failure to adapt. No matter what oral instructions are given, every advantage carries a corresponding disadvantage. When stubborn teachers encounter dull-witted disciples, the harm often precedes the benefit. A physician prescribing medicine must carefully examine the patient in person; if treatment is given merely by inquiring about symptoms, danger may arise. How much more so with such great matters as contending with the transformations of creation and the unfathomable mysteries beyond even spirits and gods? How can one resolve them without face-to-face guidance, relying only on a few letters of inquiry? If illness arises from practice, who will bear the responsibility?

Thus, what I can convey to you on paper today are only these four words: *"embracing the One and guarding the center."* *"Embracing the One"* means that the heart and breath depend on each other, spirit and qi unite without separation. *"Guarding the center"* means that after *"spirit and qi unite,"* one abides in profound stillness within the central palace, returning to the primordial state of chaos before heaven and earth existed. This is the supreme alchemical method, offering only benefit and no harm. Now that the Red Dragon has been severed, it is the perfect time to continue this practice. If one can reach its most profound and wondrous depths, one may transcend the cycle of rebirth and rise above the turning of kalpas, standing shoulder to shoulder with sages, immortals, and buddhas—looking down upon the heavens and humanity, playing freely with life and death. Trivial changes in the physical body then become insignificant.

*"The Dao spoken aloud is bland, as if without flavor."* If you are of superior capacity and sharp faculties, you will surely believe these words.

**Appendix: Original Letter from Ms. Chen Wuxuan**
Respectfully,
Since you graciously instructed me in the previous issue and also transcribed and sent the *"Song of the Great Dao of the Spiritual Source,"* the obstructions in my heart have gradually dissolved. How can I ever repay such kindness and virtue? I ought not to trouble you further but should instead await the right moment in quiet reverence. Yet I humbly await your guidance.

Yet your disciple, acutely aware of the urgency of the *Fire Talisman* and the peril of its loss, cannot but make repeated entreaties. In recent months, there has been some cause for reassurance: the *Red Dragon* has been severed yet has not returned. Still, as the true essence and subtleties of the *Fire Talisman* remain unclear to me, I secretly fear that what has been gained may yet be lost, and what has departed may yet return. Thus, I urgently beseech you, Master, to bestow your boundless compassion, look upon me with mercy, and deign to reveal a glimpse of the celestial mechanism, to transmit the true oral formula—so that I may grasp the ultimate principle of *elixir refinement* and ascend the true path of transcendence. This way, I may avoid squandering years in vain and escape the hollow pretense of cultivation.

Looking back upon the aspirations I expressed earlier, I now see them as no small boast, inviting ridicule. Upon reading the esteemed discourse on the reality of ascension in the seventy-fourth issue of this publication—where it is stated that not a single soul has yet achieved it—I realize that my dull and clumsy faculties have led me to rashly proclaim such lofty ambitions, surely provoking the scorn of those of true attainment.

Prostrate before you, Master, whose learning encompasses all schools and whose resolve to deliver sentient beings is unmatched in past or present, in China or beyond: I, in my foolish sincerity, have secluded myself to cultivate stillness and vainly pursued the Way of the Real, yet have failed to present myself before you to reverently receive your teachings. How deep is my remorse!

Herein, I humbly submit several questions, earnestly imploring you, Master, to bestow your vast grace and provide detailed instruction. The secret celestial mechanisms I especially entreat you to expound in writing. Should I ever treat these teachings with disdain or transmit them carelessly, I vow to suffer the destruction of my very being. I dare not make such bold requests lightly—only that I dread repeating past mistakes. If you would deign to look upon my sincerity with compassion and forgive my ignorance, I would be infinitely grateful.

I beseech you to graciously address each of the ten questions listed. Should you grant this request, my gratitude would know no bounds. With utmost reverence, I prostrate myself and bow a hundred times.

Your disciple from West Fork River, Baoying Lake,
Chen Wuxuan, bows her head in submission.

In response to the Venerable Zhang Huikun of Chicheng, Tiantai,
The Perfected One of Sudden Enlightenment.

The previous letter forwarded by the *Xian Dao Monthly* contained points not without reason, yet regrettably, you had not thoroughly studied the entirety of *Yang Shan Journal*. Had you, at the time, examined each issue in sequence from the first to the ninety-ninth, the editorial aims of the journal—and the gradual evolution of its style—would have become perfectly clear to you, leaving no room for doubt.

All the essays in *Yang Shan Semi-Monthly* debating the doctrines of immortals and buddhas were written from a defensive position, compelled by necessity. Otherwise, who would idly waste ink and brush? Layman Zhang Huasheng was a devotee of the Three Teachings—Confucianism, Buddhism, and Daoism—neither favoring immortals nor slighting buddhas. Thus, his writings consistently sought to harmonize the teachings of immortals and buddhas. Alas, certain parties deliberately sought to create a monolithic following, refusing to tolerate Huasheng’s efforts at reconciliation. They insisted on elevating Buddhism above both Confucianism and Daoism, forcing Huasheng to rise in opposition. This led to many complications, though such was never his original intent.

Alas! Whose fault was this?

In all times and places, for every school of thought, there will always be proponents, opponents, and reconcilers. Take, for example, the teachings of immortals and the Dao: I and my fellow believers belong to the camp of proponents. Those who slander these teachings are numerous, all falling into the camp of opponents. Then there are figures like Huasheng and Zhuqian, as well as Zunxian, who belong to the camp of reconcilers.
