You will sense a faint brightness, like moonlight in darkness. Then use intention to guide this light to illuminate the Mud Pill Palace *(Editor’s Note: This means drawing the life-qi from the top of the head to merge with one’s spirit-intention—what is called the "intention-pearl," the celestial pivot of human stability. For details, see "Revealing Heaven’s Mechanism.")*. When the brain is filled with light and the head feels crystalline (this is the marrow-washing method), over time, guide this brightness from the Double Towers to the Crimson Palace. Retain it there for a moment, and you will feel the Crimson Palace turn purely white (this is the heart-washing method). Then direct intention to the Central Yellow, retaining it as before, until the Central Yellow also turns white (this is the Pure Land method). The radiance will naturally descend with the qi, and you will feel the Lower Field gradually expand, becoming ever more serene and profound (this is the Ocean-Purifying method). With prolonged inner illumination, the light grows brighter and the space vaster. After much time, you will sense qi stirring within (this is the dragon emerging from the sea bottom). Maintain a single thought of clarity and emptiness, gently guiding the eyes’ light to circle and illuminate from the sea bottom backward. Soon, you will feel this light penetrate the Tailbone Pass (this is the tiger turning from the water’s depths). Gradually, light will rise from below (this is the Yellow River flowing backward), ultimately piercing the crown (this is the method of returning essence to replenish the brain). At this moment, employ the head-to-tail illumination method. What is this method? Let the light of both eyes rest in midair, like the sun and moon shining down upon the crown, penetrating the Three Passes straight to the deepest sea bottom (this is the secret of the sacred sun and moon illuminating the Golden Court). It will seem as if a moon’s reflection rests at the sea bottom, mirroring the moon in the upper sky (this is the secret of "water in the Yangtze, moon in the heavens"). At this juncture, all sounds fade into emptiness. Use a single intention to surge upward and penetrate downward, advancing both without conflict. With long practice, you will feel this clear light pierce the Nine Heavens above and shatter the Nine Abysses below.

At this moment, I am no longer aware of my body’s existence. Such is the entry into inner illumination—ah! Speaking of it is easy, but practicing it is difficult. I may be dull-witted, yet I shall devote myself to these words.

*(Xie’s note: This method of inner illumination is a secret never before revealed in the alchemical classics. Its essence lies in naturalness. At the outset, one must first empty and still the heart—this is the key! It constitutes the foundational practice of the "Three Observations." The initial regulation of breath is also crucial. If this method is combined with the union of heart and breath, it becomes the supreme vehicle of the Great Dao.)*

Shan Yi, having parted one day, returned shortly after and said: "Since I began practicing inner illumination and continued with the formless meditation, my mind-ground has grown clear and bright. Gradually, I felt as though my lower region had vanished, as if boundless and fathomless. This arose from prolonged inner cultivation. After my thoughts settled profoundly, this scene appeared. I felt my entire body suffused with harmonious qi, and eventually, even this vision faded beyond concern. Only then did I realize that the breath had ceased, while the lower region grew intensely warm. Suddenly, amid the extreme heat, several strands of cool qi emerged—some descending from the chest and abdomen, others flowing down the front of the spine and back of the viscera, swirling around the male root as if on the verge of leakage. I feared this was not an auspicious state and halted midway. (If one stops here without adding the fire of refinement, harm may follow.) Upon emerging, I respectfully sought instruction."

The Lazy Old Man said: "Excellent question! This cool qi flowing downward is the yin essence encountering qi and transforming. (This yin essence is precisely the strands of cool qi mentioned earlier.) If the true qi is weak and the transformation lacks refinement, it will merge with ordinary qi. (Ordinary qi is ordinary fire; at this stage, it is ministerial fire.) This may form generative essence. Without advancing the yang fire (holding the breath and concentrating the mind is called advancing yang fire), this substance will inevitably break through the barrier and escape. The method is to focus the spirit and gather qi at the sea bottom, then propel it with the light of both eyes, as if turning a millstone. At this moment, the heart grows even more tranquil, the breath halts, and true qi flows downward to the lower region. (This is the great secret of advancing yang fire.) The lower region then becomes hot as a boiling cauldron (boiling describes the state of fire and water merging), and yin essence transforms into qi."

*(Xie’s note: This segment of the method emphasizes the dual-eye spiritual light and breath retention, followed by forgetting form in emptiness. Thus, ordinary fire departs, and true fire arises. If the practitioner’s nature-cultivation is impure or the upper-body practice insufficiently refined, one may fail to forget form and still the mechanism, giving rise to desire. With desire, essence will not transform into qi but instead become turbid fluid and leak out. Be cautious! Be doubly cautious!)*

Following the qi’s ascent, it pierces the tailbone, rises to the mud pill, and transforms into true fluid. (This is the concrete evidence of returning essence to replenish the brain.) It then descends the "heavy tower," moistening the Crimson Palace. (This is called "postnatal sweet dew," a substance that transforms into blood.)

*(Xie’s note: The formless, pure aspect returns to the Central Yellow within the mud pill, while the turbid aspect enters the Crimson Palace and lower elixir field.)*

From the front of the spine behind the heart, it divides and reaches both kidneys. (At this point, the sweet dew has turned red, transforming into blood.) I then direct the light of both eyes downward to the kidneys, rotating left and right. The faster the rotation, the hotter it becomes (this refines blood into essence). The heat extends from the kidneys to the navel wheel (this is the method of refining the ordinary to return to the true, and refining qi to return to primordial qi). This heat must be several times more intense than before, so that this substance transforms from true essence into qi. From here, one must not cease (not even briefly). The heat then descends again to the sea bottom, where the work of concentration and infusion continues. (This is a crucial instruction.) As before, the yin essence (which will inevitably be present and abundant—only after achieving pure yang throughout the body will it vanish) transforms into qi and ascends. The method of refining yin to return to yang is no more than this. Its effects may be witnessed in due course (interruption makes them difficult to see, hence the warning against it). The subtlety lies in perseverance (this cannot be overemphasized). Thus, by circulating without pause and practicing at set times daily (this is the only way), how can one not achieve what the ancient masters promised—success within months? (This is certain, without doubt!)"

*(Xie’s note: Practicing the above method is no easy task! It is better to first open the bellows and form true breath before proceeding, as this makes control easier. This method is suitable for middle-aged and elderly practitioners.)*

The Great Lazy One said: "Your words are indeed so. I shall follow this practice. Yet I have heard that in the method, after the heart, one divides and descends to the two kidneys—this is the way of women’s cultivation. Since women take blood as their foundation, their mysterious pass opens naturally at the Crimson Palace. In their practice, they add rubbing at the space between the two breasts, called the Breast Stream. Kneading and rubbing a hundred or a thousand times, the chest becomes fiery and hot, and one feels only qi oppression, even a sensation of stiffness and numbness. Only then does the blood begin to flourish. The method is simply to withdraw with intention behind the heart and before the spine, dividing to pour into the two kidneys. If, like men, one were to descend straight from the heart to the abdomen, there would be the danger of blood collapse." *(Xie’s note: This is a secret never before revealed in the alchemical canons!)* "(This question concerns the true internal practice of the Great Lazy One’s venerable mother. Lazy Weng often explained it to her in ordinary times, hence this inquiry—this is the essential method of women’s elixir cultivation.) Thus, the application is just as you have said.

Now, what you describe pertains to qi. When qi ascends to the brain and transforms back into fluid, this is already extraordinary. Once it has become fluid, what hinders its direct descent to the lower field? Why must it, like women, descend to the Crimson Palace, then withdraw before reaching its destination, passing through the two kidneys and rising to the navel wheel before it finally transforms into qi? This principle is unclear. Moreover, qi and *qi* are one and the same—both are by nature fire, differing only in the names of pre-heaven and post-heaven. Having heard your discourse, my doubts multiply, and I cannot suppress them. I beg you to clarify."

Lazy Weng said: "Excellent indeed is this question! You may truly be called one who doubts well. What I have spoken is half what I heard from my teachers and half what I learned from books. Now, let me briefly outline its general principles. I say: I am ready to hear your profound teaching."

The Master said: "In men, yang resides in the abdomen; in women, yang resides in the back—this is the unchanging principle of Heaven and Earth. What I call *yin essence* is not true essence in form, though it resembles it. It is the fluid transformed from food and drink, not yet refined into blood, stagnating among the hundred apertures, becoming phlegm-like. When it lingers in the middle burner, it forms *yin-fluid* patterns; when it flows into the bladder, it becomes slippery discharge. Within the three hundred joints and eighty-four thousand pores of this body, such substance abounds, lurking in every crevice. When external pathogens exploit these gaps, they collude with this substance to wreak no small harm.

Now, when my true *qi* circulates and warms it, this substance melts and stirs, following the *qi* to protect and flow into the lower field. Its nature is yin-cold, so its movement seeks only coolness. Yet if it accumulates without transformation, it must eventually turn to fire and emerge—what the world calls *flowing fire syndrome* is none other than this.

Thus, whenever I sit in meditation and true *qi* flows, I feel a cool, rustling breeze rising from within—this is the effect of this substance being transformed and released. Therefore, when this substance flows into the lower field, I must apply great true fire to refine it (this is a most essential secret). Then it becomes like mist or cloud, rising with the true *qi* along the spine to the crown of the head. Once gathered and condensed, it becomes true fluid, like rain or dew, dripping from the nostrils into the mouth (this is the sweet dew). It moistens the Crimson Palace (here, one must hold the intention firmly), and with the heart’s fire warming it, it transforms into blood.

It must then descend between the spine and the heart, dividing to flow into the two kidneys. After further refinement, it follows the *qi* to the navel, and through great refinement, it becomes *qi*. This is the fixed process of *qi*-transformation, the same for men and women.

Who does not consume food and drink? The fluids derived from them are produced daily. If one remains ignorant of the secret of refining them through the heart’s intention, few will avoid illness—hence nine out of ten people suffer from phlegm. Those who cultivate the Way often struggle with seminal loss. The world fails to understand, attributing it to wayward thoughts, or to a lack of harmony between heart and kidneys, or to poor digestion—all are mistaken. The true cause lies in not gathering the *qi* through the heart’s intention, allowing fluids to overflow, accumulate, and congeal into phlegm, which then flows downward and leaks out. Some forcibly suppress it, only to develop external ailments—abscesses and toxins—where it transforms into fire and erupts. The harms it breeds are too numerous to count, so I have explained it in detail.

As for what is called *true essence*, it exists when embodied as a whole, but vanishes when grasped or sought."

As for the essence of intercourse, it remains a product of *qi*-transformation, thus possessing form and color; since it arises from within, it can give life. Yet this fluid from food and drink comes from without, and if not refined by the heart, the blood has not yet transformed—it merely resembles essence in form, how could it give life? It is not the supreme treasure, and if it leaks out occasionally, what cause is there for regret, for worry, for fretfulness? Is this not delusion? Rather than taking medicine to astringe it, it is better to refine it as I have said—this is called "removing the firewood from beneath the cauldron."

I speak of this matter so earnestly because, though this substance is mundane, when refined according to the method, it becomes *yin qi*. When it ascends to the brain and descends to the heart, it can transform into blood, already a treasure. If it further descends to the kidneys and rises to be refined at the navel, meeting the *earth* (note: *earth* refers to true intention and true breath), it becomes indistinguishable from true *qi*, thus manifestly the supreme treasure.

Alas! The prenatal is yang, the postnatal is yin—our cultivation is nothing but the Way of refining yin to return to yang. The secret lies in nothing more than forgetting form to nourish *qi*, forgetting *qi* to nourish spirit, forgetting spirit to nourish emptiness. The reason one must attain the state of "forgetting" is that only when the gathered essence, *qi*, and spirit all belong to the prenatal can they be free from harm. Moreover, what matters is that the body constantly undergoes refinement, and its function lies solely in fire. With sufficient fire, there is prosperity; with weak fire, there is decline. Without forgetting, there is no gathering; only by forgetting can fire be sufficient—this is the essential secret of cultivating the truth.

(Note: "Forgetting" means to forget what has been established, not empty forgetting. Thus, it is said: first preserve, then forget—preservation refers to preserving spirit.)

Alas, take heed! I say: "How dare I not listen and obey?"

Then Great Lazy One asked again: "I have heard there are three hearts—what does this mean?"

The master replied: "Indeed. They are called the Heavenly Heart, the Earthly Heart, and the Human Heart, yet in truth they are one. As the classics say: *'The heart is the mansion of spirit and brightness; the Dao of transformation arises from it.'* For the entire body moves or rests by the heart’s *qi*, just as a fish dwells in water. The ancients said: *'The solid parts of the body are Earth; the hollow parts are Heaven; bending and stretching, speech and sight and hearing—these are Man.'* They also said: *'The Heavenly Heart resides in the brain, the Earthly Heart in the abdomen, and the Human Heart in the Crimson Palace. The Crimson Palace’s heart is a solid yet empty, numinous, and unobscured entity—one thing containing three aspects.'* For the hearts in the brain and abdomen are formless and insubstantial, yet they are none other than the numinous *qi* of that solid, lotus-like center, ascending and descending with true presence. Thus I say they are one in truth."

Great Lazy One said: "I understand. *Intent* is what the heart emits. The heart itself is soundless and odorless; when thought stirs, it issues forth as intent. *Thought* refers to the present mind—it is the very heart itself. *Intent* is the heart’s resonance, meaning the thought has already arisen. The Buddhist epithet *Guanshiyin* is a great secret for cultivating body and mind—ponder it well. In my reading of the sutras, the character *shi* ('world') should be interpreted as *shen* ('body'), meaning to carefully observe the movements and stillness of *qi* within one’s own body, lest they stray into error. As Lü Dongbin said: *'The Great Dao teaches people first to stop thoughts; if thoughts do not cease, all effort is in vain.'* He also said: *'Fear not the arising of thoughts, but the slowness to awaken.'* Master Qingyunzi said: *'Thoughts still within the cavity are easily removed; once released outward, removal becomes harder.'* Thus the ancients said: *'Remove thoughts as they arise, and immortals will acknowledge you.'*"

Great Lazy One smiled and asked: "Is the secret of immortal cultivation limited to this? I have heard it said: *'To cultivate life without cultivating nature is the foremost flaw in practice,'* and also: *'To cultivate nature without cultivating life makes it difficult for the spirit to attain sagehood even after ten thousand kalpas.'* What does this mean?"

The master sighed: "Life without nature is not numinous; nature without life does not manifest. It means one must cultivate both nature and life. In my view, cultivating one part of nature preserves one part of life, for nature and life cannot be separated. In truth, sometimes one leans toward nature yet life is within it, or leans toward life yet nature is within it—like form and shadow, can they be divided? In cultivating the Dao, first establish your resolve: this is the foundation of nature’s work. Cherishing the body as jade is the foundation of life’s work. Proceeding further, stopping thoughts and eliminating delusion is the work of nature; regulating, abiding, and circulating the breath—its ascent and descent—is the work of life. Reflect on this: if thoughts do not cease, breath is not regulated, and delusion is not eliminated, progress is impossible. All practices of regulating, abiding, circulating, ascending, descending, blending, and uniting must unfold in a state of no-thought, no-worry, where all sounds are empty and not a speck of dust remains. Thus I say: *'Cultivate one part of nature, and you preserve one part of life.'* Do you agree?"

Great Lazy One replied: "Yes. You have tested this yourself. But in the alchemical tradition, the body has four seas: the heart is the Sea of Blood, the stomach the Sea of Grain, the kidneys the Sea of *Qi*, and the brain the Sea of Marrow. Their subtleties are not yet fully clear to me—would you elucidate?"

The master said: "An excellent question. The entire body relies on the natural *qi* of life to grow and take form. Only the Sea of Grain depends on postnatal, external food and drink to digest and transform, replenishing what the body’s *qi* lacks—this is common knowledge and needs no elaboration. Great Lazy One, do you understand why those who teach nourishing life always begin with the layer of *mingxin* (obscuring the heart)? It is because the heart is the Sea of Blood: when the heart is cool, blood is generated; when the heart is obscured, it becomes cool. The secret of *mingxin* lies in subtly guiding the heart’s *qi* with intent, withdrawing it to the front of the spine, sensing the body’s warm *qi* gathering protectively around the Crimson Palace—above, below, front, back, left, right, and center."

He continued: "In this way, the gentle *qi* of life, upon nearing the Crimson Palace, naturally transforms into blood, then diffuses through the muscles and channels. Its purest essence retreats and descends to the two kidneys, where the red and vibrant becomes the pure essence of *qi*, the Heavenly One. Great Lazy One, do you know whether those who teach nourishing life close their eyes before *mingxin*? Ah! Its meaning is profound, its principle refined."

The heart’s numinous spirit manifests through the eyes—this is the first principle. The two eyes also store the essence-*qi* of the liver’s *hun*, the lungs’ *po*, the spleen’s spirit, and the kidneys’ essence—this is the second. When the heart enters *mingxin* and the eyes close in advance, the *qi* of life from the viscera, limbs, interior, and exterior naturally gathers in audience at the Crimson Palace—this is the third. Moreover, whenever this gathering occurs and life-*qi* is spontaneously attained, it transforms of itself into pure blood without deliberate effort; its wondrous function also lies in the two eyes—this is the fourth. Furthermore, the ability to guide this pure blood, each following its *qi*, to distribute and moisten the channels, muscles, and interstices, arises entirely from the eyes suspended like sun and moon, illuminating all within and without, high and low, far and near—now with intent, now without, as if guiding yet not guiding—this is the fifth. You once said its mechanism lies in the eyes; from this, one may trust that the ancients’ words do not deceive.

The Lazy Master said: The kidneys are the Water viscera, called the Sea of *Qi*. You doubt this—good doubt indeed. Yet know this: that the Water viscera are called Water viscera does not mean the bladder stores turbid water. Rather, they are where the *qi* of our body’s breath gathers, purely postnatal yet divided into yin and yang—yang is called *qi*, yin is called fluid. These two kinds, without the fire of the body’s Great Yang to refine them, will stagnate and fail to transform, causing no small harm. The diseases they spawn are too numerous to name. What is the secret to refining them? It lies entirely in using the two eyes to guide true yang and store it in the Sea-Bottom. With a mind undistracted, the *qi*-mechanism flows unimpeded, neither inner nor outer, unaware of the five viscera, six bowels, four limbs, or heaven and earth. Only then do you inwardly reflect upon the Sea-Bottom, sinking a crimson sun there (this is the crucial secret). If you forget, you must promptly awaken to its presence; when present, act as if forgotten (wondrous indeed is such practice). If lost, awaken to its presence as if it were stored; thus the cycle continues (this is the essential instruction). When this one sea is settled and free of harm—ah, Lazy One!

In Dao cultivation, those who begin are as numerous as ox hairs; those who succeed are as rare as rabbit horns. Why? Because they abandon this very gate of the Sea—such cases are everywhere under heaven. If you are truly resolved, persist in this practice. To persist without firmness, or to be firm without constancy, is of no benefit (heed this warning, heed it well!). Strive on, I urge you—ten thousand times, ten thousand times!

Heed this warning, heed it well!

Lazy Old Man says: Ah, Lazy One! Take heed—what was spoken above merely points to the crucial gate of the qi sea, yet the visions therein are manifold, beyond full recounting. Ten thousand words, a thousand teachings—all the scriptures of the Three Teachings, all the works of the Hundred Schools, filling ox-carts to the rafters—none but serve the single method of cultivating the heart-mind. Remember this, Lazy One.

Good fortune is not cause for delight; ill fortune is not cause for sorrow. All such favorable or unfavorable visions, though seeming real, are but illusions. When they arise, let the heart remain unmoved, the thoughts unshaken, the conduct unobstructed. The apparitions that manifest are never beyond two kinds: astonishment and joy. Yet within them, transformations and illusions often exceed all expectation. The unchanging principle is to remain unmoved. You must recognize them all as demonic illusions or as trials sent by the perfected ones above. Only by refusing to be swayed by demons can a person reveal their original true face.

Thus, whenever demonic disturbances arise, you should redouble your resolve and redouble your courage. Ah, Lazy One! Lazy One! The reason I cry out so urgently is that the demonic and the true cannot coexist, yet they always appear side by side. Why? Without demons, the Way cannot be revealed; if demons do not retreat, the Way cannot be accomplished. Strive on, Lazy One!

*(Xie’s note: Gains and losses are ever as ordinary—attend only to your cultivation, not to the harvest! This is most crucial!)*

Lazy Master says: The brain is called the Sea of Marrow—its principle is manifest and clear, requiring no tedious explanation. Yet this single sea, as the world describes its functions, is vast indeed! Most belong to the methods of earthly immortals or ghostly immortals, not the supreme Dao, and must not be followed. What you pursue and I practice is the singular tradition of heavenly immortals, refining to purely return to the primordial for the proper attainment. Thus, one must be cautious in what one refines.

Ah, Lazy One! You must understand the ultimate fruition of heavenly immortals and the pure subtlety of the primordial unified qi—its essence is utterly pure, utterly soft, yet utterly firm and utterly keen, such that not even metal or iron can obstruct it. What it passes through is transformed; what it preserves is spirit. *(Xie’s note: When qi lies hidden, it becomes supremely spiritual; when qi arises and manifests, there is progress and transformation.)* Vast as the cosmos or minute as a speck of dust, when expanded, it can embrace the three thousand great thousand worlds like the sands of the Ganges; when transformed, it can coalesce into countless beings, mountains, waters, palaces, halls, and temples. *(Such realms are not to be feared in attainment, only in attachment to spirit. Why? Once a thought stirs, these realms manifest endlessly, growing ever more wondrous. Once one clings to form, one enters the demonic path—minor attachment leads to demonhood, major attachment to instant death. Among those who cultivate the Dao in the world, many die thus, yet neither they nor their kin and fellow practitioners realize it, often believing they have attained the Dao and departed. The harm is no small matter! Thus, the school of heavenly immortals never regards such phenomena as proof of efficacy, but rather as demonic disturbances. If one sits and such visions appear, one must not attempt to dispel them with intention—doing so only transforms them into battlegrounds, with unpredictable manifestations of conflict and subjugation, inevitably leading to madness and death. Or one may be seized by demons and die, or fall into their snare. If by some chance one prevails in battle, one’s spiritual powers and magical abilities grow without cultivation, and the deluded practitioner takes this as clear proof of Dao attainment. Little do they know they have been lured into the demon’s trap—when their life ends, they merely become part of the asura retinue. Or, if defeated in battle and the spirit departs the body entirely, the shell may be occupied by a demon. Outsiders, unaware, believe the person has attained the Dao, testing their spiritual powers and magical abilities to find them no different from ancient immortals. The demon, possessing the body, practices its demonic ways, gathering followers like clouds. In its teachings, lust, wrath, greed, and deceit are deemed harmless to the true Dao, and those who follow are led into demonic realms, becoming demonic retinues. The leaders of heterodox sects like the White Lotus of past and present often arise from such deluded cultivation, their bodies possessed by demons to form these perverse teachings. This must not be unknown! Therefore, for all who cultivate the Dao, the great secret to subduing demons is to see yet not see, hear yet not hear—so-called, "Though wind and waves rise, I do not set sail." This teaches the crucial secret of not stirring thought. All who refine the Sea of Marrow must take heed!)*

When gathered, it forms shape; when dispersed, it becomes qi. It merges the Three Pure Ones without duality and unites the Three Teachings as one *(this refers to maintaining a single, clear, and unattached thought, allowing all existence and non-existence, blue and yellow, red and white to be as they are. Scholars, beware of clinging to gathering and dispersing, merging and uniting, or forms and colors)*. This is the ultimate fruition of heavenly immortals and the wondrous function of the primordial unified qi. Those of us with aspiration can surely attain it—this is no delusion, but the nature of resolve. As the ancient immortals said: "To learn immortality, one must learn heavenly immortality; only the Golden Elixir is most authentic." Thus, resolve must be firmly established!

How to refine this Sea of Marrow? Above, it connects with heaven; below, it penetrates the earth’s bounds. In the four directions and four cardinal points, it is boundless and infinite, its aspect serene and still. No mountains, rivers, or cities exist—only a radiant golden world and a luminous moon hanging in the sky. *(Xie’s note: This scene is the true image of the exact noon hour.)* This is the secret to beginning. If visions of jade terraces, jeweled chambers, the Ten Continents, or Three Islands appear, do not regard them *(this is the secret of "supreme virtue acting without action" and "having yet not having")*. Even if iron enclosures, impassable barriers, blade mountains, sword trees, or seas of flame and boiling pools arise, do not examine them *(this is the secret of not seeking through scrutiny)*. Only maintain a single, unattachable right thought and eliminate the stirring mind—this is the essential secret to mastering the Sea of Marrow.

As for the Valley Sea’s barrier, its refinement method is this: only use your hands to rub the abdomen, aiding your yang qi to dissolve and transform. Thus, the ancients, after eating, would first use one hand to rub from the middle of the stomach to the abdomen, walking slowly for about a hundred steps. Then, with their hand on the abdomen, they would move in circles as if polishing a mirror, from inside to outside, walking about three hundred steps. If the left hand tired, they would switch to the right. Then, they would quietly observe the qi mechanism until it flowed smoothly before stopping. Later, when finding leisure to sit, they would continue by closing their eyes, calming the mind, and visualizing the spirit in the Crimson Palace—thus, the qi of the central palace could transform into blood and reach the kidneys. Practicing this method ensures no harm from fluids transforming into phlegm or essence into yin. Though it seems an active practice, it is truly an aid to non-action *(this is the method of "inferior virtue acting with ceaseless function")*.

Lazy One, take note! Do not dismiss this as a minor practice—this is precisely my teacher’s secret method for preemptively refining yin essence. It is also extremely simple.

Lazy One rose and bowed, saying: "Understood!"

Having reverently received the teaching, Lazy One straightened his robes and cap, then spoke with utmost sincerity: "I have heard that if the Mysterious Pass remains unopened, the Sacred Embryo will not form; if postnatal nurturing is improper, the Sacred Infant will suffer inner affliction; if the transference of the immortal fetus is not conducted according to the Dao, the True Person will meet an early end. Fearing these, I humbly seek your instruction: for one such as myself, may the Mysterious Pass fortunately open? May the Sacred Embryo fortunately take shape?"

Hearing this, Lazy Old Man smiled warmly and leaned forward, saying: "You are mistaken—or perhaps you speak of your own experience? Your Mysterious Pass has already swung wide open on the previous night. *(As mentioned in the 'lower section,' this was precisely the clear sign of your Pass opening afterward.)* As for whether the Embryo has formed, you must ask yourself: Do you feel unobstructed throughout your entire body? Have you experienced the misty, billowing qi phenomenon? Have you attained the state where self and other dissolve into oblivion? *(These are all essential practices—only through diligence can they be achieved.)*"

Lazy One replied: "I have encountered all of these at times. *(To experience them often is most wondrous.)*"

The Old Man asked: "Have you reached the state where the myriad sounds are empty and the solitary spirit stands revealed?"

He answered: "I have glimpsed such moments, yet my regret is that I have not sustained them for long. *(If one could sustain them, the formation of the Embryo would be near.)*"

The Old Man then asked: "What signs have you observed in your Earthly Abdomen?"

Lazy One replied: "Whenever I sit in meditation, I feel threads of true qi descending from the heart in delicate strands. Soon after, I sense an inner vastness suddenly opening—boundless without, infinitesimal within—with all manner of true qi billowing and pouring inward. I feel this space as bottomless, yet warm; now as if fire were present, now as if absent, yet a gentle warmth arises, drifting and rising from the lower region, surging upward in all directions. It ascends directly behind me, thickly reaching the back and crown of the head. Then, I feel a sudden heat descending from below the throat, and upon reaching the Crimson Palace, it abruptly transforms into cool droplets. Passing the heart’s threshold, it suddenly turns into scalding liquid rushing downward, filling the abdomen with fiery warmth. My entire body feels thoroughly unobstructed.

Lazy One said: "If this is so, you are not far from forming the Embryo." He continued: "Great Lazy One, you must understand that the formation of the Heavenly Immortal’s Embryo differs from what is commonly heard. You must carefully study the *Treatise on Dispelling Doubts in Immortal Cultivation*—how to refine, how to form, how to gather, how to tend the firing, how to guard, how to nurture, how to bathe, how to apply, how to subdue, and how to transfer the spirit and change the crucible until liberation is complete. All these are fully described within. The most essential secret lies in thought within no-thought, like a hen brooding her eggs. Sitting upright in meditative absorption is the method of gathering; intermittent focus is the way of guarding; movement, stillness, sitting, and lying are the firing times."

He added: "Diligent yet unguided, you must meet a perfected one; guided yet indolent, you will remain a lowly ghost. Keep these four lines ever in mind as a reminder."

Asked: "Beyond the *Treatise on Dispelling Doubts in Immortal Cultivation*, which books should I study?"

He answered: "*Inquiries in the Crane Forest*, *Revealing the Mysteries of the Mysterious Pass*, *On Nature and Life*, and externally, *The Ancestral Teachings of the Golden Flower*, *The Unity of Immortals and Buddhas*, *The True Principles of Heavenly Immortals*, *The Torch of Doubt*. Further, *The Seal of the Unity of the Three*, *Awakening to Reality*, and in broader scope, *Laozi’s Dao De Jing with Bai’s Commentary*, the *Vajracchedikā*, *Śūraṅgama*, and *Perfect Enlightenment* sutras. Alas! Ancestor Bai said: *'A word or half a phrase may unlock the mystery—what need for ten thousand scrolls of alchemical texts? If one is not burdened by form, the Great Brahma Heaven lies before your eyes.'*"

*(Xie’s note: This compilation may be read alongside *Continuation of Fragmentary Sayings*. The Lazy One herein is Min Yide speaking of himself.)*

*Collected Insights on Women’s Alchemy*
Author: Liu Yiming

The immortal master’s surname was Liu, given name Yiming, style Wuyuanzi, also known as the Unadorned Recluse and the Clad-in-Rough-Cloth Recluse. His ancestral home was Quwo County, Pingyang Prefecture, Shanxi Province (now northeast of Wenxi County, Shanxi). From childhood, he devoted himself to cultivation and refinement, though he did not receive true transmission.

He abandoned a family fortune of ten thousand gold to pursue the Dao. He once wandered through Shaanxi, Sichuan, and Gansu, seeking instruction and visiting masters for many years. Later, he met the Elder of Kan Valley, who distinguished the true from the false, and again encountered the Immortal Liurenzhang, through whom all doubts vanished. Only then did he grasp the secret subtleties of the elixir path.

Thereafter, he secluded himself on Qiyun Mountain and Xinglong Mountain in present-day Yuzhong County, Lanzhou, Gansu Province, where he established altars to transmit the teachings and composed writings. His Daoist works number many; in the early Republican era, they were compiled into a collection titled *Twelve Daoist Books*. In *Collected Insights*, among the verse compositions, the Immortal Master composed a poem on *Women’s Alchemy*:

A thousand scriptures, ten thousand scrolls—all elixir methods complete,
The ancestral masters, in compassion, ferry across the dusty world.
The Great Dao makes no distinction between man and woman,
For yin and yang, the Five Phases, are all the same.
Only the true oral instructions for beginning differ,
Their applications as distant as heaven from the deep.
The sun refines qi—this is the man’s principle,
The moon refines form—the woman’s path and net.
Women find it even easier than men,
In three to five years, they attain immortality.
If I did not now reveal the crucial point,
Where would one board the dharma boat?
First, raise your hand to slay the Red Dragon,
Sever the Red Dragon, and misfortune vanishes.
Heavenly *ren* and earthly *gui* meet face to face,
The yin qi of the sea-bottom spirals up and down.
The Three Corpses and Six Thieves seek to steal the treasure,
The Seven Emotions and Five Aggregates return to the cinnabar field.
Grasp the sharp-edged sword of Moye,
To cultivate the lotus in the mire.
Seize the true unified qi of creation,
Gather the spirit to ascend and descend the waxing and waning moon.
The turbid blood transforms and vanishes without trace,
The two breasts retract to the chest, the trigrams invert.
Though the woman’s form resembles the man’s body,
The foundation remains firm, unchanged.
From here, enter directly the Yang Pass Way,
Choose a numinous site to complete the Great Return.
Within the vast emptiness, establish the crucible,
Where heaven and earth unite to refine the true lead.
Kick over the Eight Trigrams, beyond birth and extinction,
Seal the Three Treasures, cutting off all threads.
The ten directions of the world shrink to a millet grain,
The sands of the Ganges appear as a hair’s tip.
Reduce and reduce again—Dao diminishes daily,
Increase and increase again—merit connects.
Until there is nothing left to reduce or increase,
From non-being guard being, the sacred embryo firms.
In the *mao* and *you* hours, bathe with care,
Following the *Zhun* and *Meng* trigrams, in accord with nature.
The heart must be pure, the mind tranquil and settled,
Water fears drying, fire fears fanning.
The slightest leak spawns transformations,
The medicine in the crucible flees like flying smoke.
Diligently nurture it for ten months,
Then—with a thunderclap—beyond the heavens.
Guard it well, do not let it wander far,
Mature, roam the four seas’ edge.
Only then is the work complete and fulfilled,
As the Queen Mother of the Jasper Pool rides her colored phoenix.
I now compose this *Women’s Alchemy*,
For boudoir heroes to delve into and study.
Burning incense and tending the fire are empty affairs,
Eating vegetarian meals and chanting sutras—mere lip-service.
To speak of returning to the Buddha-land after death
Is like gazing at plums to quench thirst—all vain illusion.
If this body is not liberated in this life,
One cannot escape the pull of evil destinies in the next.
But if one truly turns back and swiftly cultivates realization,
True women of the Dao will be transmitted through the ages.
Should anyone deceive the world with falsehoods,
They will forever sink into hell’s yellow springs.

---

*Woodcutter Yang’s Manual on Women’s Cultivation*
Transmitted by Pure Yang Ancestor Lü
Recorded by Fu Jinquan, the Helper of Unity

Refining form through the Great Yin differs little from the man’s method of cultivation. At the outset, close the eyes and abide in spirit, resting completely to still the heart and regulate the breath. Then concentrate the spirit into the qi cavity (above the heart’s hollow, between the two breasts). Cross the hands to cradle the breasts, gently massaging them twenty times. Draw the qi subtly upward from the lower cinnabar field thirty-six times. Again, use the hands to cradle the breasts, reflecting inward to harmonize the breath. Over time, the true qi will naturally come and go, opening and closing to form the *yin’e*. When spirit and qi are abundant, true yang flourishes of itself, the menstrual flow ceases, and the breasts resemble a man’s—this is called slaying the Red Dragon.

After long practice, there is no need to cradle the breasts or draw the qi; simply concentrate the spirit in the qi cavity, turning the light inward in reflection—this is the Gate of the Mysterious Female. The true breath drifts, emptiness reaches its utmost, stillness its depth. Yang qi steams and rises, the river chariot revolves, myriad purple clouds adorn the jade palace, a thousand blood vessels penetrate the mud-pill. One becomes aware of a single numinous light, neither inside nor outside, ascending from the lower field through the Crimson Palace and mud-pill, descending the heavy tower to return to the golden womb’s divine chamber. Turning the light inward, concentrating the spirit, the true breath rests within the central crucible—this is the spirit entering the chamber, the Mysterious Female, the embryonic immortal, the single point falling into the Yellow Court.

Thereafter, in ten months of effort, the yang spirit manifests, shattering emptiness. The path of true cultivation is the same for men and women, with no distinction between them.

---

*Secret Instructions on Women’s Alchemy*
by Wang Dongting, the Body-of-Truth Recluse

The study of nature and life is the same for men and women, with no difference. In sum, it hinges on the four words: *"utmost sincerity, focused attention."* The Book says: *"Only the utmost sincerity under heaven can transform."* The Classic says: *"Focus the mind to its utmost to heed the mandate."* For beginners, the first crucial step is nothing other than *"refining the self."* Refining the self means the heart and breath depending on each other. This dependence means the heart relies on the breath, and the breath also relies on the heart. But the most important is the word *"harmony."* The *Canon* says: *"Harmony follows."* It also says: *"Each attains its harmony."* Harmony does not depart from the center, the center does not depart from harmony. Are center and harmony one? Or two? Center and harmony united is called the Yellow Dame. When the Yellow Dame harmonizes, love, longing, swallowing, and spitting arise naturally. Continuous, unbroken, neither forgetting nor forcing. Laozi said: *"Can you concentrate your qi to attain suppleness like a newborn babe?"*

"The ultimate attainment of true central harmony." Yu Chan said: *"When the old husband and wife meet, affection lingers naturally."* The *Canon* states: *"Twist into one mass, blend into one place, forge into one sheet, temper in one furnace."* It also says: *"The Oxherd and Weaver Girl meet, yin and yang follow each other, crow and hare share a den, sun and moon share a palace, hun and po unite, metal and fire merge as one."*

When thoroughly realized, it is always spirit not departing from qi, qi not departing from spirit—thus the heart not departing from breath, breath not departing from the heart. Now, spirit is nature; qi is life. The *Canon* says: *"The root of nature lies in the heart; the stem of life lies in the breath."* This is so. One must know that only when the two unite is creation accomplished. For when the two unite, the Two Modes return to the One Supreme Ultimate—this is called *"dual cultivation of nature and life."*

Dual cultivation of nature and life simply teaches one that heart and breath must depend on each other, never for an instant parting. Thus, the White Patriarch said: *"Refining the medicine with fire to form the elixir is none other than guiding qi with spirit to attain the Dao."* Each day in practice, one must hold the heart to the breath and the breath to the heart. After a moment’s duration, once equilibrium is naturally achieved, great stillness arises, and one enters into profound obscurity—dim and indistinct, boundless and formless, forgetting things and forgetting form.

The *Canon* says: *"Growing to complete the father’s body, by the mother the foundation is laid."* It also says: *"Know the white, guard the black, and spirit and brightness will come of themselves."* This is precisely that moment.

It seems as though body and mind awaken with an extraordinary softness and ease. As Sanfeng said: *"Like a mute tasting honey, it cannot be spoken."* Shaozi himself wrote:

*"From the dim and indistinct, yin and yang first transform,
The primal qi of heaven and earth begins its revolving.
Amidst this, a wondrous light appears—
How could one find the words to describe it?"*

The *Canon* says: *"Golden sand enters the five viscera,
Mist scatters like wind and rain.
Steaming and permeating the four limbs,
The complexion becomes joyful and radiant."*

For at this moment, the primordial qi arrives from the midst of emptiness and nothingness. Shaozi said: *"At the midpoint of the winter solstice,
The heart of heaven remains unchanged.
Where the first yang stirs,
Before the myriad things are born."*
This is what the alchemical texts call the *living midnight hour*,
And what Ziyang termed *"When gui arises, hasten to gather."*

Shangyangzi asked: *"What is gathering?"*
He answered: *"Gathering with the gathering that is no-gathering."*
*"And what is the gathering that is no-gathering?"*
*"Splitting open the primordial chaos."*

I explain: *"What is splitting open the primordial chaos?
It is the moment of utmost emptiness and profound stillness."*
For when one attains emptiness to its utmost and guards stillness to its depth, this is returning to Kun.
Now Kun is the southwest—
The land where the medicine is born,
The place of chaos,
The aperture of the Mysterious Female.
Mizi said: *"To seek the true seed of the primordial,
One must find chaos to establish the foundation."*
Zhang Ziyang said: *"To keep the Valley Spirit from ever dying,
One must rely on the Mysterious Female to establish the foundation."*

Ah! Once the foundation is laid, the Valley Spirit does not die.
How then could a person die?

The above concerns refining the self and laying the foundation, gathering the great medicine of the primordial—identical for both men and women in cultivation. Thus it is said: *"The Great Dao makes no distinction between man and woman;
Yin and yang, the Five Phases are all the same."*

What follows speaks of the differences in post-heaven practice.

Liu Wuyuan’s *Women’s Elixir Formula* states: *"There is only one true oral instruction for beginning,
Yet their methods diverge as heaven from the abyss.
Cultivating qi in the Greater Yang—this is the man’s principle.
Cultivating form in the Greater Yin—this is the woman’s path."*

For man is yang, and his number is odd.
The *Classic* says: *"Heaven’s one generates water, and man receives it."*
Thus, he begins his work one *cun* and three *fen* below the navel, in the Kan palace.
Woman is yin, and her number is even.
The *Classic* says: *"Earth’s two generates fire, and woman receives it."*
Thus, she initiates her work between the two breasts, in the Li position.
This is an immutable principle.

What the medical texts call the *"breast stream"* and the alchemical classics term the *"breast chamber"* refers to this very aperture.

Of old, Lüzu transmitted the method to Immortal Zhang, saying:
*"Sit in fixed breathing between midnight and noon,
Pass through the Jiaji Gate and ascend Kunlun.
When you obtain the qi at that moment, think of me."*

He also said:
*"Kan and Li, Zhen and Dui divide midnight and noon.
You must recognize your own ancestral origin.
When the thunder of earth shakes the mountain’s peak, rain falls—
Wait to wash and nurture the yellow sprout as it emerges from the soil.
Seize the golden essence and firmly seal it,
Refining geng and jia to generate dragon and tiger.
When he asks who transmitted this to you,
Simply say the master’s surname is Lü."*

For one must refine the self to perfection before gaining mastery.
And one must daily steal the yang of heaven and earth,
Constantly steaming and bathing in it,
Before seeing any effect.
Whether one or two months, or three or four,
The duration depends on the depth of the practitioner’s effort.

At times during practice, one may suddenly feel qi in the aperture,
Bursting forth and splitting into two paths that surge straight to the breasts,
Penetrating to the nipples, making them firm and erect.
This is what the alchemical texts call the *living midnight hour* when the medicine is born.
Shaozi said:
*"Suddenly, in the dead of night, a clap of thunder—
A thousand doors in ten thousand households open in succession.
If you recognize the image hidden within the formless,
You may meet Fuxi himself."*

When the work reaches this point, the hundred vessels harmonize,
All gates and apertures open,
And truly, one’s whole being brims with spring.

Now *"between midnight and noon"* refers to the purest moment between *hai* and *zi*.
*"Fixed breathing"* means regulating the breath to evenness.
*"Sitting"* means the two (yin and yang) divide left and right,
As one must deploy them like left and right armies.
One earth stands at the center,
For both sides harbor the true earth.
When the true earth returns to the center, the qi flows unimpeded.
Thus, *"passing through the Jiaji Gate and ascending Kunlun"* is precisely the moment when the Yellow River’s current turns and a single channel opens.

*"When you obtain the qi at that moment, think of me"*—
*"Me"* is a metaphor for the pure yang qi,
And also for the perfected Taiyi Golden Immortal,
That is, the Taiyi containing the true qi.

*"Kan and Li, Zhen and Dui divide midnight and noon"*—
First, one establishes the four cardinal positions of Kan, Li, Zhen, and Dui,
Then distinguishes the four seasonal phases of *zi*, *wu*, *mao*, and *you*.
*"Recognize your own ancestral origin"* means to trace back to the moment of receiving the qi at birth,
To recognize that first speck of ancestral qi of the primordial.

*"When the thunder of earth shakes the mountain’s peak, rain falls"*—
This is the white clouds ascending to the celestial gate,
The sweet dew sprinkling the empty vastness.

*"Wait to wash and nurture the yellow sprout as it emerges from the soil"*—
*"Wait"* means to await the proper time.
*"Wash and nurture"* refers to bathing, purifying the heart, refining the self, and steaming.
*"Yellow"* is the color of earth.
*"Sprout"* is the mechanism of growth.
*"Emerging from the soil"* is a metaphor for the renewal of all things in the three springs—
The mountains, rivers, and great earth all take on a fresh hue.

At this moment, the yang qi connects with heaven,
The form blazes like fire,
The state resembles a scorching wind.
Swiftly gather it and send it into the Central Palace.
Thus it is said: *"Seize the golden essence and firmly seal it."*
Sanfeng said: *"Seize the golden essence and carefully guide it,
Send it into the Elixir Field to refine geng and jia."*

*"To generate dragon and tiger"* means that geng must generate jia,
And jia must generate geng—
This is the first stirring of the Dao.

*"When he asks who transmitted this to you,
Simply say the master’s surname is Lü."*
*"Lü"* implies mouth to mouth, aperture to aperture—
This is the heart-to-heart transmission,
The oral transmission of the golden elixir’s wondrous formula.

In essence, this teaching instructs one to guide the fire, urging the golden dragon to circulate through the *Zhoutian*, embodying the rising and descending of the *qi* of the Two Mysteries—Dragon and Tiger—through ceaseless diligent practice.

Ancestor Sanfeng said:
*"Wait until that single drop naturally submits,
Within the body, it transforms into the four seasons of spring.
A wisp of white cloud, a waft of fragrance,
After each rain, everything is renewed.
All day in a daze, like a drunken man,
Leisurely guarding the spring within the cave.
When all yin essence throughout the body is stripped away,
It becomes a single mass of pure yang gold."*
Such is the way.

From this point onward, the practice aligns with that of men. Among the secrets of the female true elixir, this method is the most direct path. The Patriarch Lü did not greedily reveal the Great Treasure in a single day, yet alas, people fail to recognize it. Now I have explained it clearly: the point one *cun* and three *fen* below the navel and the cavity between the two breasts are both real. Yet one must not seek them through form.

As the scriptures say:
*"Clinging to this body is not the Dao,
Departing from this body is also in error."*
And:
*"The entire body, inside and out, is yin."*
And:
*"Gazing before your eyes, you fail to recognize the true."*
Moreover, the layers and fire phases within are subtle and refined; one must receive the oral transmission and heart-to-heart instruction from a true master to grasp them with intention. Only then can one begin.

Master Shangyang said:
*"How can oral secrets be made clear on paper?"*
Do not force guesses or grope blindly, lest you mislead yourself.

With long and persistent practice, the yang *qi* will naturally arise, and the entire body will become extraordinarily robust—far surpassing the joys of gold, jade, wealth, or the pleasures of spouse and children. Even if a slight stirring of yang occurs, it must still be gathered and returned to the furnace. One must not descend to idle chatter or external affairs, so that through daily accumulation and monthly refinement, great efficacy may be achieved.

*Illustrated Explanation of Female Practice: Refining the Self and Returning the Elixir*
By Er’e Mountain Man

The Sage Master said:
*"Women, being of greater yin, first refine the form."*
At the outset of practice, the intention must dwell in the breasts, whether walking, standing, sitting, or lying down—always thus. After forty-nine days of practice, whether walking, standing, sitting, or lying down, the intention should guard the *Zhongji* (*Zhongji* being the cavity below the heart and above the *Blood Sea*, a suspended void at the center).

When walking or standing, silently guide the *qi* to the *Tianting*; when sitting or lying down, guard the *Zhongji* and *Blood Sea* with intention, like a hen brooding her eggs—no thoughts arising, all distractions absent. However, in this practice, before the true yin stirs and the meridians open, one may often feel drowsy. Thus, one must perform the exercise of *"pointing the brain downward."*

What is *"pointing the brain downward"*? It is the practice of *"turning the light around"*:
With the eyes gazing at the nose, fix the *Magpie Bridge*, descend through the *Xuan Ying*, pass the *Weighty Tower*, return to the *Zhongji*, and enter the *Blood Sea*—water meeting fire. After a moment of drowsiness, one will awaken (this is the method of regulating the medicine and refining the heart). If stray thoughts arise, return to guarding the *Zhongji*.

For young women practicing to a hundred days, undisturbed by external influences, the *Blood Sea* will naturally surge, and the true yin will stir (this stirring is not of body or mind but of the blood and *qi* rising like a tide, an indescribable yet blissful sensation—arising spontaneously from thoughtlessness. At this moment, one must not entertain thoughts, for thoughts will scatter it. Only by firmly holding the original spirit and employing the method of gathering can one proceed).

This is the arising of the *lesser medicine*, and the method of gathering must be applied two or three times (until the mechanism ceases). Then return to guarding the *Zhongji*.

The method of gathering:
With the eyes gazing at the nose, cross the *Magpie Bridge*, descend through the *Xuan Ying*, pass the *Weighty Tower*, enter the breasts, roam the *Zhongji*, return to the *Blood Sea*, part the waters, penetrate the *Jade Pillow*, ascend to the *Hundred Meetings*, descend through the *Muddy Pellet*, enter the *Bright Hall*, and finally return to the *Zhongji* and *Blood Sea*. Firmly guard the *Zhongji* and *Blood Sea* with true intention, entering stillness and samadhi.

If yin arises again, repeat the gathering method until the mechanism ceases, then return to guarding the *Zhongji* and *Blood Sea*.

In this practice, one must abstain from violent anger, wind, cold, heat, dampness, raw or cold fruits, and fried or baked foods. One must be vigilant, for if wind or cold enters the orifices, the medicine will be difficult to cure. All worldly concerns must be relinquished, and not a speck of dust should cling.

If one adheres to this method, the *qi* of true yin may stir two or three times in a single day.
*(This stirring must be discerned as true or false: there is the stirring of the *qi* mechanism, and the stirring of thoughts and desires. Only when it arises spontaneously from thoughtlessness, desirelessness, and intentionlessness can it be considered the true stirring of yin.)*

After one hundred and seven days, the blood will be entirely transformed into *qi*, the *Red Dragon* will be severed, and the body will become *qian*-like. The foundation is thus established—how could the returning elixir be difficult to achieve?

*(Note: Many female elixir texts claim that women must cease practice upon the arrival of the monthly flow, but this is erroneous, arising from a lack of clarity. The essence of female practice lies in the *qi* mechanism, yet there is a distinction between *ren* and *gui*. When *ren* water first arrives but *gui* has not, this is the onset of the flow. One will naturally sense it—perhaps with dizziness or lumbar pain. When the flow arrives but the tide has not, this is the time to turn the light around, silently guard the breasts and *Blood Sea*, and employ the gathering method to replenish the brain and build the foundation. What is gathered is *ren* water, not *gui* water. When *gui* water arrives, one should cease practice. After thirty *shi chen* (two and a half days), when *gui* is exhausted, resume the gathering method. How many days one gathers depends on profound oral secrets, which must be sought through a true master’s heart-to-heart transmission—do not guess blindly. If one receives proper instruction, even a young woman may establish her foundation in a hundred days.)*

Upon reaching this stage of practice, verification will naturally occur: the *Red Dragon* will be severed, the nipples will retract like those of a man, and the *qi* of true yin will transform into true yang.

At this stage, one must have a Dao companion of shared purpose for mutual support. When the true vision arrives, gather the *lesser medicine* and pass the barriers (the passage of the *lesser medicine* also manifests signs). Once the foundation is established and the medicine is produced, a fire-pearl will surge in the *Cinnabar Field*, the *Blood Sea* will boil like scalding soup, the nose will twitch, and the body will tremble—do not be alarmed. Here, too, there are oral secrets; only with a master’s guidance can danger be averted, lest the true fire become ordinary fire, risking either bodily immolation or madness.

For those who receive a true master’s transmission, once the medicine enters the crucible, one must know the method of refining it (the method awaits the master’s oral instruction). Without knowledge of the refining method, the medicine cannot congeal into the elixir, and what is gained will surely be lost. Since this is called the *lesser medicine*, one should employ the *lesser celestial cycle* of firing (the *lesser cycle* also has its oral secrets), advancing the *yang fire* and withdrawing the *yin tally* to temper it (the tally and fire have their proper timing and measures). Refine it until a full month’s cycle of the *lesser celestial* is complete. Whether the medicine is genuine or false, whether the elixir has formed, will naturally be verified. If the *lesser elixir* has indeed congealed, whenever one enters seclusion to sit in meditation, the entire body will radiate heat like steam from a steamer. One should silently guard the *Central Palace*, refrain from speech, and allow the transformations to unfold. In an instant, a fire-pearl the size of a bean will shoot from the *Hall of Light* to a height of over a *zhang*, flashing like lightning—this is the true realm of foundation established and medicine obtained.

At this time, though there are secret methods for refining the medicine, one must maintain a mind free of thoughts, with the five aggregates emptied. Even if the heavens overturn and the earth splits, thunder roars and lightning strikes, one should steadfastly seat the original spirit in the *Central Palace*, utterly fearless, like a hen brooding her eggs or a dragon guarding its pearl. When it is time to advance the fire, advance it; when it is time to withdraw the tally, withdraw it (advancing the fire and withdrawing the tally have their proper timing and measures). One must refine until reaching profound stillness and deep stability, with *qi* abundant and spirit complete, the fire-pearl no longer appearing, and the *lesser elixir* fully congealed.

These are the three layers of oral secrets: establishing the foundation, obtaining the medicine, and congealing the elixir. Beyond this lie four further layers, but the celestial mechanism cannot be fully disclosed at once—all immortals throughout history have transmitted their teachings in this manner. If one’s practice and conduct reach this point, the fruition of *human immortality* is attained! Thereafter, the method of practice is no different from that of men. However, as women belong to the tranquil body, though the latter four layers share the same operations as the male elixir, their progress will be even swifter!

**True Master’s Final Remarks:**
Widows, chaste maidens, and women of steadfast virtue—those who establish true and unwavering resolve, remain constant to the end, withstand demonic obstacles without retreat, endure to the point of death without wavering, remain unmoved by wealth or poverty, and maintain unshakable fidelity—may be taught these three layers of wondrous methods. Proceeding step by step, they will be invisibly protected by celestial immortals, and no inner or outer demons will dare disturb them, ultimately ensuring great accomplishment. As for married women, whose worldly affairs remain unresolved, this must not be rashly transmitted. It is only fitting to advise them to cultivate their nature, restrain desire, honor their mothers-in-law, and respect their husbands, awaiting the proper time for transmission. If one carelessly imparts these teachings without due caution, there will indeed be consequences. There is not a word of falsehood or reckless speculation here—this is truly a celestial mechanism that must not be lightly disclosed. Those who receive this transmission do so by virtue of past karmic affinity. Guard it well and treasure it.

*"Noon is the root of yin, midnight the sprout of yang.
Men possess yang externally and yin internally; women possess yin externally and yang internally.
Men seize external yang to ignite the inner elixir; women seize internal yin to ignite the outer elixir."*

In women’s practice, the first priority is to understand how to gather the yin within the body to replenish the yang within. Yang is essence and *qi*; yin is spirit and blood.

When is the time for gathering? Know that it is the moment when the monthly flow is about to arrive and when it has just ceased. What is this "flow"? It is like a traveler who has not yet returned, yet word of his coming arrives first. At the time when the signal arrives but the flow has not yet come, hasten to practice—either in full lotus or in Avalokiteśvara’s half-lotus—awaiting the stirring of spirit and *qi* within the body. Turn the light inward to illuminate the breast cavity and the Sea of Blood. Regulate the breath through the nose until even. Then, using true intention (that is, the Yellow Dame), guide the stirred spirit and *qi* from the Sea of Blood upward along the Caoxi pathway, straight to the fontanel, then descend from above to the breasts, and finally return to the Central Pole.

This method must not be used carelessly (it may be employed when the signal has come but the flow has not yet arrived, or after the flow has ceased for a day and a half). If one rashly gathers before the flow has fully ended, it will surely lead to mortal harm. Remember this well.

For young women whose blood and *qi* are abundant and whose minds are tranquil, three months of practice will suffice to sever the Red Dragon and restore the body to youth, the complexion like peach blossoms. When the practice reaches this stage, one will resemble a drunken person—dazed and silent—with a radiance that persists day and night, unscattered. After a year of steadfast practice, the foundation will be firmly established, and the work of becoming a Human Immortal will be verified.

For middle-aged women, cultivation requires the method of refining the form through the Great Yin. Those who practice this must eliminate thoughts and desires, forget emotions and worries, and only then proceed. Calculate the exact day and hour when the monthly flow is due. Two or three days before its arrival, begin quiet nurturing. When the signal comes, sit upright in a quiet chamber, hands resting on the knees, the index fingers forming a *zi-wu* mudra. Close the eyes, gather the spirit, regulate the breath, and inwardly observe, directing the gaze from the breasts to the Sea of Blood. Wait until the true yin *qi* stirs, then proceed with the refining practice.

In this stage, one must distinguish between true and false, pure and turbid. If one refines false yin or turbid *qi*, illness will surely follow, and no medicine will avail. When true yin stirs, the entire body will feel soft as cotton, resembling a drunken state. At this moment, the Sea of Blood will seem like a fish gulping water—its joy indescribable. This is the true realm of true yin’s manifestation.

Once this scene appears, use true intention to guide the *qi* past the Jiaji, up the Jade Pillow, through the Muddy Pellet, across the Magpie Bridge, down the Double Towers, into the breasts, and finally return to the Central Pole and the Sea of Blood.

If the body is weak and the *qi* feeble, and after two or three months true yin shows no sign of stirring, one may resort to deliberate effort: first knead the right breast twelve times, then the left breast twelve times, rub the navel and abdomen thirty-six times, and swallow saliva three times. After swallowing, resume the inward illumination as before, maintaining extreme emptiness and profound stillness. Practicing thus at the *zi* and *wu* hours daily without fail, within a month signs of stirring will appear, and gathering and refining may begin.

When true yin is entirely transformed into yang *qi*, the nipples retract, the Red Dragon is severed, and the body becomes masculine—then the work of refining the form through true yin is complete.

A poem says:
*"The face like peach blossoms, the skin like snow,
At this stage, the Red Dragon is forever cut off.
The pure Dharma-body is originally without dust;
When the work is complete, one ascends to the Jade Palace."*

Once the elixir foundation is laid, the Returned Elixir may be anticipated. With the Red Dragon severed, yin blood is wholly transformed. Yang *qi* cannot long abide in the Sea of Blood within the Cinnabar Field; it must pass through the barriers to become the Dharma-body. At this time, the body grows hot as fire, and *qi* surges like pearls. Then one employs the work of the Returned Elixir, which is no different from that of men.

When the elixir returns to the ancestral aperture of the Cinnabar Field, one proceeds with the work of refining the medicine through the Microcosmic Orbit. The Mysterious Pass is the ancestral aperture of the myriad spirits and *qi*; within it, the primordial ancestral *qi* gathers and congeals. One should breathe softly and continuously, focusing the intention without distraction. The two *qi* will naturally merge, the eight vessels will naturally flow, and the immortal embryo will naturally form.

Proceeding to the next stage, after three years of refining the self, the Great Return is achieved, and the sacred embryo is formed. When the immortal embryo is complete and the ten-month firing process is fulfilled, the infant will manifest. One may hear the sounds of strings and flutes, or see light in a dark room. Future events, the thoughts of others—nothing will be hidden, and all will be known upon encounter.

At this point, one may cultivate a body beyond the body. Whatever visions arise, do not cling to them, nor fear them. Simply maintain single-mindedness at the center. After nine years of facing the wall, when yin is exhausted and yang is pure, form and spirit will both be perfected, merging with the Dao in truth. Awaiting the imperial summons to ascend, one becomes an eternal attendant of the Queen Mother, liberated from the wheel of worldly rebirth.

Consider: a few years of effort yield boundless joy for eons. Why should women of this world hesitate to undertake this?

Lüzu says:
*"How laughable are those in the world who study the Dao,
Debating heaven and earth, discoursing on cultivation.
Ignorant of the wondrous celestial mechanism,
Unclear on the three families’ medicinal substances.
Without refining the true transformation within the furnace,
One cannot escape suffering and sinking in the bitter sea.
I now transmit to you the principles of the Three Teachings,
Revealing the wondrous work of cultivation.
First speak of astronomy and geography—
The Three Powers of heaven and earth must be mastered.
Men cultivate by taming the White Tiger;
Women cultivate by severing the Red Dragon.
Heaven and earth circulate through measured degrees;
Sun and moon revolve in their transformative work.
Five thousand four hundred and eight return to the Yellow Way,
Where metal, wood, water, and fire meet in turn.
Women are originally bodies of Great Yin—
Know the wondrous work of Great Yin’s transformation.
Each day it moves thirteen degrees to the right;
After two and a half days, it enters a new palace.
In a month, it completes a full celestial circuit—
Women’s qi and seasons follow the same pattern."*

To know the true oral formula of the Golden Elixir,
Heaven and humanity’s transformations are fundamentally interconnected.
Grasp the wondrous subtleties within,
And scrutinize the dark, new, crescent, and full moons with care.
The mechanism of the monthly cycle first stirs—
After two and a half days, the work begins in earnest.
If one comprehends the marvel of heaven’s mechanism,
How can the woman’s practice fail to be exquisitely refined?

There is yet another segment of the true Golden Elixir formula,
To be discussed in detail with the immortals.
Hang the Seven-Star Precious Sword in the southwest,
And beneath the Twin Trees, revolve the wheel.
In the dish, precious pearls appear in pairs,
A single white ox pierces through Kunlun.
At the hundred-foot pole, hastily let go,
Riding the ox to chase the moon, accompanied by an old monk.
Again, strike the golden bell of the Shadowless Temple,
Where water in the sixth month turns to ice.
The stringless zither plays the *Three Refrains*,
The holeless flute sounds the *Eight Tones*.
The Wood Mother runs as a wooden horse,
The Metal Duke follows the Golden Crow in flight.
The two overturn rivers and upend seas,
Soon ascending the Pavilion of Lofty Peaks.
A single drop of true sweet dew is sprinkled,
And suddenly, the seven apertures radiate light.
At this step, press forward with each step,
Never allowing disturbance or procrastination.
Wait for that single drop to return to the vessel,
Where the two and five congeal, becoming perfectly luminous.

If one asks who composed this song,
It was passed down by two mouths to deliver the female immortals.
Within it, all wondrous principles are fully encompassed—
Do not fail to heed my earnest admonitions.

**The Ten Principles of the Correct Path for Women’s Cultivation by the Queen Mother of the West**
**Preface to the Correct Path for Women’s Cultivation**

The Pure Yang Master vowed to ferry all beings, having already composed the *Annotations on the Nine Emperors’ Elixir Canon* as a bridge for men’s immortal cultivation. Yet he could not bear to witness women of latent roots and innate Daoist aspirations deprived of true transmission, straying onto false paths and sinking into ghostly realms. Thus, on the first day of the first month of winter in the *jiwei* year, at the Radiant Splendor Tower, moved by the Non-Dual Immortal Maiden, he sincerely expounded the true transmission orally bestowed by the Queen Mother of the West upon Lady Wei Huacun, originally titled *The Great Golden Elixir Formula for Women*. He revised it into *Nine Principles of the Correct Path for Women’s Cultivation*, still prefacing it with the Queen Mother’s name, and requested the proclamation of the *Nine Precepts for Female Immortals* to rectify Daoist mores. Together, they form ten principles, all to be reverently received under the compassionate decree. Yet what is most precious is the ability to personally embody them.

The Immortal Maiden exhorted: the Dao’s application is boundless, yet its foundation begins with these ten principles. Thus, this preface.

The Non-Dual Primordial Sovereign Sun Zhenyi said: Are there truly no *Elixir Books for Female Immortals* in the world? Most are muddled with distorted theories, leading deluded followers to fabricate and attach falsehoods, deceiving themselves and others. Some even guide others into the realm of spirits, spreading calamity without end. The Dao’s Ancestor, in his profound magnanimity, lamented only their descent into ghostly realms. I have long grieved over this! Fortunate to receive the Dao’s Ancestor’s commission to edit and revise, I have thus refined it. Following the original text of the *Great Golden Elixir Formula for Women* by the Queen Mother of the West and incorporating the *Mysterious Shadow of the Great Dao* orally transmitted by the Jade Purity Divine Mother, I compiled nine principles and presented them for scrutiny. The Dao is not meant to remain forever hidden, and I was graciously permitted to revise it. Entitled *The Correct Path for Women’s Cultivation by the Queen Mother of the West*, it is prefaced with the *Nine Precepts for Female Immortals*, forming ten principles in total. I further requested the elucidation of its profound secrets, so that women cultivating the Dao—though the Earthly Way achieves no completion yet fulfills its end—may know the great Dao of assisting in transformation and nurturing life, and may personally embody and diligently practice it. All are to reverently receive this under the compassionate decree. Henceforth, the lineage of female immortals will not only avoid straying onto false paths but will also easily ascend to the celestial gates. The proper course of the Dao is to be vigorously revitalized. With reverent joy, I bow and inscribe this preface at the Radiant Splendor Tower in Wulin, to mark this felicitous occasion.

The Orthodox Daoist Descendant of the Complete Truth Tradition, Sun Zhenyi, bows a hundred times and respectfully writes this preface.

**Revised and Retitled by the Patriarch Lü**
**Supplemented and Narrated by the Primordial Sovereign Sun**
**Transmitted by the Grand Master Shen of the Great Void**
**Annotated by Disciple Min Yide**

**First Principle: The Nine Precepts**

It is said: For women’s cultivation, the Nine Precepts must be received. The precepts state: Perseverance in practice yields great benefit; when the precepts’ fruits are perfected, one avoids the suffering of hell, is born into a family of the ten virtues, has one’s name inscribed in the Purple Palace, and ranks among the immortals. Now, in proclaiming the *Correct Path for Women’s Cultivation*, the *Nine Precepts* shall serve as the first principle. The text reads:

Be filial, respectful, gentle, and harmonious; speak cautiously and without jealousy.
Maintain chastity and tranquility in body, distancing oneself from all impure conduct.
Cherish all living beings, practicing compassion and refraining from killing.
Be diligent and cautious in rituals and recitations, abstaining from meat and wine.
Wear plain and simple clothing, avoiding ornate adornments.
Regulate and nurture one’s nature and emotions, preventing the arising of afflictions.
Do not frequently attend vegetarian feasts.
Do not cruelly employ servants.
Do not conceal goodness or broadcast evil.

Only by observing these Nine Precepts may one receive and uphold the correct path. For what is proclaimed here is most precious and noble. To transmit or receive it without precepts is to profane the celestial treasure. Both the giver and receiver shall be equally punished—be cautious and vigilant.

The Second Precept: *Root of Life*

If it is said: The second precept for women on the correct path is titled *"Root of Life."* Women, being of yin essence and resembling the moon, at the ages of thirteen, fourteen, or fifteen, possess abundant primordial *qi* and full true blood. Within yin there exists a single yang, and the moon’s radiance is at its brightest. Yet when *heavenly gui* descends, the primordial *qi* is broken, and true blood is drained. After marriage, should they bear sons or daughters, the primordial *qi* gradually depletes, and true blood steadily wanes. Though the monthly *water of fidelity* renews each month, it is also harmed each month.

<*Xie’s Annotation:* *Heavenly gui* marks the moment when yang reaches its peak and yin arises—this yin being impure yin. The arrival of *heavenly gui* knows no distinction between male and female, nor even among all living species, for all possess the "fidelity" of *heavenly gui.* *Heavenly gui* is the unified whole, the undifferentiated primordial state. The moment this whole is "broken" is called *heavenly gui.* Thus, the Dao of internal alchemy lies in returning to this state, preserving the harmony of the center. For women cultivating the elixir, severing the *Red Dragon* follows this principle.>

The difficulty of women’s cultivation lies precisely here. To preserve life and return to the origin, a woman must seek the method of cultivation. With the method, success comes swiftly. This is titled *"Root of Life"* because a woman’s life remains bound to *heavenly gui.* If *heavenly gui* is not transformed, how can life be preserved? Without this transformation, there is no return to the origin—hence the preciousness of the cultivation method.
