Thus, the *"Nine Precepts"* form the first precept, while *"Root of Life"* is the second, embodying the principle of *first nature, then life.* Following this precept, the next is titled *"Origin of Nature,"* for the cultivation of nature is precisely for the preservation of life.

<*Editor’s Note:* The entire text, with the first precept composed by Lü Dongbin, was later revised and compiled by the Non-Dual Primordial Sovereign. Lü Dongbin further refined it to ensure clarity, fearing that ornate language might obscure meaning and mislead later generations. Readers must not dismiss the text as unrefined and doubt its divine authorship. As for the tenth precept, it was entirely composed by Lü Dongbin, expanding upon the principles established thereafter.>

The Third Precept: *Origin of Nature*

The Third Precept: *Origin of Nature*
If it is said that the third precept of the proper path for women’s cultivation is titled *"Origin of Nature,"* this speaks to the nature of women: they are of water-nature and flower-essence. When young and their awareness has awakened, they must discipline themselves, refrain from frivolous play, and guard against reckless movement. At this time, there naturally resides within the inner *yin* a speck of initial essence—like a star, like a pearl—this being the primordial chamber of the utmost, concealed above the *Kun*-womb, positioned within the Central Yellow. If a woman at this time knows to purify her nature, refrains from viewing lewd plays or hearing lewd words, maintains serene conduct, moves in accordance with inner principles, and in stillness remains composed, then this single entity will adhere to the celestial nature, becoming the primordial unity, the unchanging crimson pearl, the untransformed celestial water. Yet how few worldly women possess such knowledge! In their childlike nature, they delight in movement—whether in play or in running and leaping—unaware that their *qi* stirs, their heart sways, their spirit becomes internally disordered, and their true *jing* is unsettled. Then this star-like celestial treasure naturally melts away, its heat like fire, bursting through the gate and shattering the door to descend—what the world calls *tian gui*. From this point onward, even if she guards her chastity and remains unmarried, she is still but an ordinary woman. There is no other reason for this but her failure to recognize the *"Origin of Nature."* If she aspires to return to cultivation, she must begin from the foundation below.

[Editor’s Note: The *inner yin* refers to the *yin* gate. Below, there is also the *spring gate*, likewise called the *yin* gate, hence the gate of the Central Yellow is termed the *inner yin*. Further note: The initial essence, the treasure of life, if one does not know to cultivate it, will adhere to the celestial nature and transform into primordial unity. Ancient sagely women practiced this—Bodhisattva Guanyin and the Heavenly Consort are clear examples. Though the world is not lacking in wise women, alas! They lack immortal parents within and sagely teachers without, leading to a thousand wisdoms and a thousand falls.]

[Commentary by Xie: Before the arrival of the monthly flow, the essence-*qi* is the primordial undifferentiated unity, concealed within the "center" of the Yellow Path. Though this essence-*qi* is the yang of growth and possesses a nature of dispersion, the cycle has not yet arrived, and consciousness has not taken flight, so the essence-*qi* does not leak—this is called maidenly purity. At this stage of cultivation, there is no need for foundational work; one may proceed directly to transforming spirit and returning to emptiness, achieving the elixir and attaining the Dao in a single step. This is called the *qingjing* (pure stillness) cultivation of nature, where *qi* is transformed into spirit, and spirit into *qi*.]

The Fourth Precept: *Cultivating the Menses*
If it is said that the fourth precept of the proper path for women’s cultivation is titled *"Cultivating the Menses,"* this speaks to the fact that once a woman’s *tian gui* has descended, her true *qi* has been broken, and her true blood has been depleted, if she does not engage in cultivating the menses, her true blood will diminish day by day, and her true *jing* will wane. Even if she wishes to cultivate diligently, what benefit can there be? The *Canon of the Elixir* states: *"When bamboo is broken, it must be mended with bamboo."* What is the method? *"For those who still have their monthly flow, first sever the Red Dragon; for those who no longer have it, they must first restore it before severing it again."*

[Commentary by Xie: True blood is true *yin* primordial essence, called *divine water* in the elixir texts. In the postnatal realm, true *qi* is the single speck of true yang within true blood; in the prenatal realm, true blood is the wondrous function of true *qi*—the *"one encircling nurturing yin."*]

[Further note: In the elderly, *yin* is abundant and *yang* is scarce, true *jing* is exhausted, so the priority is to supplement *qi*. When *qi* is sufficient, the menses will naturally return, and the foundation for supplementing blood will be established. In the young, *qi* is abundant, so the priority should be to supplement true *yin*.]

In all cases, the initial practice employs the method of the *zhou tian* (microcosmic orbit). At the *zi* and *wu* hours, sit astride as if riding a crane, release all concerns, and knock the teeth seventy-two times to open the *fei shu* (lung transport) points. Then, using both nostrils, gently inhale and exhale thirty-six times to circulate the blood and vessels throughout the body. At this time, fearing that *jing* may leak downward, one must sit firmly, not allowing any slack. Place both hands below the navel and above the gate, directing *yi* (intent) backward and upward, circulating for approximately thirty-six breaths. Next, raise both hands as if supporting the heavens, ensuring that *yi* remains at the *wei lü* (tailbone), guiding *qi* backward and upward, continuing for about thirty-six breaths. Then perform slow lifts thirty-six times and rapid lifts thirty-six times, until one feels the *qi* at the tailbone stirring, with a surging upward momentum. After this, lower the hands and place them on the waist, vigorously raising both shoulders thirty-six times, until one feels the *qi* at the *jiaji* (spine) gate and *fei shu* points stirring and ascending. If there is any blockage, clench the teeth tightly, focus *yi* on the back of the neck, and lift straight upward thirty-six times, until one feels the *yu zhen* (jade pillow) and *ni wan* (mud pill) open. Only then, cover the upper lip with the lower lip, applying gentle pressure, so that the *qi* from *ni wan* descends to the lower part of the nose. At this time, simply rest the tongue on the *heavenly bridge* without force, focusing *yi* on the point where the tongue rests, and the sweet dew will naturally descend. Then, slightly contract the nose [Commentary by Xie: Focus *yi* on the *shan gen* (mountain root), otherwise the *qi* may scatter], and direct the dew downward with *yi*, swallowing it straight to the *jiang que* (crimson palace). Retain it there for a moment, then guide it backward with *yi*, splitting it left and right to the waist, each side rotating thirty-six times. Next, guide it with *yi* to the navel wheel, rotating left thirty-six times and right thirty-six times, until one feels the entire abdomen unobstructed. At this time, place both hands below the navel and above the gate. Direct *yi* to lift simultaneously on both sides, raising thirty-six times, until one feels a single speck enter the *zi gong* (womb). Then, maintain a state of *ruo cun ruo wang* (as if present, as if absent) for a brief moment.

This outlines the general method of refining the meridians, though within it lies an unexcelled living technique that cannot yet be spoken of—yet it is nothing beyond the phrase "abide in quiescent emptiness and observe."

[Commentary by Xie: This method of practice is overly effortful and truly unsuitable for beginners. Its essence lies in "naturalness," guiding in accord with the moment rather than forcing intention. Thus the closing line states: "nothing beyond abiding in quiescent emptiness and observing." The instructions such as "rotate so many times, lift so many times" should be understood flexibly—indeed, the heart-mind and breath interdependently observed with martial fire, nothing beyond "single-mindedness."]

[Editorial note on locations: The *zi gong* (womb) is the inner *pin* (feminine gate), the mysterious aperture in men. The *Dan Shu* states: "Yang is called *xuan* (mysterious), yin is called *pin* (feminine gate)." Combined, this is what the *Laozi* terms the "gate of the mysterious feminine" and what the *Huangdi Yinfu Jing* refers to as the "marvelous vessel." Whether called marvelous vessel, mysterious aperture, feminine gate, or womb, though the names are four, the cavity is one. Editorial note: Here it is termed *zi gong* (womb) to borrow human affairs for clarity, yet it is evident that both the sacred embryo and the mundane embryo coalesce therein.

[Commentary by Xie: This aperture is a living aperture; its "form" manifests only when *qi* arises, not confined to a fixed, tangible yin cavity.]

Further note: The phrase "nothing beyond" implies there is a subtle message to be embodied and practiced—take heed not to be careless. When the womb receives a spiraling surge of warm *qi*, the gate of the spring must be tightly sealed, never loosened, to attain a sense of ease. The greatest danger lies in the arising of thoughts; even a trace of attachment leads to the entire body dissolving into numbness. Not only must one swiftly settle the mind—here the paths of immortality and mortality diverge.

[The text warns to keep the gate tightly closed, never careless. If the gate slackens even slightly, true *qi* will leak. The following passage describes even greater peril: at that moment, the gate’s interior must experience extraordinary tingling; with further lifting and sealing, the feminine gate within attains an exceptional ease. Without settling the mind—

[Commentary by Xie: Here one should remain unmoved in heart, further entering the practice of heart-mind and breath interdependently merging into emptiness, forgetting form and appearance.]

—one will inevitably dissolve into numbness throughout the body.

[Commentary by Xie: True *qi* escapes through the skin.]

Slipping into the sea of desire, even if one seeks to settle the mind, it may be too late. Thus it is said: "here the paths of immortality and mortality diverge."

Master Taixu said: "The method lies solely in *gen bei* (stabilizing the back); only then is the mind settled."

[Commentary by Xie: Place the heart-mind "at rest" within the aperture of the *jiaji* (spine). Yet one must habitually temper and nurture this aperture to full maturity, cultivating the power of inherent nature to purity and depth, only then can one avoid loss. Otherwise, clinging to the physical body, one may not see its benefits before encountering its harm.]

Otherwise, the gate will surely open wide, and essence will leak like a pouring stream. Alas!]

At this moment, one must swiftly quiet the heart-mind for an extended time, waiting in stillness until the *Zigong* (Palace of the Child) settles into tranquility—this is precisely what Wei Yuanjun meant by *"treasure returned to the Northern Sea, securely at rest."* Yet this remains but a "yellow leaf to silence a child’s cry"; one must not mistake it for the formation of the embryo.

[Cautious note: The *Juehai* (Sea of Awareness) is the Southern Sea. Thus, this *Zigong* is the Northern Sea, though its position lies north of the *Zhongji* (Central Pole) and *Zhonghuang* (Central Yellow)—the locus of the *Zhouyi*’s *"yellow center through which principle flows."* Here, front and back define south and north, not above and below. (Xie’s note: The path governed by the three fields of the *Renmai* (Conception Vessel) is called the Southern Sea, rooted in the "heart"; the path governed by the three passes of the *Dumai* (Governor Vessel) is called the Northern Sea, rooted in the single aperture of the *Yinqiao* and the lower *Dantian*.) Moreover, Wei Yuanjun’s verse provides ample proof—only when the *Zigong* is stilled may one cease practice. (Xie’s note: The stilling of the *Zigong* means the "fire of the heart" has descended, the *Juehai* is waveless, and all has returned to the Northern Sea.)]

Privately, I observe that this pertains to cultivation with the "Red Dragon" still present, extending to the stages after the Dragon is severed. Such practice demands utmost stillness in the body; a single act of carelessness, and all effort is ruined—hence the saying, *"here the paths of immortality and mortality diverge."* Further note: This method embodies the entire process of *"round reflection"*—the return to the origin and restoration of the root. When the embryo is formed, the mysterious landscape is complete. Yet this refers to refining and returning the heaven-and-earth and five phases within the body to their primordial treasure, still a minor return. Such a treasure may be attained in a day or an hour, as the *Dan Book* states: *"one grain returns to one grain."* (Xie’s note: This denotes the effects of foundational work, beginning from the inner mysterious aperture, accumulating essence and amassing *qi*: *"one grain returns to one grain"* signifies accumulation, for each day brings a time of yang’s birth.) Thus, the "yellow leaf" is used as an analogy, but the true art lies in the secrets of gathering, refining, guiding, and settling—this is the complete process of the *"great return’s* mysterious reflection." One must carefully discern this; do not pass over it recklessly. (Xie’s note: Though this discusses the minor return, the methods of the great return that follow are fundamentally similar—hence it is called the *"mysterious reflection,"* the "shadow" of the great return.)

**Fifth Method: Returning and Restoring**
If we speak of the proper path for female cultivation, the fifth method is titled *"Returning and Restoring."* It refers to women in the world—some who reach old age without their bodies becoming pure, others whose Dragon is severed by forty-five or forty-six—all of whom should cultivate to restore their original state, returning to the condition of a maiden. This practice and method are those of the previous four methods, with only this difference: what was formerly drawn upward and backward is now directed forward and downward, flowing back to the *"stream and sea."*

**Fifth Method: Returning and Restoring (Continued)**

When swallowing the sweet dew, allow it only to linger in the throat without sending it downward. Then, use the hands to massage the *"breast stream"*—thirty-six rotations to the left, thirty-six to the right—until this *"stream and sea"* reveals a subtle, flowing savor. Next, gently massage both breasts: thirty-six slow strokes, thirty-six swift strokes, light at first and then heavy, each performed thirty-six times, totaling one hundred forty-four. Naturally, one will feel the true *qi* suffusing the breasts and the stream, as cool fluid like a spring emerges from the *"twin passes"* and surges into the *"Southern Sea."* Calm the mind and await this, without allowing the *qi* to disperse into the waist. Instead, release all thoughts within the *"Central Palace,"* refraining from any deliberate guidance, letting it disperse of its own accord. The entire body will then feel exceedingly clear and harmonious.

Practicing thus without interruption each day, the weak will gradually grow strong, the frail will gradually become robust, and the aged will gradually regain youth. The complexion will bloom like flowers, the breasts will gradually retract like those of a maiden, and within, something will congeal like a peach pit. Within a hundred days, the *Heavenly Water* will attain a hue like rouge, and after three days, proceed with the practices of the fourth method—without the slightest addition or alteration—and the *Red Dragon* will be severed once more. Yet only when the sun and moon appear as twin rings is true attainment achieved.

*(Xie’s Note: This method is none other than the practice of *"mind and breath interdependent, guarding the center and embracing the One,"* beginning cultivation from the female upper cinnabar field. This is called *"generating qi through spirit, transforming blood through qi,"* thereby restoring menstruation. *"Generating qi through spirit"* means that when spirit returns to the body’s *"center,"* qi naturally returns; when qi returns to the *"heart"* and is further refined by *"emptiness and stillness,"* it transforms into blood.)*

*(Careful Note: The* Daoist Canon *states that even in elderly women, there may still be menstrual flow. Yet this is not true menstrual flow—it is merely the fluids of food and drink.)*

The substance formed by the mingling of the people’s ministerial fire, which fails to return to the liver and spleen, may transform into intestinal bleeding, red vaginal discharge, or inverted menstruation—all manifestations of this same matter. These conditions all stem from deficiency. Thus, whether the menses cease prematurely or require restoration, the method of repair is the same: only after the body is refined to resemble that of a virgin may one proceed with the severing of the Red Dragon.

*(Xie’s Note: The character "得见" should be read with the rhyme of "现," for here "见" is pronounced as "现." The encounter is unplanned, arising not from deliberate arrangement or calculation, hence it is called "现"—simply a natural occurrence! "See" here signifies the appearance of signs, which can only be perceived when the heart is still and the body at rest. The character "现" in "现若" refers to manifestation, and when the body is attuned, the signs become visible. These two characters—"见" and "现"—carry distinct layers of meaning, and one must not read them carelessly.)*

**Sixth Principle: The Breasts**
If we speak of the proper path of female cultivation, the sixth principle is titled *"The Breasts."* This refers to the breasts’ connection above to the fluids of the heart and lungs and below to the true essence of the Sea of Blood. When the breasts are refined to resemble those of a virgin or a young child, it signifies the female body’s transformation into that of a male.

The method does not depart from the fourth and fifth principles. Women are rooted in blood, yet the aim of this principle lies in refining the red back to white, hence the additional step of *"refining fluids into blood."* To transform fluids into blood, nothing surpasses the practice of *"dew lingering at the pass,"* where spirit is focused on the twin gates, melting the old stagnant fluids within like mud, allowing them to flow back to the sea. When they return, blood is generated and flourishes—its profound essence lies within the fifth principle.

If one seeks to refine blood back to white, nothing compares to directing intention to the breast channels, clenching the teeth tightly, and augmenting the mind with emptiness and stillness, so that qi naturally gathers in the channels and reaches the breasts. Then, using both palms, knead the breasts—first slowly, then swiftly; first lightly, then with greater pressure—performing one hundred and forty-four repetitions. The gathered qi will flourish abundantly; afterward, withdraw the intention and direct it to the two flanks. Further, guide the eyes’ spirit to rotate the qi left and right, completing seventy-two breaths, until the qi warms the area like moxibustion. Then, with intention, circulate the qi around the wheel without counting, until the lower extremity feels as if boiling. Thus, the red will transform into fresh white, which must then be refined into qi, ascending through the spine’s gates, crossing the pillow, and penetrating the valley.

When, at the appointed time, the inner vision reveals the Three Mystic Mountains and the Pure Garden—yet the scene is not yet pristine—one must immediately engage in *"forgetting forgetting,"* suddenly entering the profound darkness of night. Abiding in stillness, over time, one will naturally experience lightning flashes and thunderous roars, a downpour like cascading dew, the Flowery Pond brimming full, the throat unable to swallow it all, the fluid descending smoothly through the pass to the navel, and the entire body suffused with clarity and harmony. Remaining in stillness, observe this process. After a hundred uninterrupted days, those with firm breasts will find them as flat as a young boy’s, while those with hollow breasts will fill them like walnuts, resembling a virgin’s. Achieving the form of a young boy results from the completion of the white-refining practice; attaining the form of a virgin comes from the completion of the red-refining practice.

Our tradition has seen many verified practitioners, among whom Mistress Feng stands out for her poetic records. Her verses serve as testimony:

*"Left sun, right moon—one yin-yang,
Through the nose’s pass, the inner work is called ‘moving the Gang.’
To return yin and yang to sun and moon,
Grasp the true fire and knead the twin chambers."*

Let the seeker take heed.

[**Note:** The "twin passes" lie between the spine and the palace behind it, containing two cavities where the body’s muddy fluids lodge. The left is called *Gao*, the right *Huang*—places where medicinal power cannot reach and true qi does not naturally arrive. These muddy fluids, if left to fester, bring calamity to the entire body. Creation, in forming humans, established these passes to guard the heart, hence their name: the Twin Passes. The fluid is called "mud" because, though resembling liquid, it is not true liquid—it derives from transformed food and drink, a kind of essence. Borne by qi, it spreads through the lungs to moisten the meridians. When the body’s true qi is abundant, this substance is transformed and serves boundless purposes. If true qi declines, the substance remains untransformed, flowing into the organs and meridians without harm. But when it encounters extreme yin qi, it congeals into muddy fluid—seeming like essence yet not essence—blocking the qi pathways. The Twin Passes and the lower extreme are where it lingers most. Of these, the Twin Passes are the most pernicious, for true qi does not reach them naturally. Thus, it accumulates like the ice and snow of Kunlun’s yin peaks, enduring the three summer months without melting. Though the heart’s Gang of Earth guards and protects, when spirit is strong, all is well; when spirit weakens, danger arises. The ancients knew this and devised the method of "gathering spirit to warm the passes," though few in the world have heard of it. Among those who knew, practiced, and recorded their success in verse, only Perfected Feng stands out. Thus, her words are cited here as proof. Yet her success also relied on first cultivating an empty, still mind, holding to the single incantation. Only by emptying the mind could spirit return and qi flourish, and with the method of channeling streams and kneading chambers, the muddy fluids were melted and surged forth from the passes, flowing abundantly to be refined. This is the wondrous interplay of non-being and being!

**Further Note:** The left chamber of the breast connects to the liver, the right to the lungs; the streams connect to the heart, kidneys, and spleen. Thus, one must observe and channel them diligently. Yet in ordinary times, one need only maintain this with intention, whether conscious or not. For in women, the root of life lies in the heart, corresponding to the central line of the *Kun* hexagram, which forms *Li* and harbors true fire. Blood arises from coolness, and when blood is abundant, spirit is at peace. Thus, emptiness and stillness are essential—this is the key to curing illness, nurturing life, and returning to the origin to achieve the Dao. The *Scripture of Purity* and the *Three Observances* are most fitting for this practice.]

**Seventh Rule: Jade Fluid**
If we speak of the seventh step in the proper path of female cultivation, it is titled "Jade Fluid." In men, when practice begins with purity and the work advances to moving the river chariot, true essence is preserved and does not leak from the Mysterious Pass.

[**Xie’s Note:** "Does not leak from the Mysterious Pass" means the Yang Pass has closed, turning life’s mechanism inward. Once the Yang Pass closes, the Mysterious Pass naturally opens, and the primordial no longer transforms the postnatal. The current reverses to the crown, dew showers the Celestial Valley, and flows down to the Flowery Pond—also called Jade Fluid. Yet only when the yin spirit appears, the hun soul wanders the Jade Palace, the po soul pays homage to the Imperial Perfected, the round light crowns the head, the tides surge in the Mysterious Sea, and the echoes resound in the Jade Clarity, does the true return of the Jade Fluid elixir occur. The ancient perfected called this "nectar pouring on the crown."

**Xie’s Note:** Even in the minor return of Jade Fluid, there is the work of harmonizing spirit. Once the river chariot flows smoothly and the Yang Pass is tightly sealed, the yin spirit appears. Then, harmonizing and refining spirit to purity, one emits light to draw the primordial unity, filling the body with true yang. The heart’s brightness shines day and night, and only then can one proceed to the major return of Golden Fluid. Most in the world are unaware of this step of harmonizing spirit, nurturing, and bathing. Some mistakenly call this "emitting the yang spirit," but this is a grave error. At this stage, the primordial spirit has only just formed and returns to the Muddy Pellet. The Mysterious Sea is the sea of the brain; Jade Clarity is the realm of emptiness in the upper elixir field.]

As for women, Jade Fluid is the transformation of the Red Dragon’s liquid into the White Phoenix’s marrow. Only when this marrow is abundant can one proceed with the reverse flow, avoiding empty effort. The methods within, though not departing from the four rules already shown, must follow the subtleties of the six rules. Only thus can their use be inexhaustible—this is what the earlier worthies meant by: *"One grain returns to one grain, / Its use is never spent. / When the true seed is attained, / This work must still be pursued with force."* Yet the means to attain sufficiency lie entirely in cultivating an empty, still mind. Let the seeker take heed.

[**Note:** For this rule, we should cite the self-account of the Immortal Jade Maiden. She said: *"In my past practice of returning the elixir, I forgot the person through the method, forgot the method through the person, and acted when the time came—thus, I forgot the self for the sake of the self. From this day forward, I forgot the day, forgot the hour, until even heaven and earth vanished. Over time, I suddenly awoke as if enlightened, listening and seeing in stillness, yet utterly forgetting what the matter was. Only then did I feel scorched as if burning, and afterward, there appeared a grease like oil (after the North Star, the Red Dragon’s liquid transformed into the White Phoenix’s marrow), boundless and limitless, now sounding, now silent, now flowing, now stopping, now surging, now spraying. At times, it hung like a snow-white ribbon; at others, it settled like a clear ice lake. The times were not one time, the places not one place, yet the eyes were not dazzled, nor the spirit wearied."*]

Suddenly, amid this state, what was seen and heard became enough to delude the nature. At that moment, I still managed to caution myself: *"Do not be lured by phenomena."*

Then, I suddenly realized: *"Heaven and earth share the same body with me."* Turning inward to reflect, I saw that my own body was surely the same—if the principle held externally, it must also hold internally. Thus, it must be so within.

Thereupon, I turned my gaze inward to examine myself. I had no self; after abiding in stillness for a long while, the true "I" emerged. *(Xie’s note: "吾" refers to the conscious spirit and the self of perception; "我" refers to the primordial spirit and true intent.)* Yet when I sought to delve deeper into this inner reflection, there was no gate or aperture to be found.

Suddenly, as if awakening from a dream, I became aware that within this body—deep in its lowest depths—there burned a scorching heat like moxibustion. A sound arose like thunder, the roar of wind and tide surging from within. In an instant, it pierced the gates, ascended the spine, passed through the pillow bone, and reached the valley, flowing like sweet dew until it descended from the nose. The Flower Pool filled with water, so abundant that swallowing could not keep pace. In less than half a day, the fluid surged into the Southern Ocean, then poured into the waist and coiled around the navel, smelting and refining. Truly, heaven and earth shared one body—externally so, and now internally so as well. The truth of it was confirmed.

At that time, I simply followed the usual sequence, completing the work before withdrawing.

Such were the words of the immortal maiden, all describing the transformation of inner work. One can imagine that in her daily practice, she must have first devoted herself to emptiness and stillness, then later advanced to a state of utter forgetfulness. This account is thus recorded here to verify that such methods indeed belong to the art of inner cultivation.

**Eighth Method: Embryonic Breathing**

This is the eighth method in the proper path of female cultivation, titled *"Embryonic Breathing."* Embryonic breathing is the supreme Dao, the celestial ladder. After a woman completes the Returned Elixir, her essence and qi become abundant, her body one with that of a man—without embryonic breathing, the day of returning to emptiness will never come.

This single breath holds boundless efficacy, yet its practice is most simple. However, not all who cultivate it achieve the same result; the differences are profound. Is this not the work of Creation’s design? Yet Creation itself is shaped by the nature of things.

When one first enters stillness to seek the breath at the nose, there is no thought, no deliberation.
*(Xie’s note: "Emptiness" is not the Dao; "stillness" is not the Dao. "Emptiness" is not the Mysterious Aperture; "fullness" is not the Mysterious Aperture. These terms—emptiness and fullness, stillness and movement—serve only as means and tools to perceive the Dao and enter the Mysterious Aperture.)*

Morning and night, one persists until one day the Ancestral Aperture is touched—it opens of itself, neither sought nor rejected. Suddenly, the breath merges with the nose.
*(Xie’s note: This refers to the method of Golden Fluid. At the outset, mind and breath interdepend in the emptiness beyond the body—not the air-filled emptiness outside the flesh. When breath at the nose and heartbeat both vanish, the Outer Mysterious Pass activates spontaneously. Essence transforms into qi, qi into spirit, spirit returns to emptiness—all naturally, effortlessly, perpetually aware and luminous. Within the body, infinite celestial mechanisms unfold; inside and outside become one, heaven and humanity share a single qi. Hence it is called embryonic breathing, also known as the Returned Elixir.
Further note: At the outset, one begins with the Outer Elixir Field, then unites inner and outer Elixir Fields; eventually, heaven, earth, and humanity merge into primordial chaos.)*

Vast and boundless, profound and unfathomable—one no longer knows whether the Ancestor is oneself or oneself the Ancestor. A single breath through the nose: the ancients called this embryonic breathing. Within this aperture, yin and yang, the Five Phases, heaven and earth, all beings—all arise from it.

The breath responds to the mechanism as the mechanism responds, naturally giving rise to six grades of immortal kin: celestial, aquatic, terrestrial, human, spiritual, and spectral. The key lies in extreme emptiness and stillness. Those whose virtue aligns with True Unity cultivate to become Celestial Immortals; those whose virtue aligns with Mysterious Unity become Aquatic Immortals; those whose virtue aligns with Upright Unity become Terrestrial Immortals; those whose virtue aligns with Essential Unity become Human Immortals. The two lesser vehicles—those whose virtue aligns with Passionate Unity—become spirits if leaning toward yang, ghosts if leaning toward yin. Though the virtuous may attain fruition, they cannot be called true immortals. Such are the distinctions, rooted in the interplay of mechanism and response.
*(Xie’s note: Plant melons and you reap melons; plant beans and you reap beans. In cultivation, only "resolve" matters.)*

Though called a heavenly endowment, is it not self-acquired? Let the practitioner take heed.
*(Xie’s note: Responding with True Unity, one becomes a Celestial Immortal; responding with Mysterious Unity, an Aquatic Immortal... The "nose" here refers to the Outer Mysterious Aperture, the Mysterious Female of Creation. It is not the nostrils of the human body. Because one begins with breath, it is called the nose. First, "mind and breath interdepend, spirit and qi unite"; then, "spirit and breath interdepend, nature and life unite"—all transpiring within the Mysterious Aperture. Thus, a single breath through the nose unites heaven, earth, humanity, and self in one qi, one spirit, one Mysterious Aperture.)*

This humble reflection affirms: embryonic breathing is the true supreme Dao, the true celestial ladder. How could one not strive with diligence?

Here follows the translation:

---

Sixth Precept: *Namo* – On the Ninth Path of Women’s Cultivation, titled *"Namo."*
To speak of the consummation of women’s practice, none surpasses the Great Being, who through ascetic cultivation and devoted refinement attains the realization of buddhahood and bodhisattvahood. The power of this attainment lies in the two syllables *Namo*. Within these two characters is concealed a profound mystery. Only by embodying and safeguarding the truth that this very body is Buddha—like a seven-tiered crystal stupa enshrined upon Mount Putuo—can one proceed. Before the stupa stands a red child, the leader of the discriminating mind, whom the Great Being allows to wander east and west in inquiry. After fifty-three inquiries, the inquiry culminates in seeing the Buddha, and the koan becomes perfectly clear. Then, relying on the Dragon Girl of the Southern Ocean, she offers the Pearl of Spontaneous Freedom, which is shielded by the Purple Bamboo Grove. Presently, the white parrot flits up and down; in hand, she holds the Pure Bottle, inserting a willow sprig to gather the natural nectar of sweet dew. Seated steadfast upon Mount Putuo, she employs the *Dhāraṇī* method, placing a single syllable in the realm of the truly real, securing the supreme treasure within the fish basket. Reciting *Garuḍa*, she releases all of *sahā* into the Southern Sea, where waves surge unceasingly—yet she abides in spontaneous ease, beholding the spontaneously free. This great dharma, however, cannot do without the fourth precept’s inner work, which must arise moment by moment from the preceding precept. Thus, step by step, one returns to true emptiness and true quiescence. When merit is complete and conduct fulfilled, one may exchange smiles with the Great Being, serene and joyful as the liberation of the Buddha.

Let the practitioner take heed.

*(Respectfully noted: This precept is purely about transforming function and resolving the mechanism of transformation. It is to be apprehended intuitively, not expounded verbally. One must only devote oneself earnestly to *Namo*, embodying the truth that this very body is Buddha—living, vibrant, and unbound in all directions.)*

Tenth Precept of the Women’s Right Path, titled *"Vigilance at Life’s End."*
Women embody the virtue of *kun*, the Way of Earth—without achievement, yet ever completing what has begun. Thus, they ought to assist in nurturing and transforming the world beneath the bright sun of civilization. Yet the work begins with emptiness and quiescence, costing not a penny nor expending a thread of effort. It is achieved through sitting, unknown to others, yet one’s virtue parallels the workings of creation—healing the world through this very body. The practice relies entirely on regulating the mind to emptiness and quiescence: when the heart’s chamber is purified, the celestial realm attains great peace; when the *kun*-abdomen flows freely, the common folk prosper; when the four limbs circulate unimpeded, the four barbarian regions are pacified. Thus, when the body is regulated, the self is at peace; when the self is at peace, the world is governed. The resonance is immediate: a single moment of harmony yields a moment of true virtue. Though no effect is seen, the effect is inherent.

Yet one must guard against superficial learning and the failure to unify the Three Fields, for no one whose own body remains unintegrated can possess the talent to save the world.

*(Xie’s note: The Confucians say, “Cultivate the self, order the family, govern the state, bring peace to all under heaven.” How profound these words!)*

The secret lies in morning and evening devotion: if others advance by one, advance by a hundred; if others advance by ten, advance by a thousand. Though dull-witted, one will surely become enlightened.

Let the practitioner take heed.

*(Respectfully noted: This precept is the full reissue authorized by the Queen Mother of the West. The Non-Dual Primordial Sovereign, following the oral transmission of the Great Way of World-Healing from the Jade-Pure Divine Mother, compiled and amended the final precept of former transmissions to conclude the text. It is truly an unprecedented and monumental canon since the dawn of creation. Lü Dongbin called it “the greatest fortune of creation,” while the Primordial Sovereign deemed it “the timely revival of the Dao’s destiny.” Such high expectations are placed upon later learners. May all who encounter this text encourage one another.)*

*The Precious Raft of Dual Cultivation for Women’s Practice*
*Transmitted by Patriarch Li of the Mud-Pill Palace*

Master Tai Xu’s Account with Annotations, Revised by Disciple Min Yide

**First Precept**

The Master of Mud-Pill Palace states:
For women’s practice, progress begins with halting thoughts, then regulating the mind. Once thoughts are stilled and the mind harmonized, one may proceed to massage.

**The method forbids avoiding warmth to seek coolness.**
Women, whose root is blood, are by nature inclined toward yin. Yin delights in coolness, yet without the subtle activation of qi through massage, they easily sink into pure yin. Yin begets coolness, coolness congeals into ice—if not countered by movement, it breeds phlegm stagnation, blood stasis, and other ailments, obstructing progress. Thus, one must begin with halting thoughts and regulating the mind.

Women belong to *kun*, yet *kun* conceals true fire. When fire lies dormant, all is auspicious; when it flares, it scorches metal. If left unregulated and stirred, metal, pressed by fire, manifests the omen of "the bird’s cry ascending to heaven." Therefore, women’s practice must commence with halting thoughts and regulating the mind.

In halting thoughts and regulating the mind, one cannot practice too much, nor fear prolonged effort—within stillness, there is movement.

**Master Tai Xu annotates:**
When thoughts cease, qi becomes pure; when the mind is regulated, qi becomes harmonious. Continuing with massage then awakens the mechanism of yang. Yet one must guard against stagnation and restlessness. Women naturally prefer coolness and dislike heat, and upon initially achieving stillness of thought, harmony of mind, and balance of qi, they may encounter stagnation or agitation. This often sparks the desire to replenish true yin, leading to the accumulation of pure yin. For stillness congeals yin, and inactivity stifles yang—beginners invariably fall into this pitfall. Unaware of the cause of restlessness and vexation, they hastily seek temporary relief in coolness, a grave mistake! One must instead intensify practice, employing methods to circulate qi. When qi flows, agitation naturally dissolves. Those who fail to grasp this and seek results only deepen their afflictions, further inviting phlegm stagnation and blood stasis. Hence, this warning is urgent.

The purpose of continuing massage is precisely to prevent such stasis. Yet human nature favors progress and swift results, sometimes leading to overly vigorous massage. If the earthly fire blazes, all fires follow, risking the harm of scorching metal—hence the caution against "the bird’s cry ascending to heaven." *Hanyin* refers to the *you*-bird (rooster); when pressed to its limit, it flees upward. Thus, the text reemphasizes the subtlety of halting thoughts and regulating the mind.

This precept reveals the essential method for women’s practice, thorough from beginning to end.

The Second Precept

Master Niwan states: In women’s refined practice, one begins with the flourishing of yang and concludes with the restraint of yin—this method is most profound, yet few comprehend it. The deluded follow the male path in their cultivation, while the wise turn to Chan Buddhism, each able to verify a certain fruition, achieving effects such as vanishing while standing or transforming while seated. Yet they remain mired in ghostly realms, far from the Dao.

For women, blood is the foundation: when blood is abundant, essence overflows; when the heart is cool, blood is generated. As the ancients said, the refinement of fluid into blood and the transformation of blood into essence depend on a clear spirit. Without the transformation of fluid, fluid loses the warming of spirit, congeals into phlegm, flows into the spleen and stomach, steams upward to the lungs, scatters through the meridians, and gives rise to a hundred diseases. The five viscera suffer calamity, the six bowels encounter misfortune. Thus, ancient elixir methods always begin by stilling the heart. When the heart is stilled and breathing settled, the spirit becomes clear, and the heart cools.

One must wait until the heart is cool and fluid surges, then direct attention to the breast channels, applying rotating massage with the hands to ensure the qi mechanism overflows. Next, raise both hands to rotate around the breasts, waiting until this misty vapor envelops them, feeling the warmth suffuse from behind, the twin passes alight with smoky flame. The momentum presses through the passes, filling them with muddy fluid, which flows into the breast channels like a gushing spring.

Then, with true intent, guide it into the Southern Ocean, silently guarding it for approximately thirty-six breaths. Release the intent slightly, sensing within a spontaneous descent, dividing to flow into both flanks, spiraling left and right, each for thirty-six breaths of spirit. Then, with unified intent, gather it deep within the navel wheel, slowly rotating forty-nine times, swiftly rotating forty-nine times. Observe the coccyx: if the warmth penetrates from behind, and the momentum seems sluggish, employ the method of contracting the two excretory orifices to naturally ascend through the tailbone, up the spine, over Kunlun, and descend into Niwan. Feeling Niwan vast as the sea, one may pause to nurture it. Then, descending into the Crimson Palace and the Flowery Pond, the great earth’s Jambudvīpa is drenched with dewdrops, all tasks forgotten. One feels only a vague indistinctness, breathing without conscious breath, swallowing without conscious swallow, lifting without conscious lift—within, the flavor is sweet and fragrant, qi and spirit harmoniously full, the three fields unified.

Then, as mysterious conditions pervade, swiftly turn inward, releasing all entanglements. Gradually, the body feels hollow as a valley, the great earth vanishes, and a subtle coolness subtly assails one, misty vapor filling all. Suddenly, clouds disperse and fog clears, revealing the Sea of Nature below, its azure waves limpid. I remain unmoved by a single thought, forgetting both state and emotion. Suddenly, myriad golden rays appear, fine rain like pearls descending with the light, spiraling left and right, transforming into a luminous moon floating in a crystalline sea. Abruptly, one awakens as from a dream.

Master Niwan states: At this moment, swiftly introspect this body. At this time, one should feel qi refreshed, spirit clear, and the entire body harmonious—this is attainment. Attainment means the whole body remains luminously concentrated for a while, with intent directed to the feminine gate, sensing within a profound tranquility—this is it.

Then, rub the hands and face, circulate spirit around the abdomen, raise the windlass on both sides, each for forty-nine breaths. Gently twist the waist, sway the knees and legs, sit and tap the toes, each for twenty-four breaths, then stop. Practicing this for a hundred days, three times daily without interruption, the foundation for celestial immortality is established.

Master Taixu states: This precept is a general outline, anciently called the Ladder to Heaven. The great Dao’s elixir method lies herein, lacking only the final crucial step. Later scholars must first become thoroughly familiar with it, embodying each word, silently contemplating it hundreds of times daily. Then, when practicing, it will be like entering a familiar path, not led astray by phenomena. Even if manifestations slightly differ, the sequence remains orderly. Scholars must not treat this as a *Journey to the West* to be read and set aside.

For men’s elixir texts abound like cattle hairs, but women’s elixir texts are rarely complete in the world. To obtain the *Eighteen Direct Pointers of Golden Flower* is already to possess an untransmitted secret. With this guide to cross-reference, the secret method for female celestial immortality is complete. If one only obtains the *Direct Pointers*, one may attain earthly or human immortality at best.

---

The Third Precept

Master Niwan states: In dual cultivation, men do not require a vessel; those who use one will never attain the Dao. Adding oil is a minor technique, not the true method. The true method unites the Three Powers in one body. Women’s dual cultivation is fundamentally the same: without containing the Three, the elixir is nurtured to completion. Within, the true One is like granary millet—creation is the furnace, ready to be consumed at will.

He further states: Know that in the world there are Unobstructed Assemblies; seeds originally pervade the great thousandfold world. Using an altar as furnace and vessel, after Lu’s departure, the true transmission was lost.

He further states: In speaking this gatha, the Eight Divisions of Devas and Nāgas will surely be astonished, deeming me garrulous and fearing divine punishment. Yet I speak freely because I received the august decree of the Jade Purity Divine Mother, who lamented the Dao’s near extinction and commanded the Peerless Holy Maiden to solemnly proclaim it, orally transmitting it to me with the intent to reveal it directly, no longer concealing it under false names to further mislead later generations.

Her teaching states: Solitary cultivation is not the supreme Dao; those of the same kind naturally rely on one another. Those who possess a body beyond the body can forget form and serve all things.

Her method states:
*"Qian’s origin is attained from the crown,
Kun’s origin is lost from the feminine gate.
The human origin pervades the great stem,
The Three Origins are mastered by one heart.
Not beyond the heart’s stillness and emptiness,
Not beyond the body’s lack of obstruction.
Movement and stillness unite with true constancy;
I have no origin, yet it naturally merges.
When origin merges, the One also merges,
The One Origin is emotion and nature.
Emotion is nature’s origin,
Nature is endowed with talent.
Able to transform without origin or One,
One naturally transcends the supreme rank."*

This is the august decree of the Jade Purity Divine Mother and the oral transmission of the Peerless Holy Maiden. Those who can, follow it.

[Master Taixu states: The mutual necessity of like kinds is the principle of the Supreme Ultimate—this is precisely what is called the wondrous union and coagulation of the dual essences of the Two and the Five. Within and beyond *Awakening to Reality* lies the entirety of the *Triple Concordance*; what it speaks of is this single principle. Yet世人 have misunderstood it, giving rise to the defiled practices of the "Three Peaks." Now, having received the Master’s instruction, the oral transmission of a thousand years is at last made clear. How fortunate am I, Bing, to have received it. (Bing is the lineage name of Master Taixu.) How fortunate the world is to have it illuminated—this is the culminating great stratagem of the dual traditions of male and female cultivation. Yet unless one possesses the power of wisdom, few can bring it to completion.

I, Bing, have tasted the essence of the tradition: the method lies solely in the absence of self, which alone can lead to the absence of things. When both self and things are forgotten, the True One appears. Once the True One has appeared, follow the One in its upholding. The One naturally dissolves into itself, transforming and generating endlessly, without limit. Within this imperial Dao, nothing surpasses the Unobstructed Buddha Assembly. The alchemical texts speak of "living dragons and tigers filling empty space." I, Bing, have witnessed this in such an assembly. However, one must adhere strictly to the ancient regulations to avoid disgrace or regret.

Regarding this assembly, its meaning is most profound yet its manifestation most evident—take care not to misunderstand. What is called "profound" lies hidden in the heart, where gains and losses are known to none but oneself. What is called "evident" is as open as a marketplace, where every movement and stillness is revealed without the slightest concealment. Only by thus observing the method can one avoid the world’s censure.

Alas! The sage’s heart is burdened with sorrow; the sage’s vision extends far indeed!]

Fourth Section.

Nīwán Shì states: Indeed, the ancient sages have said: If the gross substance is not transformed, the Dao remains ever distant; if merit and conduct are not perfected, fruition will never come. To advance by skipping stages is but to court delusion; to attain realization without perfection is to gain only a lesser, inferior fruit. Let the learner heed this compassionate instruction: one must first temper the Dharma-body to firmness, for this provides the foundation for refinement. Without this foundation, one cannot speak of the higher principles.

The higher principles concern purely the work of transformation, yet each step arises from the physical form—this is the art of lodging the empty within the solid and, through the solid, attaining the empty. Such is the method of the Heavenly Immortal.

[Taixū Shì comments: The Dharma-body is the body beyond the body. This body is not obtained through visualization, nor can it be accomplished by alchemical refinement. Its secret lies in "borrowing the false to cultivate the real," and its practice does not extend beyond the physical form. The key is to refine this physical body until, within and without, it is pure and stainless—where "body" is no-body, and no-body is body. This is what is meant by: when the work is active, the body vanishes; when the work ceases, the body appears. In that state of vanishing, all sensations of cold and warmth are not the self; all sensations of pain and itch are not the self—this is what is called "awareness without attachment."

How is this achieved? The method lies in dwelling in emptiness with the spirit, so that the body is no longer the body. One who can recognize the True One, beyond which all is illusion, has further mastered it. Refining thus until there is no far or near, no inside or outside, one advances further. Cultivating further to the point of no going or coming, no entering or exiting, one truly attains the state of no far or near, no inside or outside. Refining still further to the point of no arising or ceasing, no movement or stillness, one truly reaches the state of no coming or exiting. In this way, the pure realm of the Dharma-body is fully realized. Yet all this is sought nowhere but within the physical body.]

Fifth Principle

Nīwán Shì says: The words of Zhēnyáng are true. (Zhēnyáng is the sobriquet bestowed upon Taixū Shì by Nīwán Shì.) Through such diligent cultivation, the Dharma-body naturally manifests; through such unwavering practice, a body exists beyond the body. You must understand: the ancient sages relied upon the final, great expedient to complete the Dao—this is the swiftest path to its attainment!

For the true yin and true yang within the body are limited; refining them involves nothing more than mutual tempering of the prior and posterior. Though daily cultivation yields gradual accumulation, the acquired impurities of the postnatal body also grow day by day. Even with diligent practice, those who encounter great calamities are many across the ages—how pitiable! There is no other reason: the innate endowment of true essence is measurable, while the accrued falsity of the postnatal is boundless. Moreover, if one does not begin cultivation in youthful purity, the stains of corruption are inescapable. In this, you may well fear for the world!

[Taixū Shì says: Whether drinking water or broth, one knows its warmth or coolness. If the Dharma-body is already formed, the methods of regulation and protection, the proper timing of gathering and releasing, need not be sought elsewhere—for inner verification is sufficient. Even if the Dharma-body is not yet formed, the methods of regulation and protection, the timing of releasing and gathering, are still to be sought within the body’s own fluctuations—nothing more than blockage and flow, ascent and descent, cold and warmth, dryness and moisture.

In applying these principles, how could they extend beyond unblocking what is blocked, warming what is cold, moistening what is dry, and circulating these transformations within? The great aim is single-mindedness and softness, not being led astray by external things, harmonizing the foundation of heart and qi, unifying the movement of qi, and recognizing this body as a borrowed vessel. All practices—massage, contraction, visualization, and frequent circulation—serve only to enliven the qi’s movement.

Once the qi’s mechanism is lively and free, the method rests solely on single-minded softness: when thoughts arise, dissolve them; when gathering, know when to rest. Beware of "riding the ox to seek the ox," of gathering without cessation—this is called "adding a head atop the head." Even when signs such as unobstructed flow, ascent and descent, warmth, coolness, and balance are achieved, avoid clinging—just as gathering must know when to rest.

Cultivating and nurturing in accordance with this, one will never face the peril of collapse. Such is my observation.]

**Sixth Principle**

Master Niwan states: Indeed, your words are correct. The woman’s spirit takes flight, the man’s essence congeals—both stem from the error of "adding a head atop the head." For the spirit clings to essence: when spirit congeals and essence is balanced, all is at peace; when essence is exhausted and spirit left solitary, it flees. The unknowing mistakenly call this "transformation," a grievous pity.

From this, one may discern the folly of excessive massage and visualization. Why is this so? The woman is inwardly yin yet outwardly yang, her trigrammatic nature belonging to *Li*; her true yin leaks away with the monthly tide. Thus, stillness triumphing over motion brings fortune, while motion triumphing over stillness invites misfortune. The man’s root lies in essence, the woman’s in blood; essence thrives with warmth, blood flourishes with coolness. Know this, and you know how to nurture.

Yet the woman’s practice does not abandon massage and visualization, for it serves two purposes: first, to free the movement of qi, ensuring the meridians flow unimpeded; second, to refine the body’s fluids, preventing stagnation from congealing into phlegm, so that fluids may transform into blood.

The ancient sages spoke of stillness and preservation as the foundation, which also holds two meanings: when ruler and ministers are at peace, the spirit remains clear and does not flee; moreover, stillness gives rise to wisdom, shielding the life-force from desire’s disturbances. This is the secret of dual cultivation within the self.

Once the qi’s mechanism is free and the will pure and tranquil, augment it with harmony, follow with integrity and purity. Though daily progress may seem slight, monthly gains accumulate. Persist in this practice, and one day you will realize a body equal to empty space, the Three Fields unified as one. You will perceive only luminous radiance in every limb, joint, and aperture. At this stage of cultivation, the self and the body beyond the self are both attained.

If you persist without retreat, spirit and qi will be full, thoughts will not stray outward, the spirit will not chase after thoughts, blood will flourish abundantly, true yin will be sufficient, and qi and essence will naturally expand to fill heaven and earth. Yet if thoughts soar and scatter, you will fall into the Two Vehicles—what the alchemical texts call "the yin spirit departing the husk." The practitioner must guard against this.

---

Master Taixu comments: I have heard from the Master that the spirit is the heart’s spirit; when it remains and does not flee, it is because it clings to essence. Once essence dries up, the spirit takes flight. Essence here refers to kidney essence; when essence does not congeal, it is governed by the spirit. Yet this congealed essence is not primordial essence—it is merely a fluid, akin to the body before its formation. Once the true spirit departs, this essence hardens.

The *Book of Changes* states: "The interplay of yin and yang is called the Dao." A verse says: "Half a catty and eight taels make the true." And again: "Solitary yin does not generate, lone yang does not grow." *Qian* and *Kun*, *Kan* and *Li*, *Zhen* and *Xun*, *Dui* and *Gen*—heaven and earth, sun and moon, nature and life, male and female—all follow the ceaseless cycle of yin and yang, which is the constant Dao. If cultivation leans toward one vehicle or perception tilts to one side, it becomes a flawed path.

It is further said: In the beginning of practice, one seeks union within the body, yet there is always a sequence—first the true, then the false. Though the false arises from the true, the true may also be called false; when the false returns to the true, it is then called primordial. If the gathering misses its time or clings to form, it strays onto side paths, becoming mere illusion—though still salvageable. The gravest danger lies in the moment when, after solitary cultivation reaches fulfillment, perception enters the profound void, and a single bias in thought leads to a corresponding bias in attainment. Though one may seek to halt it, it is already too late. The woman’s spirit flies, the man’s essence congeals—how can one not be cautious!

Alas! Know that Master Cui’s *Mirror for Taking the Medicine* says: "It is nature and life, not spirit and qi." To speak of spirit and essence is like offering yellow leaves to stop a child’s crying. Without recognizing true gold, how can one distinguish yellow leaves?

Master Zhong said: "The four great elements of the body are all yin; what, then, is yang essence?" Only when one meets a enlightened teacher’s guidance does the Daoist immortal’s work become the cultivation of the body. He also said: "The intermingling of being and non-being is the root of the elixir; the mutual support of the hidden and manifest is the water and metal. Do not cling to this body as the Dao, for solitary cultivation without substance is but solitary yin."

Combining these teachings with the Master’s instructions, there must be what is called the "true seed." Yet if it is not sought outside this body, its meaning is profoundly subtle.

---

**Seventh Principle**

Master Niwan states: Indeed.

**Seventh Principle**

Master Niwan states: Indeed.

The *Daode Jing* says: "There is a thing, formlessly formed, born before heaven and earth. Silent and void, it stands alone and does not change, circulates without cease, and may be called the mother of all under heaven. I know not its name; forced to designate it, I call it the Dao." It also says: "Vague and elusive, yet within it there is form; dim and obscure, yet within it there is essence. Its essence is most real, and within it there is truth."

This one thing is enclosed within the mountain of form. The ancients said: "Seek it not within the body, nor gather it outside the body." Vague and elusive, it seems to dwell in the void and obscurity between being and non-being, yet it does not lie beyond the single aperture of the Mysterious Pass. This aperture—vast without boundary, minute without interior—cannot be grasped by thought nor opened by effort. The method lies only in making the body equal to emptiness, releasing all conditions, forgetting even emptiness, forgetting even stillness. Then the spirit naturally enters the mark, and qi naturally emerges from within. When the qi-body becomes misty and boundless, without head or tail, this is the manifestation of that thing, the first sign of the body beyond the body.

If this aperture does not open, even if one severs the dragon and transforms the spirit, it remains but the illusory existence of yellow leaves—how can it be called "conceiving the embryo" or "entering the gate"? What was shown before is still but yellow leaves, not true gold.

Master Taixu states: Massage, though delusive, cannot be abandoned lest the qi-mechanism stagnate; visualization, though false, cannot be discarded lest qi and essence falter. Advancing further, one cultivates until there is something yet nothing, yet the teacher’s intent still does not deem this ultimate—because it remains but this-side’s affair! Nevertheless, when this-side’s affair is complete, the far shore is easily reached; if the far shore is not reached, the mechanism is blocked by layered mountains. When it is reached, guide it with mindfulness—effortlessly, abundantly, and the four neighbors will arrive of themselves. Thus, though separated by mountains and lakes, the qi-mechanism’s communion is as if face-to-face.

What is the method? As the teacher said: "Emit light to draw it, concentrate the mind to await it." If it ascends while you descend, or retreats while you advance, the meeting is futile. The method lies only in stillness amid motion, empty and receptive. When the qi-mechanism arrives, sense its harmonious ease, yet remain still and unmoving. Envelop it with intention, store it deep within for inner refinement, proceeding from *kun* to *gen*, riding the raft into the Milky Way. Perceive golden lightning flashing, cool qi filling the void, like clouds or mist swirling within and without. At this moment, guard against杂念—whether admiration or doubt—dismiss thoughts as they arise. Sense a kind of qi-mechanism, effortlessly filling the center, without inside or outside, without boundary. In an instant, myriad transformations appear, impossible to count, depict, or describe. Yet there are also times of stillness without radiance, pitch-black as night. These are all called "mysterious reflections," also named "round images of the far shore." In truth, they are the perfect interpenetration of self and other—what is called the three realms of the *Huayan*, *Śūraṅgama*, and *Lotus Sutra*, the wondrous scenes of Three Mountains and Ten Isles. In reality, they are the qi-mechanism of transformative craft between self and other, the far shore yet not the far shore. Yet the attainment of the far shore does not lie beyond this.

The teacher said: "I once inquired of the Pure and Tranquil Primordial Sovereign, who replied, 'So it is, so it is.' And further: 'Why should the work of men be different?'"

**Eighth Principle**

Master Niwan states: The verse says: "Turning and overturning, the affairs of heaven and earth; the two qi conjoin in essence to form *gen*-metal." It also says: "The hawk seizes the sparrow, the falcon strikes the winter crow—subtle within the subtle, wondrous within the wondrous." Yet this does not lie beyond "knowing the white and guarding the black, knowing the male and guarding the female"—how could it lie beyond "preserving non-being and guarding being"?

Master Taixu states: The *Daode Jing* and *Nanhua* are not texts a woman can recite daily; the *Qingjing Jing* should be read until familiar, revered within. Perhaps only the *Kun Ning* and *Zhen Yi* sutras! For without thoroughgoing nature, life cannot be preserved; without strict discipline, merit cannot be firm. The verse the teacher cited is profoundly abstruse—how could it be easily fathomed? Even after receiving the highest teachings, how many women truly understand? They remain adrift in longing—such is common under heaven. It contains the entire *Fire Record* within.

Study the *Yellow Emperor’s Yin Convergence*, ponder the *Dragon-Tiger*, *Triple Unification*, and *Awakening to Reality*—only then can one speak of this principle. I shall briefly indicate the outline:

Turning and overturning,
its affairs are cyclical.
Recognize the one within the one,
and the one ever precedes.
All comes down to the two qi,
their essence conjoined in myriad forms.
When the body is without one, it appears,
able to embrace the great thousand.
The great thousand’s radiance gleams,
gleaming is the other’s origin.
If not led astray by the other’s origin,
the origin’s origin is my origin.
Origin upon origin, not one by one,
each one lacks wholeness.
Still and unrelenting,
is the work truly ordinary?
Sparrows and swallows follow their nature,
crows endure the cold.
When not hungry, they do not come;
when the time comes, they feast at will.
This is wondrous within the wondrous,
mystery within mystery.
Knowing the white, thus guard the black,
and the great whole is attained.
How does it achieve this?
The utmost non-ultimate contains all.
The teacher’s profound meaning is thus—
yet being and non-being generate each other,
grasping and relinquishing must follow the one.
Without transforming the colored body, nothing is accomplished.

**Ninth Principle**

Master Niwan states: Well said! There are teachings that say: To transcend the mundane, first purify mundane thoughts, then empty the three realms. Yet do not transgress inner principles, nor flatter ghosts and spirits. Be filial, respectful, compassionate, and kind, without defying the Master. Be gentle, yielding, upright, and steadfast, without violating the *kun*-Way.

When in motion, follow principle; when at rest, release all attachments.
The wondrous Dao is lodged in holding the dustpan and broom,
the firing times are realized in tending the hearth and cooking.
The *Ode* says:
*"Gentle and graceful,
like mountains, like rivers.
If this child is unworthy,
what can be said?"*
Such is its admonition—how profound!

**Master Taixu states:** This principle of the Master is most subtle. Those in the world who take refuge in the Dao or in the Buddha seldom follow inner principles, rarely grasp the nature of the school. Though they may be gentle and yielding in serving their teachers and elders, they often harbor resentment and defy ethical norms. Their disciples and masters alike are scorned by the teachings of proper conduct, and they will cast themselves into the iron-ringed Avīci hell—is this not lamentable?

**A Note by Min Yide:** My master, the Venerable Taixu, received the supreme Great Dao from our lineage ancestor, Master Niwan, in nearly its entirety, as further evidenced in this text. Yet this central transmission is not merely a precious raft for the Women’s School—those in the Men’s School who have penetrated its secrets in midnight meditation are likewise numerous.

The original text, having been copied and recopied through generations, contains many errors, which I have carefully corrected and emended. It is regrettable that *The Precious Raft of Dual Cultivation for the Men’s School* was taken away by the Yuan family of Changshan. I await its recovery, for it should not be lost. Within the texts of the Men’s School, traces of *The Precious Secrets of the Women’s School* also appear, though its transcribed copies suffer from many omissions. If these could be obtained, corrected, and printed together, they would form a complete work, and the two schools could be mutually referenced—no small contribution to the salvation of the world.

I record this to inform those gentlemen who possess the texts of the Men’s School: to destroy or discard sacred writings is to invite karmic retribution, as attested in the scriptures. Can one not be warned?

Respectfully inscribed by Min Yide of Jingaishan.
On the full moon of the first autumn month, in the gengyin year of the Daoguang reign (1830).

*Essentials of Women’s Alchemy*

Jiyi Zi of Jinxī, Fu Jinquan, has compiled this collection.

The Patriarch Lü’s *Lyrics on Ascending the Toad Palace* states:
The Kan and Li, Zhen and Dui divide at midnight and noon,
One must recognize one’s own ancestral lineage.
The thunder shakes the earth, rain falls upon the mountain peak,
Washing and nurturing the yellow sprout that emerges from Kun’s soil.
Seize the golden essence and firmly secure it,
Refining geng and jia to give birth to dragon and tiger.
When he asks who transmitted this to you,
Simply say, “The master’s surname is Lü.”

The *Three Mandates of the Sacred Mirror of Superior Medicines* states:
The subtlety of life is beyond words!
Within it, the workings shift in myriad transformations.
The human navel is called the “Gate of Life,”
Within it lies the Yellow Court, behind it the Dark Palace,
Above it the Mysterious Origin, below it the Sea of Qi,
To the left the sun, to the right the moon—all radiant.
The radiance of life also manifests in three forms:
The yellow radiance is the Cinnabar Field,
The white is the Womb Origin,
The purple is the Blood Origin.
The Blood Origin refers to the breasts,
Located one *cun* and two *fen* within, not the two breasts.
A man’s life resides in the Cinnabar Field,
The Cinnabar Field being the true soil that generates the elixir.
A woman’s life resides in the breasts,
The breasts being the essence of the mother’s qi, the wood spirit.
The Womb Origin forms the embryo,
The Blood Origin generates blood,
The Cinnabar Field produces the elixir.
The practice is conducted at the hours of zi and wu,
Focusing the mind to observe the hollow cavity within the breasts,
Breathing softly and continuously, exhaling less and inhaling more.
When the monthly signal arrives, guide it upward from the Cinnabar Field to the breasts.
The “monthly signal” does not refer to the arrival of menstruation.
The word “signal” is like a message arriving before a traveler returns home.
On the day the signal arrives, she will know it herself—
Perhaps with aching waist and legs, discomfort in the head and eyes, or loss of appetite.
This is the signal’s arrival, as blood is formed, which is qi.
One must concentrate and apply effort two and a half days prior.
If menstruation begins, the Red Dragon’s yin essence cannot be controlled;
Reckless circulation and misguided practice may harm many.
One must wait two and a half days after menstruation ends,
Testing with white silk—when its color turns golden, it is the sign that menstruation has ceased.
Then, following the previous method, guide it upward to sever it.
After several months, the menses will turn yellow,
The yellow will turn white,
And the white will vanish entirely.
Behold, this is the Dao of returning from existence to non-existence.
For women, blood serves as the kidneys, which are hollow cavities.
After forty-nine years, the waist dries, blood dries up, and vitality is lost.
Yet with prolonged nurturing, the Blood Origin revives like that of a maiden—
This is the marvel of generating existence from non-existence.
When one sees its presence, a single severing transforms it, and life is reborn.
At this stage, the work of cultivating life and nature becomes the same as for men.
Within the navel, wind arises, thunder rumbles, lightning flashes—
The transformation of the wood spirit.
Clouds gather, mists shift, flowers smile, birds take flight—
The generation of the earth spirit.
Who can fathom its wonders?

The Lazy Daoist says:
Why does a woman’s life have three aspects? They are the upper, middle, and lower.
The upper is the Yang Cavity,
The middle is the Yellow Chamber,
The lower is the Cinnabar Field.
In youth, one begins with the upper;
In decline, with the middle;
Only upon completion does one proceed with the lower.
Moreover, women are internally yang and externally yin;
First, one must sever the Red Dragon to preserve the body’s integrity,
Thus transforming Kan into Qian.
Then, employing the man’s method,
After a year of practice, the golden elixir will reside within—such is the principle.

The *Method of Cultivating the Great Yin* states:
The method of cultivating the Great Yin’s form
Largely resembles that of cultivating the Great Yang’s form, with minor differences.
At the outset, close the eyes and abide in spirit, resting deeply for a time,
Calming the heart and regulating the breath before concentrating the spirit into the qi cavity
(Located between the breasts, above the heart’s hollow).
Cross the hands to cradle the breasts,
Gently massaging them three hundred and sixty times.
Then, lightly draw the qi upward from the lower Cinnabar Field twenty-four times,
Still cradling the breasts, return to observe and regulate the breath.
With prolonged practice, true breathing will naturally ebb and flow,
Opening and closing, nurturing the barrier until spirit and qi are abundant,
True yang flourishes on its own,
The menstrual flow ceases,
And the breasts shrink like those of a man—this is called severing the Red Dragon.
After sustained practice,
There is no need to cradle the breasts or draw qi;
Simply concentrate the spirit within the qi cavity,
Returning the light to illuminate it—this is the Gate of the Mysterious Female.
True breathing becomes serene,
Utterly still and profoundly tranquil,
Yang qi steams and ascends, the river chariot reverses its course,
A myriad purple clouds gather at the Jade Palace,
A thousand white channels plant seeds in the Muddy Pellet.
One senses a single point of numinous light,
Neither inside nor outside,
Rising from the lower field to the Crimson Palace and Muddy Pellet,
Descending the heavy tower to return to the golden womb’s divine chamber.
After ten months of practice, the yang spirit manifests—
No different from the initial work of men.

The *Mysterious Subtleties of the Primordial* states:
Before a woman is born, at the moment of her parents’ union,
The father’s essence arrives first, the mother’s blood later,
Blood envelops essence to form the female body.
At the moment of a woman’s conception,
She first receives one *liang* of the mother’s lead qi,
Which first generates the right kidney,
Drawing a thread upward to form the two eyes,
And another thread downward to form the golden elixir.
From then on, every twelve days, one *zhu* of gui water is generated,
Every one hundred eighty days, one *liang* of gui water is generated.
Thereafter, every fifteen days, one *zhu* of gui water is generated,
Every year, one *liang* of gui water is generated,
Until at fourteen years, fourteen *liang* of gui water is generated in the Sea of Blood,
Combined with the two *liang* carried from the womb,
Completing the full measure of one *jin*.
Three hundred eighty-four *zhu*,
Corresponding to the three hundred eighty-four degrees of the celestial cycle,
Three hundred eighty-four days in a year,
Three hundred eighty-four lines in the *Book of Changes*—
The numbers of heaven and earth.
When yin reaches its extreme, yang is born;
When gui is exhausted, lead appears.
Thus, at fourteen, the celestial gui descends.
After the celestial gui descends at fourteen,
Over twenty-six months and seven and a half days,
One *liang* of gui water is depleted,
By forty-nine years, it is entirely exhausted.

Within lies a secret formula, difficult to express in full.

*Questions on the Difficulties of Cultivating the Real* asks: How do the starting points differ for men and women?

The answer: For men, the starting point lies in refining *qi* as the essential practice; for women, it lies in refining the form as the essential practice. Refining *qi* means to subdue one’s *qi*; subduing *qi* requires that the *qi* return, so that emptiness reaches its extreme and stillness becomes profound, root and origin reunite, and the White Tiger descends. Refining the form means to conceal one’s form; concealing the form requires that the form be extinguished. When the form is extinguished, the Four Great Elements enter emptiness, the limbs rot away, and the Red Channel is severed.

When the White Tiger descends in men, they revert to a youthful body, and the post-heaven essence no longer leaks. Thus, they may form the elixir and prolong life. When the Red Channel is severed in women, they transform into a male body, and the impure yin blood no longer flows downward. Thus, they may transcend death and enter life. Therefore, men’s cultivation is called *Taiyang Refining Qi*, while women’s cultivation is called *Taiyin Refining Form*.

Another question: Do women refining form not subdue *qi*?

The answer: Women’s nature is yin, so their *qi* is easily subdued, but the Red Channel is most harmful to the Dao. What matters most lies here. Thus, one begins by applying effort where it is most needed. Once the Red Channel is severed, the *qi* naturally becomes docile—not like men, whose nature is yang and whose *qi* is difficult to subdue. For example, if subduing *qi* takes a man three years, a woman may accomplish it in one.

If a woman of true fortitude obtains her teacher’s oral instructions and practices the *Taiyin Refining Form* method, she may attain the Dao in three to five years, with less effort than a man. Yet such women of fortitude are most rare. Only those whose resolve exceeds a man’s by a hundredfold can succeed. Those equal in strength to men cannot possibly do so!

Another question: The Great Dao makes no distinction between men and women—why then are there differences?

The answer: The Dao is the same, but its application differs. Since their natures and forms are not alike, though the Dao of life and destiny is one, the methods of practice differ greatly.

Question: How is the Red Channel severed?

Answer: The Red Channel arises from post-heaven yin *qi*; when yin *qi* stirs, impure blood flows. To transform the blood, first forge the *qi*. When the *qi* is transformed, the blood returns upward into the breasts. Red turns to white and circulates throughout the body, freeing one from the affliction of raging desire-fire.
