When desire-fire is extinguished, true fire emerges. From this point onward, stability and smooth progress ensure that preserving life and perfecting form are no longer difficult.

*Collected Explanations of the Female Elixir*
Edited by the Buddha of Immeasurable Kalpas

The Elder of Yuexi in Guangdong recounted the words of the Dark Heaven Supreme Emperor:

*The Book of Changes* states: "Qian is the father, Kun the mother," making the meaning of yin and yang abundantly clear. Only with heaven and earth do male and female come to be, so the Dao of yin and yang is self-evident. Thus, it is manifest that just as heaven and earth cannot be without male and female, so too must they exist. The male receives the transformations of Qian and Kun to complete his form, while the female inherits the harmonious union of Qian and Kun to possess her body. All who bear these forms and images possess the *qi* of Qian and Kun, standing together within the cosmos.

Now, in this era of compassionate ferrying and shared salvation, when the precious raft is universally poled, why should men alone be taught through manifold methods while the feminine principle is neglected? Guidance on the profound essence and wondrous subtleties of the male abounds like books filling a house to the rafters, yet methods and models for the deliverance of women remain pitifully few! With deep sorrow, I take up this topic alone. In this collection, though the words are vast, there is little systematic discourse—here, I distill their wonders into restraint.

The female body belongs to the yin image, but where then does yang return? The body is yin, while *qi* is yang. If *qi* is likened to form, yin and yang become indescribable; if *qi* is spoken of in terms of blood, yin and yang find their place. Blood is originally sweat, yet without *qi*, blood does not move. *Qi* contains *qi*, and thus the clear and turbid are distinguished. Blood is yin, yet without the yang *qi* stored within yin, *qi* does not flow. Having distinguished thus far, I must now shatter the truth in one breath:

The *Qi* Sea belongs to yang, containing yin within; the Blood Sea belongs to yin, harboring yang within. Between these cavities lies a dividing membrane, through which the twelve double-hours flow without cease. *(The Qi Sea and Blood Sea lie beneath the navel, separated by a membrane one cun and three fen apart.)* When yang reaches its peak, yin grows; when yin reaches its peak, yang is born. The two revolve and intersect, and after thirty such cycles, the monthly signal stirs of itself. What intersects is yin and yang, yet in truth, it is *qi* that effects their union.

This cavity, though one, divides into two. When the signal halts, *qi* surges; when the signal appears, *qi* leaks. Thus, when the monthly signal stirs, practice must cease. If *qi* leaks while practice continues, turbid *qi* will rush into the Mysterious Pass—how can this not be guarded against?

The male body channels *qi* from essence into the Mysterious Pass, while the female body steeps the Mysterious Pass in *qi* from blood. When the Mysterious Pass is full, the Lotus Cavity is full; when the Lotus Cavity is full, the drawing and replenishing begin to move. Only then does the descent of sweet dew arise. *(The above text is incomplete.)* Yet they do not know that the *qi* in a man’s essence is abundant, while the *qi* in a woman’s blood is faint—hence the names: man as yang, woman as yin.

Those who cultivate our Dao take severing the seven emotions as fundamental and cutting off the six desires as primary. Then, the faintest *qi* in women surpasses that of superior men. Why? A man’s heart is easily stirred, while a woman’s thoughts are somewhat still. Stirring leads to easy leakage of *qi*; stillness leads to easy growth of *qi*. One grows easily, the other leaks easily—how vast the discrepancy, like the distance of a thousand *li*!

A man’s seven lotuses are easy to gather but hard to release; a woman’s seven lotuses are easy to release and easy to gather. If she can remain unwavering in true sincerity, without waiting three to five years, sweet dew will descend constantly, and the seven lotuses will bloom perpetually. If blooming is easy, how could gathering be difficult? The distinction between male and female is thus made clear.

As for the words in this collection—speaking of emptiness, void, mystery, subtlety, spirit, and transformation—these are the great commonalities of men and women. Let me further clarify and distinguish their truth.

Why, then, is it called "embryo" for men but only "breath" for women, never "embryo"? Lest later generations misconstrue the term "embryo" and ultimately suffer false accusations! Alas! A woman’s breath, if not congealed, remains so; once congealed, it seals and solidifies; congealed again, it guards itself; congealed a third time, it roots firmly. Strengthening these three, her lotuses become easy to release and easy to gather. Can the chaste and resolute woman not hasten to awaken to this wonder?

Further, in discussing the Dao, a woman’s *qi* and breath are originally soft in nature; what is not soft arises from later harms. Those aspiring to transcend the dust must only guard against one word: rigidity. Always embrace one word: softness. If she constantly embodies gentle warmth without cease, then emptiness, subtlety, void, and mystery—all are stored within the word "softness," encompassing the myriad things.

Moreover, when a man’s spirit departs, his true nature must be utterly pure and yang before the opportunity for shedding the husk arises, for yang contains yin. When a woman’s spirit departs, her true nature differs from a man’s. Why? When a woman reaches the stage of the Three Yangs, she may transcend a hundred *li*; when she attains the union of the two purest and oldest yangs, once departed, she departs forever, without risk of premature demise. For a man, yang contains yin, with yin within and yang without; for a woman, yin contains yang, with yin without and yang within. When yang prevails, all yin readily retreats.

I now spare no truth, revealing it here, solely in the earnest hope that those who swiftly attain the real may multiply.

The Dark Heaven Supreme Emperor inscribed: Can you now know the true elixir of women? What I have distinguished is most certainly so—compared to other

Where there is method and where there is none, it is ever plainly revealed. Where there is thought and where there is none, it must yet be carefully discussed. Too much adherence—what fault is this? Too much attachment—what transgression is that? All stems from the worldly, mingled with what comes before and after. The "after" is the six desires; the "before" is the numinous origin. When before and after are used together, the numinous *qi* does not turn. The *qi* of prior Heaven is but a single thread. The three barriers and nine apertures—each aperture is thus. Once the later arises and mingles, the mysterious pass is blocked. The *qi* of prior Heaven is obstructed, and the nine apertures are unsettled. After a single sitting, joint by joint, bitterness ensues. The whole body stiffens, *qi* fails to pass the barriers. If one aperture remains unopened, affliction will cling. In your cultivation, who among you knows this? Without compassion, I would not descend to explain in detail—so that you may guard against calamity, and not blame the immortals for misleading you. By method, I would not have you all tremble in fear!

Between prior and posterior *qi*, only a thought’s breath divides. Thought is inherently hard to purify; it must follow nature. Do not rigidly fix thought, for rigidity blocks the pass. In the central field, *qi* gathers in its entirety. The immortals speak of "gathering"—gathering the prior Heaven. When posterior thought ceases, prior Heaven arises naturally. United as one, the three barriers are filled. Harmonizing yin and yang, the two link as pairs. Yin wanes, yang waxes, solidifying into a single mass. From this, the elixir grows; from this, the sprout takes hold.

Now observing sentient beings, each suffers from clinging illness. All belongs to prior and posterior, their boundaries undistinguished. I have now pointed this out—let each of you reflect and strive.

Before ascending the seat, first cultivate a state of ease—neither constrained nor bound, lively and natural. Only then ascend; no restraints shall linger. As thoughts arise, let them depart of their own accord. As they transform naturally, preserve only the wholeness of spirit. If thoughts accumulate, do not cling to them in the slightest. Close the eyes and contemplate sleep; the body dissolves, the form remains complete. Neither self nor other exists—only a lifeless mass. Through such practice, illness naturally subsides. No ailment shall arise, and the entire being relaxes in peace.

To rigidly fix thought is to block *qi*; fire then scorches the source. To forcefully direct *qi* is to scatter it; perverse flames blaze even brighter. Illness arises from this, burning away the true origin. In women, the Sea of Blood is where *qi* transforms and emerges. When perverse fire stirs, it steams through the vital origin. Blood gradually withers, and healing becomes difficult. When blood stirs, all the more should one relax and expand. Do not let restlessness arise; do not harbor anger. Thoughts should be purified further, spirit further stilled. As all distractions dissolve, sitting then becomes natural.

If one acts with impatience or anger, the central field is offended. Day and night, the heart burns, the mouth turns bitter, the tongue parched—all stems from this. Who discerns this cause? Those who cultivate and refine must not transgress even the slightest.

Even the slightest speck of dust on the casket harms the true origin. You remain unaware, yet suffering draws near. Chills and fever arise from imbalance. Do not claim to cultivate the Dao to cure illness and prolong life—if you fail to examine yourself, suffering will be immense.

At every moment, in every thought, scrutinize carefully. Avoid offense, avoid disturbance, and the elixir will grow effortlessly. No need to yearn—mystery unfolds of itself. No need for arduous effort—the pill forms through nine transformations. No need for strenuous sitting—every moment is Chan. In stillness or movement, in solitude or company, the wondrous elixir grows.

You who cultivate, your minds are not unwhole—yet later intrusions sever the primordial. Few escape illness; how then to blame the immortals? I now point this out—ponder it carefully. All wondrous methods are sharp as a blade, yet whole. Not a hair’s breadth may err, not a thread’s weight may cling.

Morning and evening, wander freely, at ease and unburdened. Whether eating or fasting, let it not weigh on your mind. Whether acting or still, do not circle in distraction. After a hundred days, wondrous signs will appear. After a year of practice, the ten thousand phenomena will align naturally.

Do not cling to the word *cultivate*; refine it further. If not bound by even a single word, transformation flows like a spring. Only then is it true cultivation, true refinement. Cultivation uproots evil; refinement restores wholeness. To refine the formed invites illness; to refine the formless is true mystery.

Today, I stand before you, sweeping away the ten thousand phenomena. First guard against the six thieves—yet let it be natural. To guard with intent is the hardest of hardships. To guard without intent is to stand firm. Unbreakable, what need is there for defense?

Women and men alike, unite in diligence. Wherever you dwell, whatever vow you hold, the matter is ordinary—do not see it as difficult. How simple it is: only distinguish worldly ties. When thoughts cease, you are Buddha; when desires cease, you are immortal. Immortal and Buddha differ not—they ferry all from the dusty world.

You inherently possess the mind—refine it into a golden immortal. Without refining, it forms itself; without establishing, it stands itself. Sweep away thoughts and delusions—do not let them cling. Joy day after day—this is the immortal. Persist thus, and why fear the Western Heaven?

I come to ferry you, to restore your golden body whole. Measure yourselves—value your own dedication. My words may seem shallow, but their wonder lies in deeper exploration. From beginning to end, the great method is complete.

The Golden Sand Ancient Buddha says:
The method is not wondrous, nor the formula—wonder lies in the firing time, the foremost essential.
The Dao arises from the Limitless; the Limitless originally enfolds the aperture.
Essence issues from here, *qi* stirs from here, the medicine is born from here, the embryo is preserved from here.
Examine closely—the mechanism leaps of itself, alive and flowing, deep and vast.
All take root in this aperture.

From a broad view, the hundred vessels branch from the Limitless to shape form.
From a subtle perspective, it belongs to the formless and imageless, yet originally encompasses all transformations.
Men and women share this supreme treasure—only divided into two paths: blood and essence.
Male essence ascends to become immortal; female blood rises straight to the heart aperture.
Thus, each has its own method, its own illumination.
Though women’s practice employs the *congealing* method, do not tightly grasp the mind-ground.
If the mind-horse is hard to tether, even a fleeting thought stirs the Sea of Blood.

The Sea of Blood and the Sea of *Qi* are distinct—before the Sea of Blood lies seven-tenths.
Here is the aperture of the Sea of *Qi*, located in the wondrous gate neither above nor below, neither left nor right.
Blood transforms, *qi* congeals—mysterious is the transmutation of postnatal *qi* into the primordial.
A single taint of human desire severs it—with the postnatal but no primordial, you become mortal.
Know that immortal and mortal differ here.

The Dao here is not yet the Dao; *qi* must return to the root, the Limitless aperture,
to congeal this spiritual sprout, to form the pill when the firing time arrives.
How to distinguish this point of before and after? The firing time must not be lacking.
If the Water of *Gui* has not yet come, practice diligently without slack.
Morning and evening, be lively and joyful.

Too loose, the spirit scatters; too tight, the *qi*-aperture closes.
It must be neither loose nor tight, neither late nor early.
Not dwelling is dwelling; not good is the good.
Not congealing is congealing; not illuminating is illumination.
This firing time is most subtle—women must attend to it carefully.
Without recognizing this point, it is not cultivation.
The words *cultivation* and *refinement* must be forgotten.
To cling too much to *refinement* is to leave traces—one clinging stirs the roots of illness.
Once this illness takes hold, medicine cannot reach it.

People say illness roots in the organs—this illness hides in the marrow’s path.
How can medicine remove it? Only by the single yang point piercing the inner aperture can this illness be eradicated.

Good, good, good. I will show you another principle, peel back layers of the firing time.
Without layer-by-layer revelation, confusion remains, and illness deepens.
*Qi*’s surging must return to the aperture. When movement arises, stillness cannot begin.
Let it be unknown, unperceived—return to the root.
At the first stirring, life and destiny, yin and yang meet.
Water and fire intermingle, the Limitless divides, the Supreme Ultimate enfolds, transforming into primordial chaos.

Sit and slightly refine—congeal the formless, do not hold to form.
A hint of stillness—do not seize it. Let it be natural and quiet.
Do not rashly engage the conscious mind.

Let everything go—sleep as it comes, dullness as it comes.
Do not err in the slightest shock.
Few recognize this firing time.
Most mistake stillness for delusion—when the body moves, *qi* scatters, becoming demonic obstruction.
A thousand, ten thousand thoughts swirl.
At this moment, descend from the platform, take a walk, then return to rest.
Wait a moment, then ascend again to nurture stillness—stillness will naturally return to the root.

If forced sitting is imposed, disease takes root within.
With too many deluded thoughts, first sleep, then apply focused spirit—
where there is no delusion, do not force it; where delusion arises, refine the heart-mind.
The word "refine" must be understood flexibly:
a faint congealment, a state of dim indistinction—
only then is it the method of *ninglian* (congealing and refining),
only then is it the first vehicle of entering stillness,
this is precisely the firing time of ascending the platform.

When movement occurs, the firing time must be clearly distinguished:
the moment of movement must be sensed, and when sensed, do not let worldly dust intrude.
Here lies the boundary between heaven and humanity,
here the division between immortals and mortals.
It is like the body of an infant yet unawakened—
the precelestial body is already aware, while the postcelestial gives rise to this realm.
Examine this closely:
at the first instant of awareness, there is still a trace of dim indistinction;
once awareness arises again, ten thousand thoughts entangle.
The words "first" and "again" are like lightning—
in a single flash, all chaotic images vanish.
The correct thought listens to the division of *qi*;
if deluded thoughts disturb the congealing and refining,
advance one layer—still listen to the *qi* returning yin and yang,
and when both are restored to their origin, wander freely again.
In applying this effort, never slacken—
apart from this method, there is no higher vehicle.

I now reveal this true and wondrous secret:
let men and women alike bear it in mind.
If not refining the true seed with a true heart,
carelessly leaking celestial mechanism invites thunderous retribution.
Though the method seems simple and plain,
only through careful reflection does its subtlety become clear.
This is the practice before attaining the Golden Elixir,
a daily gate one must never depart from.

The Perfected of White Lotus says:
Establish resolve with steadfast integrity,
and never let worldly dust pollute your being.
The method is fundamentally level and easy—
in its circulation, do not pause or linger.
At times the method should be applied,
but know not to be overly rigid.
At times the method should be set aside,
silently guarding your original true nature.
Movement and stillness mutually interpenetrate,
moment by moment aligning with the heart-mind of heaven.
The chaste woman originally has no method—
this is but a touch to the eye.

Blood and *qi* wax and wane;
the work of nurturing must run deep.
With time, blood transforms into *qi*,
white essence pervades the entire body.
Naturally, yin completes yang,
and the red dust no longer stirs the heart.
Only then can the *Qian* body be achieved,
only then can the highest truth be realized.
Even the slightest deceitful thought
may yet cause one to fall into the abyss.

The Perfected of White Lotus says:
Stages are the steps of cultivation;
chastity and stillness, free from dust, are the first dhyāna.
Add to this the refinement and nurturing of true *qi*—
yin descends, yang ascends, revealing the Mysterious Pass.
The Mysterious Pass is not sought outside the body—
it is found within an inch of space to seek the Great Elixir.
When the heart-mind is still, the spirit at ease,
vibrantly and freely circulate the *Zhoutian*.
*Qi* returns to its source, blood returns to its source—
gently refine them within the furnace.
Neither scorching in summer nor freezing in winter,
warmly nurture this true beauty.
After ten months, the Elixir is complete;
three years of nursing follow naturally.
Naturally ascend to the Great Brahma Heaven,
naturally ascend to the Great Brahma Heaven.

The Ancient Buddha of Golden Sand says:
From whence does the Female Elixir arise?
Man and woman do not correspond,
woman and man differ greatly.
The male elixir transforms essence into *qi*,
*qi* into spirit, spirit into emptiness—
when emptiness reaches its extreme and stillness is profound,
the Elixir naturally coalesces.
The female elixir transforms blood into *qi*,
*qi* into spirit, spirit into emptiness—
in the emptiness of nonbeing, the Elixir naturally forms.
Yet though *qi* arises from blood, there are two interpretations:
if the heart-mind is unsettled, thoughts impure,
the body restless, *qi* unbalanced,
then blood cannot transform into *qi*,
and blood remains mere blood.
If *qi* does not manifest as *qi*, blood becomes entirely turbid,
and the monthly flow appears.
This flow is inherently foul and turbid—
how can it transform into *qi*?
What transforms into *qi* is blood,
but what enables this transformation is the primordial *qi* within the blood.
What is primordial *qi*?
Blood is the essence-*qi* that pervades the entire body.
With this blood, essence-*qi* is stored;
without it, *qi* has no place to reside.
Blood is like seawater—
when water congeals, *qi* congeals;
when it surges upward, rain and dew descend.
The human body has blood like the sea—
thus blood naturally transforms into *qi* and ascends throughout the body,
then flows through the hundred vessels.
When the hundred vessels are connected, a single point descends—
from this, the hope of the Elixir’s formation arises.
Otherwise, if the mind is filled with worldly concerns,
daily entangled in external affairs,
with a temper hasty and reckless,
drawn by worldly splendor,
plagued by sorrow and depression,
disturbed by deluded thoughts,
never a moment of tranquility—
then turbid *qi* blocks true *qi*,
heaven and earth do not commune, yin and yang are not harmonized,
cold and heat are not regulated, the *Zhoutian* does not align,
and disease becomes inevitable in nearly every case.
This is not the fault of the Dao—
it is truly the fault of the person!

I now point this out to all beings:
each should carefully reflect and comprehend.
Do not say the Dao is not true—
the problem lies only in your heart not being true!
If your heart is truly sincere,
sweep away all floating thoughts,
discard all worldly splendor,
soften your temperament,
banish all violence,
free yourself from worries and attain a joyful spirit,
cut off external affairs—
then heavenly *qi* descends, earthly *qi* ascends,
and primordial true *qi* naturally flows forth,
filling the sea of blood.
*Qi* then naturally connects with spirit-*qi*.
If you do not sit, so be it—
but once you sit, it happens of itself,
within which there is an inexplicable wonder,
a realm entirely different from all human worlds.
Only then do you realize the Dao is not empty,
immortality is not false,
and the secret does not mislead—
it only requires self-nature to awaken itself.

I now offer another elixir of words:
Some say that if the Red Dragon is not slain, the Elixir cannot form,
and the Dao cannot be achieved—
but if blood is exhausted, *qi* is also exhausted.
Just as when a man’s essence is depleted and the Elixir is difficult to form,
the principle is the same.
For men, essence; for women, blood—
neither should be entirely cut off.
*Qi* departs from blood, and *qi* has no way to arise;
blood transforms into *qi*, and essence begins to flow.
If one claims that blood must be exhausted to refine the Elixir,
why do young women with withered blood fall ill instead?
This ultimately does not depart from the consideration of blood.

Others say that after years of refinement, there is no effect—
not because there is no secret,
but truly because the heart-mind has no moment of stillness.
Even if one sits morning and night,
not a single hour in the twelve is tranquil—
even if there is stillness, it lasts only a few moments.
When does *qi* have time to transform?

When does the spirit congeal? When does the Elixir coalesce?
Year after year, one merely becomes a dullard!
Those who claim to cultivate the Dao or preserve chastity,
yet remain uninvolved in worldly affairs—
I observe their reality, and they differ little from ordinary folk.

Others say: so-and-so has obtained the true secret,
or so-and-so has practiced for many years yet achieved nothing.
Little do they know that those who gain the true wondrous secret
begin with diligence but end in slackness;
those who practice for many years merely wait in complacency.
To cultivate the Dao in this manner is to deceive the Dao most gravely!

Now I exhort you, all beings:
When I speak of your wealth, it cannot compare;
when I speak of your nobility, it is incomparable;
when I speak of your clothing and food, they pale beside mine.
Yet I have already severed all attachments in this very moment—
what difficulty do you have in letting go?
Those who cannot sever attachments are truly deluded,
and in their delusion, they fear they will become beings without affinity—
how lamentable!

For the immortals and buddhas, with compassion, deliver the world;
people must not abandon themselves.
If they could become immortals and buddhas, I would rejoice,
for my heart is set on universal salvation—
only do not cut yourselves off from me.

Samantabhadra Bodhisattva says:
Morning and night, one cultivates in hope of forming the Golden Elixir.
The mercury of the Elixir is not the unrefined Elixir.
The Elixir resides within the body, formless and traceless.
Where there is trace, it is not wondrous;
where there is no trace, it is utterly mysterious.
When mystery abides, the Elixir is complete—
without mystery, it cannot be spoken of.
To refine with intention is to waste the mind’s monkey;
only when refinement occurs without deliberate refinement
is it called the Great Elixir.
The Elixir descends from emptiness, one with heaven and earth.
Tangible *qi* is not the wondrous explanation;
the formless origin contains all phenomena.
Once attained, it is eternally attained—
emptiness swirling in emptiness.

When things arise, here the first signs appear;
when things flourish, here the spark ignites;
when things withdraw, here the wonder is mastered.
What has form and image is called the posterior heaven;
what is imageless and shadowless is the prior heaven.
The posterior heaven is generated and completed;
the prior heaven is the origin of signs.
In human life, the principle is fundamentally one.
Imageless and intangible, it conceals a mystery within.
The posterior heaven obscures it, and the mystery ceases to be mysterious.
Now I reveal the wondrous method, having refined it for years.
Who does not know this? Yet later generations find it hard to speak of.
Once the spirit is recognized, thoughts are not yet a clear pool.
Too often, human desires intrude; too rarely is the mystery of the Dao glimpsed.
Seven days to return—yet even this is difficult.
The heart is thick with dust, the spirit steeped in delusion.
Neither bright nor pure, neither clean nor dry,
both spirit and *qi* are harmed—how can the pass be opened?
If the pass is not opened, how can the aperture begin?
If the aperture does not open, how can the drawing and adding be set in motion?
If drawing and adding are not set in motion, one sits on the meditation cushion in vain.

Now I speak again of gathering and preserving the spirit whole.
Gathering is self-gathering, yet it holds a mystery.
The moment a thought stirs, it turns of itself.
Its emergence must have its time, tested in the central field.
The previously revealed wondrous method moves as if moving,
yet as if uninvolved.
This "as if" movement severs heaven and earth.
When suddenly it arises "as if," the maiden and mercury unite.
This point is most wondrous, never before spoken of.
Now I reveal it in detail—do not transmit it lightly.

The classics and scriptures on the Elixir each proclaim:
All speak of "as if," of the maiden uniting with the phoenix.
Yet this is only half the story, without distinction of boundary,
without division of time, without precedence.
Now I speak further, to be studied in detail:
When "as if" moves, prior and posterior both partake.
Knowing the "as if" movement, the womb has its key.
When it moves in profound obscurity, "as if" occurs naturally—
only then is the test understood.
The origin of the spirit’s emergence:
To move knowing it moves is still posterior heaven;
to not know the sudden movement is "as if" in joy.
Indescribably wondrous, boundless delight—
only then is it called "as if" movement, and the Great Elixir is formed.
Witnessing this wondrous realm, worldly affinities vanish of themselves.
No need to sweep away appearances—all thoughts are relinquished.
The skandhas do not cling to emptiness; emptiness is naturally empty.
Not clinging to the form of emptiness, all realms are an empty pool.
The movement of heaven and earth, I am one with the whole;
the stillness of heaven and earth, I am one with the mystery.
The arising of heaven and earth, I share in it;
the withdrawal of heaven and earth, I am one with the origin.
When one reaches this point, the Great Awakening may begin to be spoken of.
Without reaching this realm, even immortality is difficult to attain—
how much more the Great Awakening? How lightly can it be spoken of!

Now I reveal the turning of "as if,"
the mechanism fully exposed, the wondrous method boundless.

The Queen Mother of the Jasper Pool says:
The true maiden is originally a child’s body,
distinguished only by purity and turbidity.
Though lead and mercury are complete,
alas, they have already transformed into form.
Once entering the womb,
they can no longer be called by their true names.
Having fallen into the posterior heaven,
how can they take flight?
Even if the primordial *qi* is fully rounded,
it must still be refined into undifferentiated oneness.
Only by returning from being to non-being
can one speak of returning to the root.

As for the principle of returning,
women have not understood its melody.
They constantly cling and guard,
their eyes fixed on the breast’s courtyard.
Purity and turbidity are hard to distinguish;
how can *qi* congeal in confusion?
Purity ascends and turbidity descends—
this is the constant principle one hears of.
If one over-fixates and *qi* does not move,
turbid *qi* rises instead.
When pure *qi* sinks,
how can one recognize the spirit’s numen?

Women have no other secret—
liveliness is the essential scripture.
When the heart is lively, *qi* naturally flourishes;
when the spirit is lively, *qi* naturally becomes numinous;
when intention is lively, *qi* naturally stabilizes;
when nature is lively, *qi* naturally ascends.
Liveliness is not external—
in the heart, no trace is left.
When the heart is settled, one sits upright;
sitting upright, the breath is harmonized.
When breath is harmonized, the body transforms,
and true joy arises within.
In joy, one forgets joy,
and the whole body’s *qi* merges into oneness.
Naturally, it returns to the ancestral aperture,
with no trace of mechanism remaining.
If one can be still for a moment, for a moment it returns to the central courtyard;
if one can be still for an hour, for an hour *qi* circles back.
If one can be still every morning and night,
in a month, the practice bears numen.
In a hundred days, there will be signs;
in twelve years, one will surely ascend.

How can one achieve such swift attainment?
The primordial *qi* has not yet leaked or collapsed.
Alas, too much restraint—
*qi* and blood remain undifferentiated.
At times *qi* transforms into blood,
at times blood transmutes into silver.
In transformation, not the slightest awareness arises;
in a trance, it shifts and inclines again.
Thus, through years and months,
the numinous efficacy remains unseen.
Instead, one withers into desiccation,
and illness clings to the body.
Without contemplating the great Dao’s unfolding,
how can one discern the luminous truth?

Xiang Yi Gu Mu says:
Now I discourse on the profound principle,
speaking solely of the Queen of Methods for women.
Woman is inherently a tranquil being,
within yin, yang is also contained.
To guard stillness is ever difficult to still—
mechanisms lie hidden within the yellow center.
Though stillness is her original nature,
governing softness still relies on firmness.
Firmness is the master of yang,
softness the repository of yin.
Recognizing firmness within softness,
one may attain strength within weakness.
*Qi* and blood arise later,
while the ancestral aperture spontaneously emits yang.
When one *qi* flows through the four limbs,
the hundred vessels all become nectar.
Why sever the Red Dragon?
When turbidity is exhausted, radiance flows.
This distinction is fundamental—
women are divided in two.
The female body is not whole,
for primordial *qi* has already been harmed.
To restore the *qi* of Kun’s yin,
activation begins in the breasts.
With the subtlest application of true intention,
guide the fire with precious care.
If one is even slightly too overt,
blood stagnates and illness lurks unseen.
Move with neither intent nor absence of intent—
neither assist nor forget.
Over time, *qi* returns to its source,
and yin *qi* naturally perishes.
Yin subdued, yang ascends,
refining into the firmness of Qian’s primordial yang.
For virgins, this method is unnecessary—
only true stillness from beginning to end suffices.
When *qi* is still, blood transforms of itself;
when spirit is clear, *qi* naturally rises.
Without knowing or recognizing,
transformation is wholly contained.
The celestial circuit divides by degrees,
unobstructed, harmonizing yin and yang.
Beginning with blood transforming into *qi*,
culminating in softness becoming firmness.
In a month, *qi* converges and meets—
expelling turbidity, retaining primordial yang.
When turbidity is exhausted, purity ascends,
naturally cleansing the foul intestines.
Radiance shines with true brilliance,
the bone marrow reveals its lustrous glow.
If the original source is not purified,
thoughts and cares will secretly injure.
When fire blazes, the whole body grows hot—
this is the true yang manifesting contrary to the Dao.
If one knows the method to halt the fire,
without intent, silently forget.
Perverse fire instantly vanishes,
and true primordial *qi* remains unharmed.
This is the true oral transmission—
women must be vigilant.
If one can truly be thus,
the Dao will be attained and the Queen of Methods met.

Bailian Zhenren says:

Those with aspirations beyond the dusty world,
set their resolve without bias—
yet must gather and restrain both outer and inner,
for stillness unmoved is the root-source.
Sit in tranquility long, and vexations scatter;
even slight constraint makes *qi* hard to perfect.
Women are inherently tranquil—
in stillness they refine,
true *qi* leaps and surges of itself,
forgetting intent, forgetting words, abiding in utmost goodness,
unshifting, unchanging, uniting with the Mysterious Pass.
Let *qi* flow without stagnation,
let it settle without forced addition.
In refining, neither overdone nor deficient—
cold and dryness both are bias.
If one can practice thus,
merit will be complete and the primordial seen.
How is the primordial seen?
Only when the heart holds no entanglements,
unbound and unclinging, spirit moves freely,
spirit free, life and nature twine together,
spinning ceaselessly, yin and yang meet,
their union fills and perfects true *qi*.
Perfect and full, it flows through the crown,
then descends, dripping upon the seven lotuses.
The lotus, nourished by sweet dew, revives at its heart—
in seven days and seven dawns, it blooms in full,
the lotus heart unfolds, the true heart appears,
the self-so Tathāgata pervades the great chiliocosm,
roaming freely through the worlds of the great chiliocosm,
gazing upon the sea of suffering at the edge of the red dust,
then knowing the immortals’ subtle pointers were not in vain,
truly not misleading those who board the compassionate vessel.
Women of chastity, refine with urgency—
surely you will bear fruit and wander the Western Heaven.

Guanghui Ancient Buddha says:
Now I point to a single firing time,
for chaste women to observe together.
Do not force sitting when weary,
but roam freely, unconstrained.
Let it be naturally released, naturally gathered—
when thoughts are still, spontaneously enter meditation;
when thoughts are not still, do not sit,
for forced sitting severs *qi* from the ancestral source.
This point of primordial *qi* arises in stillness,
growing gradually in ease, the two entwined.
Even in this entwining there is a test:
if the spirit grows dull and craves sleep,
then lightly sit upon the meditation bench—
in one sitting, true *qi* gathers naturally.
Without this method, spirit cannot unite;
with this practice over time, the crown becomes full.
Only by dissolving all worldly burdens
can the postnatal be shed and the primordial embraced.
If not among the chaste of both kinds,
do not covet this practice in vain.
If you covet it, sleep-demons will form,
and spirit and *qi* will be blocked at the apertures.
Again, for the chaste woman’s practice:
at the *zi* hour, when yang stirs, sit before the bench.
Silently recite the Buddha’s name thirty to fifty times,
then proceed as instructed before.
If at the *zi* hour the body does not move,
celestial and demonic forces will clash here.
If you can shift the body to dissolve demonic burdens,
a single Buddha’s name will resound through heaven and earth.
At the *chen* hour, do not move lightly—
reckless movement disrupts the spirit’s mechanism and harms the root.
This is the supreme secret of true cultivation,
for chaste women to observe together.
Why distinguish two kinds in refining the firing time?
The chaste woman’s spirit-source resides between both.
The faithful widow’s resolve may be firm,
yet before cultivation, she has often suffered depletion—
her inner store of primordial *qi* is already damaged,
and she must rekindle the furnace to restore the original.
At the *chen* hour, rise to sit only when spirit and *qi* are full;
if insufficient and unmoving, the elixir is further harmed.
Why is the elixir named as if it had form?
The elixir is *qi* congealed, called the Mysterious.
The Mysterious is another name for the elixir—
when spirit is complete, *qi* naturally returns in dual reunion.
This is the true firing time for the chaste woman:
after a hundred days of practice, then refine the elixir.
Women inherently hold true yin concealing true yang—
thus at the *chen* hour, apply effort in practice.
At the *zi* hour, when the first yang stirs,
it moves freely, circulating the microcosmic orbit.
When the first yang stirs, true yin flourishes—
sitting then, one naturally embraces and returns.
This points to the wondrous celestial mechanism within—
attend carefully, ponder deeply, do not speak idly.
The oral instructions are all provisional;
true cultivation lies in relinquishing all thoughts.
If you can cast off the ten thousand conditions, pure as water,
the bright pearl shines in your palm, radiant and full.

Queen Mother of the Jasper Pool says:
I now remind you:
women’s golden elixir
advances by degrees,
finds ease through effort.
From below to above,
from later to earlier.
Slowly refine,
gradually simmer.

Neither slack nor tense—
the fire’s timing comes naturally.
When the appointed time arrives and water surges,
the Northern Sea roars to the heavens.
Like a river in flood,
hasten to steer your boat.
If waves toss wildly,
the boat will surely be lost.

For women who cultivate stillness,
the sea’s waters are most steadfast.
When the term is fulfilled,
it blazes like wildfire across the plain.
If practice is not paused,
disaster will strike before your brows.
Stop for one seven-day cycle,
a second seven brings no harm.
Do not call this laziness—
the work is hard to resume.
Wait until the dew is clear,
then speak of entering the mystery.
If you do not wait until it is exhausted,
foul qi will mingle within.

When the tide of water floods the sea,
the time has come in full cycle.
Every aperture gathers and meets,
the microcosmic orbit is complete.
Flowing together, they descend—
thus it is called "roaring to the heavens."
Like a river’s tide,
a hundred streams and springs,
mountain brooks and small valleys,
all converge as one.
This is called "flooding"—
the principle is clearly spoken.

If stillness is cultivated without pause,
you will meet the appointed time in meditation.
When true fire arises,
foul impurities are burned away.
But if it becomes a chronic ailment,
the medicinal sprouts will not heal.
Not only the Northern Sea—
foulness dries to desiccation.
A hundred vessels are blocked,
the vital center hardens.
Strength cannot break through the blood,
dryness enters the marrow.

I now reveal this clearly,
speaking in detail.
Beware the strange calamity—
each one fears the difficulty.
This is the wondrous method,
never lightly transmitted.
I now point it out,
to encourage women of virtue.

Pause longer when the term arrives,
and you will not fall ill.
On the day the term is fulfilled,
liveliness comes first.
Do not worry, do not fret—
cast aside the seven emotions.
Sweep away the six desires,
abide in ease.
Free and unburdened,
do not crave cold drinks.
Spicy and pungent things—
do not let them touch your lips.
Illness will depart naturally,
and you will live in peace for a lifetime.

Within this karmic thread,
there are several strands.
In this life’s pursuit of the Dao,
past lives’ grievances accumulate.
Grievance repays grievance—
how can the body be at peace?
Often afflicted by illness,
karma is hard to complete.
Those who abandon the path midway
are secretly entangled.
Though life may not be joyful,
in death they attain immortality.
If one can complete the work in life,
they hold the Golden Immortal in their grasp.
From immortality upward,
they ascend straight to the Western Heaven.
The two paths of life and death—
why cling to them in the heart?

I now speak this to you,
all worthy women.
Suffering within suffering—
do not crave rich delicacies.
Let it pass just a little,
sweep away worldly ties.
When worldly ties are swept clean,
the true spirit is whole.
Preserve this single point,
and drift among the immortal mountains.
If you wish to climb the jeweled pagoda,
climb as high as you desire.
If you wish to reach Potalaka,
explore as far as your feet may go.
If you wish to wander the Eastern Capital,
roam at leisure.
If you wish to reach the Western Land,
the Buddha will guide you across the pass.
If you wish to step into the Numinous Empyrean,
advance as you will.

What I have said
contains no falsehood.
Women’s practice
is the same as men’s.
Only the stages differ—
the ground itself is not mysterious.
All wondrous transformations
are no different from men’s.
You must awaken to this—
it is all recorded in these writings.
Not a single error—
each must cultivate in seclusion.

Remember this well—
my heart rejoices greatly.

*Resonant Moon Wenchong Ancient Buddha annotates:*

Disaster arises before the brows when the tide of blood surges like fire—if you do not cease practice and instead fight fire with fire, the blood will overheat and wither into desiccation. The "sea tide" refers to the time when the moon’s influence flows forth; you must cease practice and sit in stillness. If you persist for several days, it is like sailing a boat on a river, knowing the waves rage yet deliberately setting forth—you will surely lose everything. Remember this well, and do not neglect it!

*Resonant Moon Wenchong Ancient Buddha says:*
Though the Dao is divided into stages, it is merely to tether the heart of the cultivator. If we speak of chastity, no refinement is needed—only the two words *true* and *still* hold profound mystery. Woman is inherently a vessel of stillness; opening and closing arise naturally, the numinous qi manifests of itself, blood transforms into golden elixir, yin qi dissolves entirely, and true fire steams within the marrow. What obstruction or illness remains? What need is there for the "slaying of the dragon"? Transformation occurs not by force, but of itself—Earth’s position turns to Heaven.

*Resonant Moon Wenchong Ancient Buddha says:*
Purity and sincerity are the wondrous mystery. Do not let later-arising thoughts disturb the primordial. When the mind is settled, sit long and steadfast; when the spirit grows dull, do not probe rigidly. The true nature shines bright as the moon, the Great Mystery Gate clear as autumn waters. Lively yet unstained, unobstructed, it drifts in profound stillness as if at ease. The single spirit moves, and dross dissolves; joyous realms unfold like fish and kites. Do not confine the true self within the false body—only then can you return to the root and restore the original.

*Resonant Moon Wenchong Ancient Buddha says:*
The jeweled lotus throne and pagoda await such a one—truly, truly, the original cause is never obscured. First, clearly distinguish the pure from the turbid; with long sitting, numinous qi gradually arises. Do not fear the rising and steaming of primordial qi—let it ascend and descend, naturally harmonizing. Neither forget nor force the true firing times; whether intentional or unintentional, do not linger. If vexation arises, walk and disperse it; if rigidity takes hold, the spirit will not settle. Movement of thought is fire, not true medicine; stillness of nature, unstained, is true gold. Refinement requires no division into stages—once the dross is washed away, clarity comes of itself. No need to seek other true oral instructions—tonight’s words must be strictly heeded.

*Golden Sand Ancient Buddha says:*
I awaken the women cultivating truth within their karmic conditions: chastity and its opposite arise from the roots of hearing. Know this wondrous secret—it is not without method, for the method itself emerges from the secret. Constantly wash the mortal body and return to the realm of stillness; diligently nurture the immortal heart, and filth melts like ice. Value the immortal root and minimize worldly disturbances; sever mortal bones and exchange them for an immortal frame. Clearly and constantly reflect upon your former self; the seven stars of the Dipper radiate brilliance. Let the eyes’ spiritual light ever arise within; let the ears’ numinous qi ever close their gates. Let the nose not be drawn by worldly fragrances—true fragrance stirs and pierces the seven stars. Let the mouth shut out coarse, vulgar breath; in walking, standing, sitting, and lying, chant the Buddha’s name. Let the hands not cling to worldly affections—often turn the pages of scriptures and recite the sutras. Let the feet stand firm upon the Terrace of Heaven; wander freely through the Elixir Chamber and Meditation Palace. If your steps are light and your heart sways, delusion stirs the ears and eyes, disturbing the spirit. When the spirit is disturbed, the heart follows external conditions, scattering without return—how can qi be harmonized? If inner absorption is uneven, outer qi intrudes; when inner and outer unite in a single breath, you return to the root. If the inner master does not waver, the spirit steadies itself; if it wavers and does not settle, qi cannot fill. Even if true mechanism stirs, weariness without return disturbs the Yellow Court. When breath is even, the primordial moves; the acquired yields to the primordial’s course. If you can contemplate death and sever the acquired, the primordial will arise from left and right. This mechanism comes naturally—no technique or secret instruction is needed to illuminate it. I have now revealed the supreme wonder; may you, in your mortal frame, reflect and act upon it. Together, guard the true aspiration and do not covet secrets; I point out your barriers and strengthen your resolve. If your aspiration aligns with mine, if your heart can be as clear as mine—if your heart is as clear as water, after three years I will come to you in person. I will manifest to deliver your virginal body; my form will soar through empty space like clouds. My form will always dwell within your heart—your heart is my Avalokiteśvara. The Bodhisattva Avalokiteśvara will always be present; when your merit is complete and the fruit ripens, you will accompany my body. A single lotus can transform into a thousand myriad blossoms; a thousand myriad lotuses will cover your body. If you do not tread this swift path, where else will you bow to the World-Honored One?

*Golden Sand Ancient Buddha says:*
I have no other method—only the supreme means of gathering the heart, the most wondrous way of sweeping thoughts—each is clearly pointed out to you. The wandering of heart and intent is nothing other than failing to chew and contemplate the Great Dao. Consider this body dwelling in the red dust—it is like being in a sea of suffering. This life falls into the human realm; the next may be lost, and suffering will be unbearable. As the saying goes, "Once the human body is lost, ten thousand kalpas will pass in difficulty." Fortunately, you have now encountered the Great Dao. Sitting on the meditation cushion, neither the heart needs gathering, nor the intent observing, nor thoughts sweeping, nor the monkey tethering. Have a body as if without a body; let the heart be as if without barriers. Neither observe your heart nor memorize your dharma words. Simply take a single intent and place it between the breasts—if the heart is unsettled for a moment, do not cast it aside for that moment; if two or three thoughts are impure, do not idle for those two or three. Yet do not bind it too tightly—it should rest in the space between intention and non-intention. If too tight, qi will stagnate; if inattentive, thoughts will stray. I have another method, also a supreme elixir for gathering the heart: constantly recite the classics. Whether chanting aloud or silently, recite a sutra once—this takes only a moment or two. When you feel dazed, thoughts will naturally fall away, and effortlessly the merit will be complete. After a hundred days, you will perceive the primordial; if sleep demons arise during sitting, upon waking, immediately engage in meditation. With a clear aspiration, no need to gather—when thoughts arise, use this method to collect deluded thoughts. Truly difficult! Truly difficult!

Truly difficult to drag you from these entanglements! Endlessly severing the reds and greens, the gaudy robes of worldly adornment. Unseverable are the southern fields and northern lands, the long strings of affection for sons and daughters-in-law. Even with the powers of immortals and buddhas, it is hard to ferry you to the immortal gardens, hard to carry you aboard my boat. I urge you not to retreat, lest you cast your golden elixir into the boundless sea of karmic debt. In life, you knew no repentance; only in death do you awaken.

Awaken now, chaste maidens, each reflect deeply: the roots of your past lives were not shallow. In this life, you have encountered a rare opportunity—no one has led you by the hand, yet you have heard the profound mysteries of the Great Dao expounded. Each of you, by your own heart’s resolve, has seen through the red-dust world, severed the seven emotions, and remained unstained. Truly, this is a rarity through the ages, a woman who is a marvel among men. Yet the eye is the chief of the six thieves—it cannot bear the sight of reds and greens, the allure of gaudy blossoms. A single thought turns you back; in every matter, you crave appearances. False human sentiments waste true mindfulness. I now urge you: do not cling to these.

Do not fret that these affairs will bear no fruit, nor that this great karmic bond will go unfulfilled. Do not worry that no one from Mount Potalaka will call to you. If you can sever all worldly attachments, naturally golden boys and jade maidens will come to tend you at all hours, ensuring your Dao-qi is not disturbed by demons, your Dao-methods not ensnared by evil. Press on to full awakening, unstained and untainted—your body will grow light, your form at ease, a hundred illnesses will not arise, and boundless joy will be yours. When your merit is complete, a jeweled canopy and banners will appear, guardian deities and Skanda will lead the way, the eighteen arhats will attend your carriage, and countless flower immortals and celestial maidens will surround you, escorting you to the Western Paradise. Chaste maidens, is this not a wondrous prospect?

Truly, your past roots are no less than your present karmic conditions. These are the precious teachings of the heavenly immortals, earnest words from a pained heart. Take heed, and let each of you remember them well.

**The Illuminated Dao Mother says:**
The luminous qi is originally round,
qi originally dwells in one cavity.
This cavity divides into nine apertures,
east and west, south and north.
The constellations array their positions,
all pivoting on the One.
Unseen and unheard,
it seems to exist, seems not—yet distinct.
Existence and non-existence converge at the center,
radiant brilliance fills the four directions.
This cavity is not large,
yet it encompasses all phenomena.
Vast as the space beyond the heavens,
small as the form it matches—unfathomable.
Lofty as the three heavens,
low as the depths of the sea.
The cavity’s path is clearly marked,
let all listen plainly.
Now, I do not repeatedly point it out—
its subtlety is hard to fathom.

It is neither yin nor yang,
yang essence mingles with yin blood.
Yin qi returns to the sea of blood,
yang essence is discharged here.
Its arousal goes unnoticed,
yet in reverie, the heart is greatly pleased.
Floating and drifting,
the clear and turbid separate like black and white.
If displeased, the heart grows vexed and stifled;
yin and yang fail to connect.
Once the spirit attains ethereal subtlety,
qi envelops without obstruction.
At the midnight hour, the lotus begins to bloom,
yin and yang leaves intertwine.
Yin unites with the ancestral qi of yang,
lotus stamens array across the pond.
Yang joins with the ancestral qi of yin,
flowers bloom, branches and leaves flourish.
When this single flower opens,
seven blossoms all unfold.
The sea of blood connects to ancestral qi,
ancestral qi returns to the sea of blood.
When blood dries, qi is obstructed;
when qi is obstructed, blood is exhausted.
From obstruction and exhaustion, illness arises—
all due to qi stagnation.
And whence comes stagnation?
From constraint and lack of ease.
Because the heart is not detached,
the gates of prior and posterior qi are sealed.
Sealing is lower obstructing upper;
blockage is spoken of in vain.
Because sealing halts blood’s movement,
stasis leads to obstruction.
When qi is obstructed, the gates seal themselves,
not a single thread passes through.

The blood and qi have purity and turbidity—
how to distinguish them?
When the heart is pure, free of selfish delusion,
breath too is bright and clear.
Bright clarity unites with true yin,
true yang naturally presses in.
Pure and turbid separate of themselves—
trust this, and you will not lose even a month’s progress.
The light and pure ascend,
the turbid naturally leaks downward.
When the heart is impure, qi grows restless,
breath too becomes fierce.
Restlessness mingles with yang,
wicked fire blazes like iron.
It burns the true yang qi,
drying and withering—illness comes easily.
Worldly physicians are like the blind—
they diagnose pulses and prescribe recklessly.
First, they supplement qi and blood,
yet never address the passage of the gates.
Once turbid qi congeals,
meridians grow more obstructed.
When heart illness arises,
vexation and heat flare up.
Mouth parched, tongue scorched,
cold food offers temporary relief.
Medical arts grow ever more confused—
they question symptoms, then distinguish further.
Hearing of heat symptoms,
they prescribe cooling herbs like *zhi* and *huangbai*.
First supplementing, then cooling—
chronic illness becomes incurable.
After consuming every herb,
the complexion grows pale and emaciated.
When all else fails,
they add ginseng, deer antler, angelica, and turtle shell.
Nourishing yin and fostering yang,
the threads grow ever more tangled.
Cultivators of the true suffer harm,
each fearing to awaken.
Those who do not cultivate remain carefree,
while those who do endure setbacks.
I now make this clear warning:
when blood stagnates, there are rules to follow.
Blood is like the waters of a mountain valley—
it cannot be forced to flow by damming.
Once a dam breaks and surges,
it disrupts the proper meridian points.
Forced to flow askew,
it may even breach its bounds.
Within the sea of blood in the human body,
there are only three vessels.
The seas of qi and blood,
the *Ren* and *Du* vessels—all one cavity.
Essence passes through here,
the turbid is discharged here.
If not for cold stagnation,
there would be no obstruction.
When blocked and unable to flow smoothly,
use medicine to open the passages.
It must be warming, not too drying—
distinguish the clear from the turbid.
Treat this illness thus,
and the skilled physician is called a master.

I now reveal this to spare you suffering.
Distinguish the paths of yin and yang—
for men and women, the principle is the same.
Men possess this ancestral qi,
distributed within the essence cavity.
For women, ancestral qi unites—
yin is spoken of in terms of the sea of blood.
Men have this yang gate—
whether flowing forward or backward, do not be confused.

Women possess the Northern Sea’s earth,
its waves surging as if pressed by water.
The great *zhou tian* stirs greatly,
the small *zhou tian* likewise expands.
Twelve two-hour watches await,
the *zi* and *wu* poles converge.
This point admits of distinction—
those who cultivate may yet lack the dwelling.
The cultivator unites *zi* and *wu*,
true *qi* truly conjoins.
Without cultivation, though union occurs,
true ancestral *qi* is hard to release.
Here lies the true life’s essence—
do not lightly or recklessly speak of it.

The Northern Sea holds clear and turbid;
the turbid is *qi* faint and insipid.
Turbidity reveals form and substance—
on this day, thoughts must be swept away.
When thoughts are pure, clarity floats upward,
meeting ancestral *qi*.
When thoughts are mixed, *qi* enters substance,
and clarity instead turns foul.
If the monthly cycle errs,
it is because thoughts are too heavy.
Heavy thoughts dull the spirit,
and when the spirit is dull, no distinction is made.
Clear and turbid intermingle,
true *qi* fails to rise.
If this is the constant state,
such is the illness that arises in the pulse.
It must be addressed on that very day—
do not indulge in idle or deluded thoughts.
Abide in ease without the slightest stagnation,
flowing freely and unconstrained.

Do not worry, nor fret,
do not startle, nor fear.
Do not strain, nor inflate,
but remain bright and pure.
In movement and stillness, unobstructed,
alert and joyful.
Unknowing and unaware,
hearing and listening without attachment.
The body drifts as if weightless,
illumined by heaven’s light and earth’s whiteness.
Hands and feet feel as light as feathers,
floating without clinging.

Most to be avoided is an overzealous heart,
fearing that effort may be flawed.
This thought is a grave illness—
swiftly remedy it without delay.
Before the twenty-one days of discharge are complete,
do not restrict bedding or routine.
Wait until the discharge fully ceases,
then ascend the bed—only then is it proper.
This is an immutable method,
not to be transmitted to the unworthy.

The essence of heaven and earth—
once lost here, it cannot be regained.
I now urge you, women,
do not fixate on these secrets in your hearts.
Without secrets, the Dao is hard to fathom,
but clinging to secrets creates barriers in *qi*.
In daily life, let heart and mouth
quietly recite the Buddha’s name.
Recite only when thoughts arise;
when thoughts cease, do not recite.
Attend only to worldly affairs,
and do not let your hands chase butterflies.
Beyond mending clothes and shoes,
constantly examine your inner practice.
Engage in worldly tasks,
but let your thoughts remain cold as iron.
The eye is the thief that shakes the heart—
do not be drawn to the colors of flowers and shadows.
These are the burdens of the mundane frame;
if you wish to cultivate virtue,
cultivate virtue and the true,
refine your nature and purify your heart’s impurities.
Purify impurities, and virtue renews itself—
one morning, *qi* will steam forth.
You will ascend beyond the body, above the clouds,
drifting and resting in the far north.
I ride a phoenix chariot,
golden flowers and immortal maidens welcome you.
They guide you to wander the upper realms,
escort you to the Buddha’s land.
Ascend the tiers of the immortal pagoda,
your eyes beholding the vast expanse.
The toiling masses of the red dust,
their worldly fetters so pitiful.
Gazing southward,
tears fall like silk.
Though great compassion stirs,
it cannot aid those without affinity.
Even the great vow’s ship
cannot ferry those who create their own suffering.

The great Buddha of the Western Heaven,
even myriad methods cannot purify all.
I am the original luminous ancestor,
descended to this dwelling.
I point clearly, again and again—
how earnestly I hope for your awakening.
Do not forget this earnest instruction;
tranquility at dawn and dusk is the secret.

If you are often entangled and disturbed,
it is because the eye invites thieves.
See as if you have not seen,
turn inward to contemplate the inner cavity.
Neither light nor heavy,
neither urgent nor idle.
Neither restless nor reckless,
never forced in any way.
Neither clinging nor detached,
all vexations vanish.
Without seeking joy, joy arises naturally;
without forcing cessation, cessation occurs naturally.
When seated above, do not exert intent—
like a corpse, silent and still.
Though heaven collapses, you do not collapse;
though earth splits, you do not split.
Though others speak, do not be moved—
understand for yourself, clearly.

Worldly blessings and red fortunes—
regard the red as you would black.
Discern the true from the false in blue and white;
people are mixed, each of different kinds.
Without a vajra body,
do not recklessly wander the Land of Bliss.
Do not calculate length or shortness,
do not listen, and delusions will vanish of themselves.
Transcend the world by how many ranks?
Do not conform to the vulgar.
Let your aspirations be great, but your words not boastful;
let your heart be true, but your thoughts not timid.
Constantly embody the immortals and Buddhas—
here I speak of the profound secret.

Women read few books,
and the principles of nature are even harder to attain.
Simply maintain a single pure thought,
without the slightest inner obstruction.
Like the light of heaven and the transforming sun,
like stars and the moon.
Like the brightness of the North Star,
the Seven Stars hanging in the celestial palace.
Bright and radiant,
luminous without a speck of darkness.
Let your heart be as bright as the Dipper,
the inner Seven Stars resplendent.
Dark clouds cannot obscure it—
its true nature remains unbroken.
When clouds pass, the stars still shine;
let your heart be like a blazing star.
With not a speck of dust in the heart,
if dust arises, the heart strays elsewhere.

The heart is originally without delusion—
delusion enters only through what is seen.
The heart is originally without other thoughts—
hearing brings misfortune.
The heart is originally without clinging—
the body’s lack of agility causes it.
When body and speech do not align with intent,
anger and displeasure arise.
With this single angry state,
fire erupts from the five viscera.
If this root is not eradicated,
all cultivation of the Dao is in vain.

Now I point out in detail—
the word "greed" must be severed.
Do not covet clothing or food,
for what is natural will come.
Do not cling even to good thoughts—
the thoughts of immortals and mortals differ.
Do not cling even to wondrous methods—
abiding in stillness is unfathomably subtle.
Do not cling even to effort—
sit in absorption whenever the moment allows.
Do not cling even to wondrous realms—
realm and form are without shape or color.
Abide in peace and joy,
in delight and gladness.
Flowing freely and unconstrained,
spacious and at ease.
This is the wondrous realm—
this realm cannot be grasped.
Let it come and go of itself,
let it conjoin and transform naturally.
Let thoughts be still, and the spirit undisturbed—
in two or three years, you will surely attain.

Now, in great compassion,
I explain this step by step.
You women—
do not cling to this wondrous secret.
Once clung to, it becomes an illness;
do not blame the Dao for deception.
Neither internally nor externally bound,
the spirit moves freely, *qi* transcends.
Roaming with thoughts clear and bright,
the heart remains pure and radiant.
Why be constrained in coming and going?
The moon in the high sky may wax and wane.

---

Life’s desires are seldom fulfilled—
only at the end does one know red from black.
In this age of thin *qi* and frail virtue,
heed not the words of others.
Each cultivates their own nature and form;
immortals and mortals are distinct.
Immortals arise from immortal roots,
mortals bear the karma of past lives.
Though one may enjoy wealth and rank in this life,
the body’s decay is fearful to behold.
Without good deeds to one’s credit,
sins are recorded in the Black Ledger.
A lifetime without merit to offset them—
silver and gold slip through empty hands.
Only sins remain, a body bent in dust,
knees bloodied in the mire.
Condemned to the Great Hell,
in the next life one is reborn deaf and blind.

Here lies the divide between immortal and mortal—
yet cultivation holds further truths.
Even if one fails to reach the highest rank,
immortals and buddhas may intercede in calamity.
Cultivate one’s nature in the inner chambers,
and when merit is complete, ascend to the celestial palace.
When the elixir of true cultivation is full,
a divine decree descends with an immortal’s writ.
Golden youths bear jeweled banners,
jade flutes resound through heaven and earth.
They welcome you to the Land of Ultimate Bliss,
to enjoy boundless kalpas.
No longer entering the wheel of rebirth,
neither born nor extinguished,
neither dying nor aging—
a guest inscribed on the roster of eternal life.
Now drifting with mist and clouds,
now resting in phoenix pavilions,
now roaming the ends of the sky,
now wandering isles in the sea,
beholding endless vistas of golden splendor,
gazing upon inexhaustible hues of lapis lazuli.
This is the great joy of merit perfected,
the supreme secret of returning to the root through cultivation!

---

**Women’s Alchemical Secrets**
*By Pu Yang’s Unhearted Master Chen Yongqing*

**The Secret of Refining Form in the Great Yin**

Women’s cultivation of the true holds its own secrets,
not idle speculations spun from thin air.
The human body inherently possesses yin and yang—
the principles of yin and yang demand repeated reflection.
A man’s essence is yang within yin,
a woman’s essence is yin within yang.
Seek a wise teacher without delay to shatter the mystery,
and return to youth in the homeland of the origin.

In stillness, cultivate the true without doubt,
awaiting the arrival of the one yang within the body.
Return to the realm of the primordial,
and plant the golden crow in the moon.
Who devised this method of true cultivation,
drawing noblewomen to shave their heads?
Day after day, they guard empty chambers,
hearts as dead as ash, wielding the blade of life and death.
Alas, the Red Dragon, that demonic force,
endlessly encircling the sun and moon.
Place the dragon’s head upon the executioner’s block,
sever it before dawn breaks.
Clasp the gate tightly with both hands,
lest the Yellow Tiger slip past the wall.
To lead him home is no difficult task—
quickly set him ablaze.
Mount the crane and count the breaths,
the cold sound of jade dew like fragrant milk.
Gently guide it past the Purple Tenuity Palace,
suffusing the body with softness until noon.
Temper the civil and martial fires with care,
lest the mind become cluttered and chaotic.
Ever vigilant, guard against the true seed’s escape—
draw it back to the breasts to form the sacred embryo.
Once the sacred embryo gathers in the breasts,
longevity rivals heaven’s, boundless and immeasurable.
Thus concludes the cultivation of the true in this life—
within seven days, yang is reborn.
If the celestial heart revives in seven days,
this is the sublime marvel of the highest vehicle.
Henceforth, the practice aligns with that of men—
each oral instruction must come from the teacher.

**The Secret of Threefold Severing of the Red Dragon**

Women who cultivate the true are bold indeed,
raising the blade to sever the Red Dragon.
Defying husbands and rebelling against mothers, hearts filled with venom—
all for the rare chance to transform this human form.
Strike with all one’s strength,
lest the vital essence leak outward.
Reverse the flow of the Yellow River,
yin wanes as yang waxes, governed by breath.
Breath is but a furnace’s fire,
the yellow sprout simmered in the cauldron.
Warm vapors rise to the heavens,
then descend the tower to the earthen crucible.
A broken bamboo must be mended with bamboo—
do not boil cinnabar and mercury with silver and lead.
Take only those of the same kind to engender one another,
swiftly gather them into the two breasts.
Seizing the mechanism of heaven and earth’s creation,
each person possesses a ladder to the heavens.
Yang’s rise and yin’s retreat hold no other secret—
only in thought free from delusion.
Free from delusion, one has resolve,
wielding the merciless sword in the dark.
Sever the Red Dragon two or three times,
then a noblewoman’s skill is revealed.
When skill is high, so too is the dharma’s power—
gathering the phoenix without duality, soaring with the clouds.
Though all are women in skirts,
who says their names cannot be inscribed among the immortals?
Let the resolve of women in skirts stand firm as a mountain,
planting flowers in fire to bloom white lotuses.
Cultivate a heart of compassion,
and one may ascend to immortality from level ground.

Only a single grain of golden elixir,
radiant day after day.
Its form like a millet seed, sweet as honey,
its power to revive the dead and restore life is doubled.
Alas, people remain unaware of the golden elixir—
even spirits and gods may not fathom it.
Its wondrous illusion requires a teacher’s transmission—
yet it is but a remedy from one’s own garden.

**Women’s Secrets of Cultivating the True**

Noblewomen study meditation day by day,
silent and speechless, their hearts devoted.
If even a trace of selfish desire arises,
the true lead will flee the furnace.
True lead is the medicine of the primordial—
why do people fail to grasp it?
Guard the gate with care,
lest it steal away from the chamber.
If it escapes, do not fear—
raise a tempest of wind and fire.
Drive it straight to the ninefold heavens,
seizing heaven and earth to hang upon the breasts.
Without steadfast integrity, do not transmit the Dao,
lest foolish passions invite mockery.
To leak the mystery is unforgivable to heaven—
the sin is no small matter.
Do not teach the secret to those who lack understanding,
lest they babble to others in confusion.
Though I have exhorted you again and again,
do not treat the immortal’s way as mere trifle.

Women’s natures are wayward,
their hearts set only on ascending to the Jasper Terrace.
If you speak of this to others,
how could such learning befit a woman in skirts?
Women who study the Dao often bring shame,
heedlessly encountering packs of dogs.
Lured into secret rites with blind masters,
they check their navels to verify their progress.
Better to sit steadfast in the incense chamber,
honoring parents-in-law and obeying husbands.
After death, the soul returns to the Pure Land,
where the Buddha of the West calls your name.

I urge women to abandon the study of the Dao—
amidst the Dao, false paths disrupt the true one.

Cultivate a heart of loyalty, kindness, and benevolence—
what matter if the Way be false or true?
Even if the true Way requires no seeking,
the fire of desire arises unbidden, unrestrained.
Young in years yet already disgraced—
do you know shame or not?

*Essential Teachings on the Female Elixir*
*Transmitted by the Pure Yang Ancestor Lü*
*Respectfully recorded by the disciple Fu Jinquan*

The Three Flowers of essence and qi never wane,
the Purple Qi of the Clear Void follows established rules.
The Nine Revolutions of the Golden Elixir are refined by the Primordial Lady,
and longevity resembles the Yellow Peace turtle seated upon its treasure.

As for the text *"Purple Qi of the Clear Void,"* it was bestowed by the Primordial Lady.
When asked how long the Yellow Peace turtle remains seated, the answer was:
"This turtle fears the light of sun and moon, emerging but once every thirty years.
I have sat upon this turtle and witnessed three emergences."

You fail to understand that the old yang has no birth or cessation.
Let me offer a comparison:
"Like the crescent moon on the third day, by the fifth or sixth it remains full."
Women’s cultivation is the same as men’s—
what is difficult is maintaining purity.
Know that women’s desires exceed those of men.
Once the menstrual flow has ceased,
the heart is like a lotus just opening,
and only with heaven’s rain and dew does it bear fruit.
A woman without a man is solitary yin—
solitary yin does not give birth to the lotus.
Without receiving the grace of rain and dew,
even fertile soil will be of no use.
Heaven’s rain and dew exist to bring forth the myriad things—
can this act be in vain?
If the myriad things do not receive rain and dew,
then solitary yang cannot grow.

The Way can be verified through things,
and understood through affairs.
Even in shallow discourse, profound principles are present—
it is only that people do not reflect and comprehend them.

Women may employ the method of massage:
Upon rising in the morning, sit in stillness for a moment.
Press the heart firmly with the right hand,
while the left hand strokes the abdomen and navel twenty times.
Then stroke down to the waist, kneading and patting once.
Reverse the hands—left hand pressing the heart, right hand stroking,
then right hand pressing the heart, left hand stroking.
After kneading and patting the waist with both hands,
rub the hands until warm and smooth the face.
Massage the ears, pressing and flicking them,
then knead the shoulders, pinch them,
swallow the generated saliva,
stretch the waist, stand, and rub the hands together.
Walk a few steps before attending to external matters.
Perform this again in the evening before taking the pills.

**Pill Formula:**
- *Polygonum multiflorum* (prepared) – 2 kernels
- Walnuts – 3
- *Ophiopogon japonicus* – 1 *liang*
- *Rehmannia glutinosa* (prepared) – 2.5 *liang*
- *Psoralea corylifolia* – 6 *fen*
- *Amomum villosum* – 3 *fen*
- *Eucommia ulmoides* – 8 *fen*
- *Asparagus cochinchinensis* – 1 *liang*
- Fresh ginger – 3 *fen*

Grind the eight ingredients into a fine powder,
then mix with half a *jin* of lard (for those who eat meat, use lard;
for vegetarians, use human milk, cow’s milk, or goat’s milk—
milk is *su*, not meat. In the northwest, this is called "milk tea,"
which strengthens the spirit, nourishes the complexion,
blackens the hair, and extends life.
The Buddha consumed it during his ascetic practice on Snow Mountain,
which is why it is not forbidden in Buddhist monasteries.
If using imitation *su* oil, it is often sheep’s fat—
better to use human milk).
Form into pills and take for one month.
The spirit will grow strong, the hair black, and life extended—
no other medicine compares.

On the days of *yin*, *wu*, *shen*, and *hai* each month,
take three *fen* of the medicine with a bowl of water.
At dawn, face east, inhale the fresh qi three times, and swallow.
Recite:
*"The light of the rising sun is rooted in true yang.
I absorb the proper qi of the eastern direction,
refining it into the jade liquid of nectar.
The Golden Essence of Taiyi penetrates the crown,
the Li Palace forges pure hardness.
The two qi transform the northern direction,
and the robust body resides within."*

Press the palms together and stretch seven times.
With a finger, write:
*"Supreme Divine Numinous Highest Longevity Eternal Life Heavenly Worthy"*
in the bowl of water.
After swallowing the pill, face west, inhale once, and swallow.
Then proceed with daily affairs.
Guard against carelessly transmitting this to the unworthy.
Once the Great Elixir is accomplished, prepare and take the medicine again.

**Female True Elixir**
*Excerpted from* The Secret Manual of Nourishing the True *by the Realized One of the Elixir Pavilion, Ancestor Lu*
*Recorded by Fu Shan of Taiyuan*

The Realized One said:
In the cultivation of the female true elixir, there is also the method of closing the menstrual blood.
This method was transmitted from our ancestor, the Primordial Lady of Silence,
to the Primordial Lady of Wei,
who passed it to Yellow Flower Maiden,
who then transmitted it to Maid Ma,
who gave it to Maiden Qi—
this formed one lineage.
Ancestor Lü transmitted it to Immortal He,
who taught Wang Chongyang,
who initiated Sun the Immortal Maiden,
who then taught Zhang the True Slave—
this formed another lineage.
The Realized One of the Straw Cloak transmitted it to Golden Lotus Woman.
All first closed the menses.

Though male essence and female blood are dregs,
the qi of the prior heaven is entirely concealed within them.
If the posterior heaven is discharged,
then the prior heaven is also discharged—
hence the closing of this pathway.

The *Vast Principles of Nourishing Life* asks:
"May I inquire about the method of closing the menses?"

The Realized One said:
For female cultivators, first practice breath-counting and seated meditation as before.
Once the qi in the body is circulating smoothly,
begin the practice one day before the menstrual period at the *zi* or *wu* hour.
At midnight, put on clothes, sit cross-legged,
clench the fists, and embrace the ribs.
Wait until the qi in the body rises and falls several times,
then use the left heel to press against the *yin* gate and anus.
Clench the teeth, strain the eyes, shrug the shoulders,
and exert force to lift,
visualizing two streams of red qi rising from the uterus,
passing through the coccyx, the Three Passes,
ascending to the Mud Pill Palace,
descending to the root of the tongue,
and pouring into the breasts.
Continue until the body grows warm before stopping.
Then insert a piece of white, soft silk into the *yin* gate
to observe whether the flow is more or less than the previous month.
Repeat the previous practice to disperse the blood and qi,
preventing illness.
Within a hundred days, it will naturally cease.
Note the day of the previous month’s onset—
for example, if it came on the first day,
wait until the third day to sever it once.
Sever it once in the second month,
and once more in the third month.
After no more than three months, it will stop.

First sever the tail in the first month,
sever the waist in the second,
sever the head in the third—
this is called "severing the Red Dragon."
Mark this well.

*Observations from Heart-Fasting Studio*
*Recorded Sayings of Lord Wenchang*

Only after the division of yin and yang
do male and female distinctions arise;
only through opening and closing, gathering and receiving
is the work of Qian and Kun established.
Endowed with constant inclinations and innate goodness,
they share the same qi to form their bodies.
The origins of human relationships begin
with the pairing that first transforms the source.

Heaven and Earth possess no solitary Way,
and how could creatures have a mechanism for solitary birth?
Thus, Fu Xi and King Wen expounded the hexagrams,
revealing the profound subtleties of the Six Children;
the Zhou dynasty laid its foundations,
greatly manifesting the refined transformation of the *Er Nan*.

The sagely teachings do not neglect the model for the inner chambers,
and true cultivation fundamentally relies on the primal power of Kun.
